Taharah — Purification

The Subject Matter of Fiqh: Actions of the Mukallaf
Definition of fiqh's scope and categories of rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten Hanafi categories of rulings (ahkam taklifiyyah) and identify whether a person is mukallaf, determining if their actions fall under the subject of fiqh.

Core Idea
Fiqh only governs the actions of a mukallaf — a mature, sane person — and classifies them into ten distinct rulings.

Fiqh is not about every human action; it is specifically about the actions of a legally responsible person (mukallaf). This passage defines the scope of fiqh by listing all possible rulings (ahkam) that can apply to a mukallaf's deed. Understanding this foundation helps you see why children and the insane are not accountable in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Define 'mukallaf'
Identify the term from the passage and state its meaning: a person who is mature (baligh) and sane (aqil). Why is this term central? Because sharia rulings only apply to such individuals.
Minors and the insane are excluded (ghayr mukallaf).
2
List the ten categories of rulings
Read the passage and enumerate all ten categories mentioned. Group them as: obligatory (fard, wajib), recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah, sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, nafl, mustahabb), prohibited (haram, makruh tahrimi), disliked (makruh tanzihi), and permissible (mubah).
Memorize the list; it forms the Ahkam Taklifiyyah.
3
Explain the restriction to mukallaf
The passage explicitly says sharia does not apply rulings to the actions of a minor or insane person. Why? Because they lack legal capacity (ahliyyah). Actions of non-mukallaf are not subject to fiqh discussions.
This is a key principle: accountability requires capacity.
4
Apply the definition to a scenario
Given an action by a specific person, first determine if the person is mukallaf. If yes, the action falls under fiqh's subject matter; if no, it does not. For example, a five-year-old child's prayer is valid but not obligatory.
Practice: Is a 12-year-old sane boy mukallaf? (In Hanafi, puberty begins at 15 or with signs.)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علم فقہ کا موضوع
مکلف آدمی کا فعل اور عمل جس سے یہ بحث کی جائے کہ یہ فرض ہے (۲) یا واجب ہے (۳) یا سنت مؤکدہ ہے (۴) یا سنت غیر مؤکدہ ہے (۵) یا نفل ہے (۶) یا مستحب ہے (۷) یا حرام ہے (۸) یا مکروہ تحریمی ہے (۹) یا مکروہ تنزیہی ہے (۱۰) یا مباح ہے۔ مکلف آدمی کے اعمال کے بارے میں اوپر کی بحثیں کرنا اور حکم لگا نا علم فقہ کا موضوع ہے۔
مکلف کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ نابالغ بچہ اور مجنون کے اعمال پر شرعیت نہ حکم لگاتی ہے اور نہ اس سے بحث کی جاتی ہے۔ صرف مکلف کے اعمال سے بحث کرتی ہے۔
The Subject Matter of the Knowledge of Fiqh: The action and deed of a legally responsible (mukallaf) person, regarding which it is discussed whether it is (1) fard, (2) wajib, (3) sunnah mu'akkadah, (4) sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, (5) nafl, (6) mustahabb, (7) haram, (8) makruh tahrimi, (9) makruh tanzihi, or (10) mubah. To conduct these discussions and apply rulings concerning the actions of a mukallaf is the subject matter of the knowledge of fiqh. The qualification of 'mukallaf' is added because sharia neither applies rulings to the actions of a minor child or an insane person nor is it discussed. It only discusses the actions of a mukallaf.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This is a definition_ruling passage. The author defines the subject matter (mawdu') of fiqh as the actions of a mukallaf (legally responsible person). It lists the ten categories of rulings (ahkam taklifiyyah) that fiqh applies: fard, wajib, sunnah mu'akkadah, sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, nafl, mustahabb, haram, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, and mubah. The passage explains why the term 'mukallaf' is used: the rulings do not apply to minors or the insane, as they lack legal capacity. This is standard Hanafi fiqh: the subject is the acts of a responsible person categorised into these ten types.

Key Terms
مکلف (mukallaf): A person who is legally responsible according to sharia, i.e., mature, sane, and capable.
فرض (fard): An obligatory action proven by definitive evidence (Quran or mutawatir hadith).
واجب (wajib): An obligatory action proven by speculative evidence.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An action that is prohibited but not with definitive evidence; close to haram.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An action that is disliked but not sinful; better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many categories of rulings are listed as the subject matter of fiqh in the passage?
A) 5
B) 7
C) 9
D) 10

Key Takeaway
Fiqh solely concerns the actions of a mukallaf, classified into ten distinct rulings, and does not apply to minors or the insane.

Taharah — Purification

The Precedence of Taharah and Its Proofs
Introduces the book of Taharah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and Hadith proofs for the obligation of taharah and explain why it is placed first in Hanafi fiqh works.

Core Idea
Taharah is the key to prayer—without it, salah is invalid, so it takes precedence in fiqh texts.

This lesson opens the Book of Taharah. The author immediately presents the foundational proofs: the Quranic verse commanding wudu and ghusl, and the hadith that purification is half of faith and the key to prayer. Understanding these proofs establishes why taharah is an obligatory condition for salah and why every Hanafi fiqh manual begins with this topic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Recognise that 'taharah' (purification) is not a single act but includes wudu and ghusl when required. The ruling level is fard 'ayn for any worshiper needing to perform salah.
Fard 'ayn means individually obligatory on each responsible Muslim.
2
Extract the Quranic proof
Locate verse 5:6. Note the imperative 'faghslu' (wash) and the conditional phrase 'idha qumtum ila al-salah' (when you stand for prayer). This shows purification is a condition for prayer.
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless another evidence specifies otherwise.
3
Extract the Hadith proof
Identify the two hadiths: 'al-tahuru shatru al-iman' (purification is half of faith) and 'miftahu al-salah al-tahuru' (the key to prayer is purification). These strengthen the case from the Quran.
The second hadith directly ties taharah to the validity of salah.
4
Understand the author's arrangement
Realise that because salah is the most frequent and important physical worship, and taharah is its essential condition, the author places Kitab al-Taharah first. This is a standard Hanafi structural choice.
This arrangement highlights the logical priority; it is not arbitrary.
5
Note the cross-madhhab consensus
All four Sunni schools agree that taharah is required for salah; the proofs are decisive (qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah). Therefore this ruling is 'muttafaq alayh' (unanimously agreed).
Differences exist on details, but the obligation itself is not disputed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة. قال الله تعالى: {يا أيها الذين آمنوا إذا قمتم إلى الصلاة فاغسلوا وجوهكم وأيديكم إلى المرافق وامسحوا برءوسكم وأرجلكم إلى الكعبين وإن كنتم جنبا فاطهروا} [المائدة:6]. وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "الطهور شطر الإيمان"، "مفتاح الصلاة الطهور" (رواه الترمذي).
The Book of Taharah. Allah says: 'O you who believe, when you stand up for prayer, wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows, wipe your heads and your feet up to the ankles, and if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves.' The Prophet said: 'Purification is half of faith' and 'The key to prayer is purification.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Taharah. The author provides two proofs for its precedence: first, the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6) which commands wudu and ghusl, showing purification is a prerequisite for prayer. Second, the hadith stating 'purification is half of faith' and 'the key to prayer is purification.' Since prayer is the most important physical worship (obligatory five times daily), and taharah is its essential condition, the author places the chapter on taharah first. This follows the standard methodology of Hanafi fiqh works like Nur al-Idah. The commentary also explains the linguistic breakdown of 'kitab' and its usage in fiqh texts.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): Purification from hadath (impurity) by wudu or ghusl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafi jurists place Kitab al-Taharah at the beginning of their works?
A) Because taharah is more important than iman
B) Because salah is the most frequent obligatory worship and requires taharah
C) Because the author of Nur al-Idah decided arbitrarily
D) Because taharah is mentioned first in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Taharah is an obligatory condition for valid salah, proven by the Quranic command and Prophetic hadith, which is why it is placed first in Hanafi fiqh works.

Taharah — Purification

8 min
The Primacy of Taharah: Definition, Proofs, and Place in Fiqh
Introductory passage defining taharah and establishing its proofs and priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define taharah linguistically and technically, cite the primary textual proofs for its obligation, and explain why Hanafi fiqh works give it precedence.

Core Idea
Taharah is the key to prayer — and prayer is the pillar of religion.

This lesson opens Kitab al-Taharah by defining the term, establishing its importance through Quran and Hadith, and explaining why Hanafi authors place purification before all other topics. Understanding this framing is essential for grasping the role of taharah in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Define taharah
Distinguish the linguistic meaning (cleanliness) from the technical (removal of hadath or najasa).
Linguistic: al-taharah means cleanliness. Technical: either removal of ritual impurity (hadath) or removal of filth (najasa).
2
Identify the primary textual proofs
Locate the Quranic verse (Ma'idah 5:6) and the hadith 'Purity is half of faith' and 'The key to prayer is purity'.
The Quranic imperative 'faghsilu' indicates wudu for prayer; 'fattahharu' indicates ghusl for janaba.
3
Explain the precedence given to taharah
Understand that prayer is the most frequent act of worship and requires taharah as a condition, so taharah is prioritized.
Prayer is obligatory five times daily, so taharah's need is constant.
4
Recognize the organizational structure
Note the terms kitab, bab, fasl used in fiqh works; 'Kitab al-Taharah' is a general heading containing chapters and sections.
A kitab encompasses many issues; a bab is for one type; a fasl is for one kind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
ضروری نوٹ : الطہا را : مصدر ہے۔ اور کتاب الطہارۃ، مرکب اضافی ناقص ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے پہلے مبتدا یا اس کے آخر میں خبر محذوف ماننی پڑے گی ۔ مثلا ھذا کتاب الطهارة، يا كتاب الطهارة هذا، يا كتاب الطہارۃ کو اقرء کا مفعول مانیں اور یوں عبارت رکھیں اقرء كتاب الطهارة۔
طہارة كا ثبوت : آیت میں طہارت کا ثبوت ہے۔ یا ایها الذین آمنوا اذا قمتم الى الصلوة فاغسلوا وجوهكم وايـديـكــم الــى المرافق وامسحوا برء وسكم وارجلكم الى الكعبين، وان كنتم جنبا فاطهروا - آیت ۶ ،سورة المائدة ۵۔حدیث میں ہے الطهور شطر الایمان ، یہ بھی ہے مفتاح الصلوة الطهور - ( ترمذی، باب ماجاء مفتاح الصلوۃ الطهو رص ۶ نمبر۳) طہارۃ کو مقدم کرنے کی۔

( آيت ٣ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) حدیث میں ہے الصلوة عماد الدين من اقامها فقد اقام الدین اسی لئے تمام مصنفین نے ابواب نماز کو مقدم کیا ہے۔ اور نماز کی شرط طہارت ہے، بغیر طہارت کے نماز ادا نہیں ہوگی اس لئے کتاب الطہارۃ کو مقدم کیا۔ (۲) حج عمر میں ایک مرتبہ فرض ہے۔ زکوۃ سال میں ایک مرتبہ فرض ہے۔ روزہ سال میں ایک ماہ فرض ہے۔ لیکن نماز دن میں پانچ مرتبہ فرض ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی ضرورت بار بار پڑتی ہے۔ اور نماز کے لئے طہارت کی ضرورت پڑے گی تو طہارت کی ضرورت بھی دن میں پانچ بار پڑی۔ اس لئے کثرت ضرورت کی بنا پر بھی طہارت کو پہلے ذکر کیا۔ لغوی تحقیق کتاب فعال کے وزن پر مفعول کے معنی میں ہیں۔ جیسے لباس ملبوس کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح کتاب بھی مکتوب کے معنی میں استعمال ہوا ہے۔ اس کا معنی ہے لکھے ہوئے اوراق کا مجموعہ ۔ کتب کا معنی ہیں لکھنا۔ کتاب میں بہت سے مسائل لکھے ہوئے ہوتے ہیں اس لئے اس کو کتاب کہتے ہیں۔ نوٹ: فقہ کی کتابوں میں تین الفاظ ذکر کرتے ہیں۔ (۱) کتاب (۲) باب (۳) فصل ۔ کتاب میں مختلف انواع اور اقسام کے مسائل مذکور ہوتے ہیں اور اس میں بعض مرتبہ کئی ابواب بھی شامل ہوتے ہیں۔ گویا کہ وہ عام لفظ ہے۔ باب میں ایک قسم کے مسائل ذکر کرتے ہیں۔ اور فصل میں ایک نوع کے مسائل ذکر کرتے ہیں۔

( ا ) المياه التى يجوز التطهير بها سبعة مياه. ماء السماء وماء البحر وماء النهر وماء البئر وماء ذاب [من الثلج] وماء ذاب [من البرد] وماء العين.
الطهارة: طهر اسکا مصدر ہے اس کا معنی ہے طہارۃ اور پاکیزگی ، اس کا الٹا ہے دنس ۔ شریعت میں مخصوص اعضاء کے دھونے کو طہارت کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا الٹا ہے حدث بعض علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ رفع حدث یا ازالہ نجس کا نام طہارت ہے۔ نوٹ: پاک کرنے کو طهارة بفتح ط ، پاک کرنے کے بعد جو پانی باقی رہ جائے اس کو طھارۃ ط کے ضمہ کے ساتھ ۔اور پاک کرنے کا جو آلہ ہوتا ہے جیسے پانی اور مٹی اس کو طھارة ط کے کسرہ کے ساتھ بولتے ہیں۔ پاک پانی نہ ہو تو مٹی پاک کرنے کے لئے چند شرائط کے ساتھ پانی کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے۔ نوٹ: اقسام طہارت : (۱) اعتقادات کی طہارت جیسے اللہ رسول اور قیامت کے ساتھ وہ اعتقاد رکھنا جو قرآن اور حدیث کے مطابق ہو (۲) مال کی طہارۃ جیسے مال کی زکوۃ دینا (۳) بدن کی طہارۃ جیسے وضو کر نا غسل کرنا۔ کپڑے کی طھارۃ جیسے کپڑے کو پاک کرنا۔ طہارۃ مصدر میں یہ سب طہارتیں شامل ہیں۔
پانی کے احکام
ضروری نوٹ : حضرت مصنف نے پانی کے احکام پہلے لائے، کیونکہ پانی سے ہی طہارت ہوتی ہے، اور طہارت سے ہی نماز وغیرہ پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔ ترجمه: (1) جس پانی سے پاک کرنا جائز ہے وہ سات قسم کے پانی ہیں۔ [1] آسمان کا پانی، [۲]سمندرکا پانی[۳] نہر کا پانی [۴] کنواں کا پانی، [۵] برف [۶]، اور اولے سے پگھلا ہوا پانی [۷] چشمہ کا پانی۔
تشریح یہ سات قسم کے پانی ہیں جو پاک میں اور ان سے جسم کو اور کپڑوں کو پاک کرنا جائز ہے، کیوں کہ یہ خود بھی پاک ہیں اور دوسروں کو بھی پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتے ہیں۔
وجه (۱) یہ سب پانی پاک ہیں اس لئے یہ پانی تھوڑی ناپاکی گرنے کی وجہ سے ناپاک نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔اس لئے ان سے وضو کرنا اور غسل کرنا دونوں جائز ہیں (۲) آسمان کا پانی پاک ہے اس کے بارے میں یہ آیت ہے۔ وانــزلـنــا من السماء ماء طهورا۔ (آیت ۴۸ ، سورۃ الفرقان (۲۵) (۳) سمندر کے پانی کے سلسلے میں یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابي هريرة رضي الله عنه يقول سأل رجل رسول الله الله ... افنتوضأ من البحر فقال رسول الله و هو الطهور ماء ه و الحل ميتته. (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی ماء البحرانه طهور ص ۲۱، نمبر ۶۹ رابوداود شریف، باب الوضوء بماء البحر،ص ۱۳ نمبر ۸۳ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سمندر کا پانی پاک ہے اور اسکی مری ہوئی مچھلی بھی حلال ہے۔۔ سمندر بڑا ہوتا ہے اور نہر چھوٹا ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس
Book of Purification
Necessary note: 'al-tahara' is a masdar. And 'kitab al-tahara' is an incomplete genitive construction. Therefore one must assume before it a mubtada or at its end a deleted khabar. For example, 'hadha kitab al-tahara', or 'kitab al-tahara hadha', or consider 'kitab al-tahara' as maf'ul of 'iqra' and phrase it 'iqra' kitab al-tahara'.
Proof of tahara: The verse contains proof of tahara: 'O you who believe, when you stand up for prayer, wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows, and wipe your heads and your feet up to the ankles. And if you are in a state of janaba, then purify yourselves.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). In hadith: 'Purity is half of faith.' Also: 'The key to prayer is purity.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the key to prayer, p. 6, no. 3). Reason for giving precedence to tahara:
Point (1): Among acts of worship, prayer is most important. After faith, the greatest importance is given to prayer. The divine command: 'Those who believe in the unseen and establish prayer' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:3). In hadith: 'Prayer is the pillar of religion; whoever establishes it has established religion.' Therefore all authors have given precedence to the chapters on prayer. And the condition of prayer is tahara; without tahara, prayer is not valid. Hence the book of tahara is given precedence. (2) Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime. Zakat is obligatory once a year. Fasting is obligatory one month a year. But prayer is obligatory five times a day. Therefore its need occurs repeatedly. And for prayer, tahara is needed, so the need for tahara also occurs five times a day. Thus due to the frequency of need, tahara is mentioned first. Linguistic research: 'Kitab' is on the pattern of 'fi'al' and means 'maf'ul' (the object). Just as 'libas' is used in the meaning of 'malbus' (what is worn), similarly 'kitab' is used in the meaning of 'maktub' (what is written). Its meaning is a collection of written pages. 'Kataba' means to write. Since a book contains many written issues, it is called 'kitab'. Note: In books of fiqh, three terms are used: (1) Kitab, (2) Bab, (3) Fasl. A kitab contains issues of various types and kinds, and sometimes includes several abwab. So it is a general term. A bab contains one type of issues. And a fasl contains one kind of issues.

(1) The waters with which purification is permissible are seven waters: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, water melted from snow, water melted from hail, and spring water.
Tahara: 'Tahr' is its masdar; its meaning is cleanliness and purity; its opposite is 'danas'. In Shari'ah, washing specific limbs is called tahara. Its opposite is hadath. Some scholars say that raising a hadath or removing najas is called tahara. Note: The act of purifying is 'tahara' with fatha on ta; the water remaining after purification is 'tuhara' with damma on ta; and the instrument of purification, like water and earth, is 'tihara' with kasra on ta. If pure water is not available, then earth, with certain conditions, stands in place of water for purification. Note: Types of tahara: (1) Purification of beliefs, like having a belief in Allah, the Messenger, and the Day of Judgment that conforms to Quran and Hadith. (2) Purification of wealth, like giving zakat on wealth. (3) Purification of the body, like performing wudu and ghusl. Purification of clothes, like making clothes pure. As a masdar, tahara includes all these purifications.
Rulings on water
Necessary note: The author brought the rulings on water first, because purification is done with water, and through purification prayer etc. can be performed. Translation: (1) The waters with which purification is permissible are seven types: [1] Rainwater, [2] Seawater, [3] River water, [4] Well water, [5] Snow, [6] Water melted from hail, [7] Spring water.
Explanation: These seven types of water are pure, and with them it is permissible to purify the body and clothes, because they themselves are pure and also have the capacity to purify others.
Point (1): All these waters are pure, so they do not become impure due to a small amount of impurity falling into them. Therefore performing wudu and ghusl with them is permissible. (2) Rainwater is pure; regarding it there is this verse: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (Surah al-Furqan 25:48). (3) Regarding seawater, there is this hadith: From Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: A man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'May we perform wudu with seawater?' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'It is pure, its water is pure, and its dead [animals] are permissible.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on seawater being pure, p. 21, no. 69; Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu with seawater, p. 13, no. 83). This hadith shows that seawater is pure and its dead fish is also halal. The sea is large and the river is small, therefore it
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an introductory lesson from a Hanafi fiqh text, opening the chapter on purification (Kitab al-Taharah). The author first explains the grammatical construction of the title, noting that 'kitab al-tahara' is an incomplete genitive phrase requiring an implicit mubtada or khabar. This is a typical academic framing in classical books.

The author then provides evidence (dalil) for the obligation of purification from the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) and hadith ("Purity is half of faith," "The key to prayer is purity"), establishing the importance of taharah. The commentary explains why taharah is given precedence over other topics: because prayer is the most important act of worship after faith, and prayer requires taharah; also the frequency of prayer (five times daily) necessitates frequent taharah, so the topic is placed first.

A linguistic note follows: the word 'kitab' is derived from 'kataba' (to write) and means a collection of written material, like 'libas' means clothing. The author distinguishes between three organizational terms in fiqh works: 'kitab' (general topic), 'bab' (chapter on a specific type), and 'fasl' (section on a particular kind).

The second part of the lesson lists the seven types of water with which purification is valid: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, snow water, hail water, and spring water. This is a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh: these waters are inherently pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir). The passage explains that these waters do not become impure by a small amount of impurity (najasa) falling into them, unlike small quantities of other waters. Proofs for rainwater and seawater are cited from Quran and hadith. The hadith also shows that the dead fish of the sea are halal, an added benefit.

The lesson also includes a brief definition of 'tahara' linguistically and technically: linguistically meaning cleanliness; technically, the removal of hadath or the removal of najasa. The different vowelizations (tahara, tuhara, tihara) correspond to different meanings: the act, the residual water, and the instrument. This nuance is characteristic of Hanafi linguistic precision.

Overall, this lesson establishes the central role of taharah in worship and identifies the primary means of achieving it—pure water—along with its evidence from primary sources.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): Linguistically: cleanliness and purity. Technically: the removal of hadath (ritual impurity) or the removal of najasa (filth).
كتاب (kitab): A collection of written pages; in fiqh, a general topic containing chapters (abwab) and sections (fusul).
باب (bab): A chapter in fiqh, focusing on one type of issue.
فصل (fasl): A section within a chapter, focusing on one kind of issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Taharah — Purification

The Seven Pure Waters: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling statement with proof: listing the seven pure waters and their evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the seven types of pure water recognized in the Hanafi school, state their ruling (tahir and mutahhir), and cite the evidence for rainwater and seawater.

Core Idea
Seven natural waters are pure and purifying — they do not become impure by a small amount of impurity.

This lesson introduces the first substantive ruling in Kitab al-Taharah: the types of water that can be used for purification. The Hanafi school lists seven, all of which are inherently pure (tahir) and capable of purifying other things (mutahhir). The passage provides Quranic and Hadith evidence for rainwater and seawater, establishing a pattern of relying on primary texts.

Guided Path
1
List the seven waters
Name all seven: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, water melted from snow, water melted from hail, and spring water.
These are all naturally occurring, unaltered waters.
2
Understand the ruling
They are tahur: both pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir). They do not become impure by contact with najasa unless a change occurs in one of three properties: color, taste, smell.
This is the Hanafi principle: small amounts of impurity do not render large bodies of water impure.
3
Examine the evidence for rainwater
Quran 25:48: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water.'
The word 'tahura' indicates both purity and purifying capability.
4
Examine the evidence for seawater
Hadith of Abu Huraira: The Prophet said, 'Its water is pure, and its dead [animals] are permissible.'
This hadith also establishes the permissibility of eating dead sea creatures.

الطهارة: طهر اسکا مصدر ہے اس کا معنی ہے طہارۃ اور پاکیزگی ، اس کا الٹا ہے دنس ۔ شریعت میں مخصوص اعضاء کے دھونے کو طہارت کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا الٹا ہے حدث بعض علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ رفع حدث یا ازالہ نجس کا نام طہارت ہے۔ نوٹ: پاک کرنے کو طهارة بفتح ط ، پاک کرنے کے بعد جو پانی باقی رہ جائے اس کو طھارۃ ط کے ضمہ کے ساتھ ۔اور پاک کرنے کا جو آلہ ہوتا ہے جیسے پانی اور مٹی اس کو طھارة ط کے کسرہ کے ساتھ بولتے ہیں۔ پاک پانی نہ ہو تو مٹی پاک کرنے کے لئے چند شرائط کے ساتھ پانی کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے۔ نوٹ: اقسام طہارت : (۱) اعتقادات کی طہارت جیسے اللہ رسول اور قیامت کے ساتھ وہ اعتقاد رکھنا جو قرآن اور حدیث کے مطابق ہو (۲) مال کی طہارۃ جیسے مال کی زکوۃ دینا (۳) بدن کی طہارۃ جیسے وضو کر نا غسل کرنا۔ کپڑے کی طھارۃ جیسے کپڑے کو پاک کرنا۔ طہارۃ مصدر میں یہ سب طہارتیں شامل ہیں۔
پانی کے احکام
ضروری نوٹ : حضرت مصنف نے پانی کے احکام پہلے لائے، کیونکہ پانی سے ہی طہارت ہوتی ہے، اور طہارت سے ہی نماز وغیرہ پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔ ترجمه: (1) جس پانی سے پاک کرنا جائز ہے وہ سات قسم کے پانی ہیں۔ [1] آسمان کا پانی، [۲]سمندرکا پانی[۳] نہر کا پانی [۴] کنواں کا پانی، [۵] برف [۶]، اور اولے سے پگھلا ہوا پانی [۷] چشمہ کا پانی۔
تشریح یہ سات قسم کے پانی ہیں جو پاک میں اور ان سے جسم کو اور کپڑوں کو پاک کرنا جائز ہے، کیوں کہ یہ خود بھی پاک ہیں اور دوسروں کو بھی پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتے ہیں۔

Book of Purification
Necessary note: 'al-tahara' is a masdar. And 'kitab al-tahara' is an incomplete genitive construction. Therefore one must assume before it a mubtada or at its end a deleted khabar. For example, 'hadha kitab al-tahara', or 'kitab al-tahara hadha', or consider 'kitab al-tahara' as maf'ul of 'iqra' and phrase it 'iqra' kitab al-tahara'.
Proof of tahara: The verse contains proof of tahara: 'O you who believe, when you stand up for prayer, wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows, and wipe your heads and your feet up to the ankles. And if you are in a state of janaba, then purify yourselves.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). In hadith: 'Purity is half of faith.' Also: 'The key to prayer is purity.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the key to prayer, p. 6, no. 3). Reason for giving precedence to tahara:
Point (1): Among acts of worship, prayer is most important. After faith, the greatest importance is given to prayer. The divine command: 'Those who believe in the unseen and establish prayer' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:3). In hadith: 'Prayer is the pillar of religion; whoever establishes it has established religion.' Therefore all authors have given precedence to the chapters on prayer. And the condition of prayer is tahara; without tahara, prayer is not valid. Hence the book of tahara is given precedence. (2) Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime. Zakat is obligatory once a year. Fasting is obligatory one month a year. But prayer is obligatory five times a day. Therefore its need occurs repeatedly. And for prayer, tahara is needed, so the need for tahara also occurs five times a day. Thus due to the frequency of need, tahara is mentioned first. Linguistic research: 'Kitab' is on the pattern of 'fi'al' and means 'maf'ul' (the object). Just as 'libas' is used in the meaning of 'malbus' (what is worn), similarly 'kitab' is used in the meaning of 'maktub' (what is written). Its meaning is a collection of written pages. 'Kataba' means to write. Since a book contains many written issues, it is called 'kitab'. Note: In books of fiqh, three terms are used: (1) Kitab, (2) Bab, (3) Fasl. A kitab contains issues of various types and kinds, and sometimes includes several abwab. So it is a general term. A bab contains one type of issues. And a fasl contains one kind of issues.

(1) The waters with which purification is permissible are seven waters: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, water melted from snow, water melted from hail, and spring water.
Tahara: 'Tahr' is its masdar; its meaning is cleanliness and purity; its opposite is 'danas'. In Shari'ah, washing specific limbs is called tahara. Its opposite is hadath. Some scholars say that raising a hadath or removing najas is called tahara. Note: The act of purifying is 'tahara' with fatha on ta; the water remaining after purification is 'tuhara' with damma on ta; and the instrument of purification, like water and earth, is 'tihara' with kasra on ta. If pure water is not available, then earth, with certain conditions, stands in place of water for purification. Note: Types of tahara: (1) Purification of beliefs, like having a belief in Allah, the Messenger, and the Day of Judgment that conforms to Quran and Hadith. (2) Purification of wealth, like giving zakat on wealth. (3) Purification of the body, like performing wudu and ghusl. Purification of clothes, like making clothes pure. As a masdar, tahara includes all these purifications.
Rulings on water
Necessary note: The author brought the rulings on water first, because purification is done with water, and through purification prayer etc. can be performed. Translation: (1) The waters with which purification is permissible are seven types: [1] Rainwater, [2] Seawater, [3] River water, [4] Well water, [5] Snow, [6] Water melted from hail, [7] Spring water.
Explanation: These seven types of water are pure, and with them it is permissible to purify the body and clothes, because they themselves are pure and also have the capacity to purify others.
Point (1): All these waters are pure, so they do not become impure due to a small amount of impurity falling into them. Therefore performing wudu and ghusl with them is permissible. (2) Rainwater is pure; regarding it there is this verse: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (Surah al-Furqan 25:48). (3) Regarding seawater, there is this hadith: From Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: A man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'May we perform wudu with seawater?' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'It is pure, its water is pure, and its dead [animals] are permissible.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on seawater being pure, p. 21, no. 69; Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu with seawater, p. 13, no. 83). This hadith shows that seawater is pure and its dead fish is also halal. The sea is large and the river is small, therefore it

Commentary
This passage is an introductory lesson from a Hanafi fiqh text, opening the chapter on purification (Kitab al-Taharah). The author first explains the grammatical construction of the title, noting that 'kitab al-tahara' is an incomplete genitive phrase requiring an implicit mubtada or khabar. The author then provides evidence (dalil) for the obligation of purification from the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) and hadith ("Purity is half of faith," "The key to prayer is purity"), establishing the importance of taharah. A linguistic note follows: the word 'kitab' is derived from 'kataba' (to write) and means a collection of written material, like 'libas' means clothing. The author distinguishes between three organizational terms in fiqh works: 'kitab' (general topic), 'bab' (chapter on a specific type), and 'fasl' (section on a particular kind).

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): Linguistically: cleanliness and purity. Technically: the removal of hadath (ritual impurity) or the removal of najasa (filth).
ماء طهور (ma' tahur): Water that is inherently pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir); used for wudu, ghusl, and removing najasa.
ماء البحر (ma' al-bahr): Seawater; included in the seven pure waters, valid for purification.

Taharah: Definition and Types (Hanafi Perspective)
Definitions and types of taharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of taharah in Hanafi fiqh and identify its three categories: purification of beliefs, wealth, and body/clothing.

Core Idea
Taharah in Hanafi fiqh encompasses physical, spiritual, and financial purity — it is more than just washing.

The word 'taharah' is often translated simply as 'purification', but this passage reveals its depth. The author begins with the linguistic root, then moves to the technical fiqh definition, highlighting that taharah includes both removing ritual impurity (hadath) and physical filth (najas). He also notes the careful distinction in vowel patterns — a hallmark of Hanafi precision. Finally, he expands the concept beyond the body to include beliefs and wealth, showing that purity is a comprehensive legal and spiritual obligation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic vs. technical meaning
Identify the root meaning of taharah (purity, cleanliness) and then note how the Shariah narrows it to specific actions — washing particular limbs or removing hadath/najas.
The opposite of taharah is either najas or hadath depending on context.
2
Analyze the verbal noun variations
Pay attention to the three vowellings of 'taharah': fatḥah for the act, ḍammah for the remaining water, kasrah for the instrument. This linguistic precision is important for accurate fiqh terminology.
Hanafi scholars often derived subtle legal implications from such vowel differences.
3
Identify the three categories of taharah
The author lists purification of beliefs (iʿtiqādāt), wealth (māl), and body (badan) including clothing. Note that these are all included under the same verbal noun 'taharah'.
This classification shows that fiqh addresses both inward and outward purification.
4
Recognize the scope in Hanafi fiqh
Understand that taharah is the key that unlocks many acts of worship. The conditions for water, the substitute of soil, and the distinction between hadath and najas all build on this foundation.
Later lessons will detail the rulings for each type of taharah.

Book of Purification. Purification: tahara is its verbal noun, its meaning is purity and cleanliness, its opposite is filth. In Shariah, washing specific limbs is called taharah. Its opposite is hadath. Some scholars say that removing hadath or removing najas is called taharah. Note: The act of purifying is called taharah with fatha on ta, the water that remains after purifying is called tuharah with damma on ta, and the instrument used for purifying like water and soil is called tiharah with kasra on ta. If pure water is not available, then soil stands in place of water with certain conditions. Note: Types of taharah: (1) Purification of beliefs, like believing in Allah, Messenger, and the Day of Judgment in accordance with Quran and Hadith. (2) Purification of wealth, like giving zakat of wealth. (3) Purification of body, like performing wudu and ghusl. Purification of clothing, like cleansing clothes. The verbal noun taharah includes all these purifications.

حدث (hadath): A state of ritual impurity that requires wudu or ghusl.

The Seven Types of Purifying Water
Categorization of purifying waters with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven types of purifying water and state the textual proof for each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Seven pure waters are tahur: rain, sea, river, well, snow, hail, spring—all supported by Quran and Sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling that seven specific types of water are inherently pure and purifying. Understanding this classification is essential for valid wudu, ghusl, and removal of impurities. The author lists each water type and provides explicit proofs from the Quran and Hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that seven types of water are permissible for purification. Determine the hukm level: these waters are tahur (pure and purifying).
The ruling applies to using these waters for wudu, ghusl, and removing najas.
2
Examine the proof for each water type
For each of the seven, note the specific dalil: Quran 25:48 for rain, hadith from Tirmidhi/Abu Dawud for sea, analogy for river, hadith from Tirmidhi for well, hadith from Muslim for snow/hail, and Quran 39:21 for spring.
The proofs are either direct (Quran/hadith) or by analogy (river is like sea).
3
Understand the legal consequence
Because these waters are tahur, they remain pure even if a small impurity falls into them, as long as one of their qualities (color, taste, smell) does not change.
This is the default Hanafi position; other schools may have different thresholds.
4
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Recognize that any natural water from acceptable sources is tahur. For example, melted ice from a mountain stream is included via the proof for snow/hail.
The classification is based on origin, not artificial processing.

The waters with which purification is permissible are seven waters: rainwater, seawater, river water, well water, melted snow, melted hail, and spring water. Rulings of water: Essential note: The author presented the rulings of water first, because purification is done with water, and through purification prayer and other acts can be performed. Translation: (1) The water with which purification is permissible is seven types of water: [1] Rainwater, [2] Seawater, [3] River water, [4] Well water, [5] Snow, [6] Melted hail, [7] Spring water. Explanation: These seven types of water are pure, and it is permissible to purify the body and clothes with them, because they are themselves pure and have the ability to purify others. Reason: (1) All these waters are pure, so they do not become impure by a small impurity falling into them. Therefore, performing wudu and ghusl with them is permissible. (2) Rainwater is pure; regarding it there is this verse: 'And We send down from the sky water that is purifying' (Quran 25:48). (3) Regarding seawater, there is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) that a man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ... 'Can we perform wudu with seawater?' The Messenger of Allah said: 'It is purifying, its water is purifying, and its dead animals are permissible.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on seawater being purifying, p. 21, no. 69; Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu with seawater, p. 13, no. 83) This hadith shows that seawater is pure and its dead fish are halal. The sea is large and the river is small, therefore this hadith proves that river water is also pure. (4) Regarding wells, there is this hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'O Messenger of Allah, can we perform wudu from the well of Buda'ah?' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Water is purifying and nothing makes it impure.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on water not being made impure by anything, p. 21, no. 66) This hadith states that well water is pure. (5) Regarding snow and hail, there is this hadith: I heard Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa narrate from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to say: 'O Allah, to You is all praise filling the heavens and the earth and whatever You wish besides; O Allah, purify me with snow, hail, and cold water.' (Muslim, chapter on what to say when raising the head from ruku', p. 198, no. 1069) This hadith mentions purification with snow and hail, indicating that the water from snow and hail is pure and has the ability to purify others. (6) Regarding springs, there is this verse: 'Do you not see that Allah sends down from the sky water and then makes it flow as springs in the earth?' (Quran 39:21) This verse indicates that spring water is pure. Lexicon: al-bahr: sea; al-birr: well; dhab: to melt; thalj: snow; barad: hail, the ice that freezes on the ground is called thalj, and the ice that falls from the sky like pebbles is called barad; 'ayn: spring.

Commentary
This lesson details the seven types of water that are inherently pure and purifying (tahur). The author provides textual evidence from Quran and Sunnah for each type. The Hanafi position is that these waters remain pure even if a small impurity falls into them, as long as one of its three qualities (color, taste, smell) does not change significantly. The lesson also clarifies that seawater is purifying and its dead fish are halal. The linguistic notes at the end help clarify technical terms.

Key Terms
طهور (tahur): Water that is itself pure and has the property to purify other things.
مطلق پانی (mutlaq pani): Absolute water, free from any admixture, as mentioned in the next lesson.
برد (barad): Hail, frozen rain that falls from the sky.

Taharah — Purification

6 min
Mutlaq Water: The Foundation of Purification
Introduces five water categories and defines mutlaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three defining characteristics of mutlaq water and identify the Quranic and hadith evidence that establishes its purifying status.

Core Idea
Mutlaq water is pure and purifying, without any disliked quality — the foundational water for all purification.

Water is the primary means of purification in Islam, but not all water is equal in the Hanafi school. This lesson introduces the five-fold classification of water and delves into the first and highest category: mutlaq (absolute) water. Understanding its precise definition — pure, purifying, and free from dislike — is essential for valid acts of worship like wudu and ghusl. We will then examine the Quranic and Prophetic proofs that establish this water as tahur.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the five-category framework
The Hanafi school divides water into five types: mutlaq (absolute), musta'mal (used), mixed with a pure substance (e.g., rose water), mixed with an impure substance (e.g., water that has changed color/taste due to impurity), and mashkuk (suspect, i.e., questionable). Each category has different rulings for purification. The first category, mutlaq, is the most fundamental.
Mutlaq water is the default water for all acts of purification.
2
Define mutlaq water precisely
Mutlaq water must satisfy three conditions: (1) it is itself pure (tahir), (2) it has the ability to purify other things (mutahhir), and (3) it is not disliked (ghayr makruh). Water that is disliked includes water left over from wudu or ghusl, or water that has been heated excessively in the sun (according to some Hanafi scholars).
The term 'mutlaq' means 'unrestricted' or 'absolute' — it is not tied to any additional description.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The primary Quranic verse is Surah Al-Furqan 25:48: 'And We send down from the sky water that is tahur.' The word 'tahur' is an intensive form (fa'ul) indicating that it is inherently pure and continuously purifying. This establishes that celestial water (rain, snow, hail) is mutlaq.
4
Confirm with the Sunnah
The hadith of Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) records that when asked about performing wudu with seawater, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'It is tahur, its water is purifying, and its dead (sea animals) are permissible.' This extends the category of mutlaq water to all naturally occurring waters that remain in their original state, including seas, rivers, and springs.
The hadith uses the same word 'tahur' as the Quran, affirming that seawater shares the same ruling.
5
Apply the definition
Any water that meets the three conditions — pure, purifying, not disliked — is mutlaq. This includes rainwater, river water, well water, spring water, and seawater, provided they have not been altered by use or admixture. Water that has been used for wudu (musta'mal) is tahir but no longer mutahhir, so it falls into the second category.
The seven types of water mentioned earlier in the text (e.g., rain, snow, hail, etc.) all fall under mutlaq.

Commentary
This lesson introduces the five categories of water according to the Hanafi school, and explains the first category: mutlaq (absolute) water. Mutlaq water is water that is pure in itself and purifying for others, without any disliked quality. The author notes that the seven types mentioned earlier fall under this category. He then provides textual evidence from Quran and Hadith to establish the purifying nature of such water.

Key Terms
مطلق پانی (mutlaq pani): Absolute water, pure in itself and purifying, without any admixture or dislike.
طاهر مطهّر (tahir mutahhir): Pure and purifying, refers to water that is both clean and can make other things clean.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked, which in this context means water that is disliked for use, e.g., water left after wudu or ghusl.
طهور (tahur): An intensive form indicating water that is inherently pure and continuously purifying.

Key Takeaway
Mutlaq water is the pure and purifying water that forms the basis for all purification in the Hanafi school; it must be tahir, mutahhir, and ghayr makruh.

Absolute Water: Definition and Proof
Defines and proves absolute water from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of absolute water and identify its proof from the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Absolute water is pure and purifying by nature — the default for all purification.

Water is the primary means of purification in Islam. But not all water is equal. The Hanafi school classifies water into five types, and the first and fundamental type is 'absolute water' (al-ma' al-mutlaq). In this lesson, we will define what makes water absolute and examine the Quranic and Prophetic proofs that establish its purifying quality.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of absolute water
Based on the text: water that is pure (tahir), purifying (mutahhir), and not disliked (ghayr makruh).
2
List the seven subtypes mentioned
Identify the seven types of water that fall under this category: rain, sea, river, well, snow, hail, and spring.
All these are absolute as long as they remain unchanged.
3
Identify the primary proof from the Quran
Locate the verse (Surah Al-Furqan 25:48) that uses the word 'tahur'.
The word 'tahur' is a hyperbolic form implying both purity and purifying ability.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith about sea water (from Abu Hurairah) also uses 'tahur', confirming that sea water is absolute.
5
Confirm the ruling
Synthesize: absolute water is valid for all purification without any dislike.

Book of Purification. Snow, hail, and spring water. (2) Then waters are of five types: pure, purifying, not disliked, and it is water... It is proven from hadith that river water is also pure. (4) Regarding the well, there is this hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... he said: O Messenger of Allah, do we perform wudu from Bi'r Buda'ah?... He said: Water is purifying, nothing makes it impure. (Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that well water is pure. (5) Regarding snow and hail, this hadith: I heard Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa narrate from the Prophet that he would say: O Allah, to You is praise filling the heavens, etc. then: O Allah, purify me with snow, hail, and cold water. (Muslim) This hadith shows that snow and hail water is pure and has the ability to purify others. (6) Regarding a spring, there is the verse: Do you not see that Allah sends down water from the sky and causes it to emerge as springs in the earth? (Surah Zumar 39:21) This verse shows that spring water is pure. Lexicon: al-bahr: sea; al-birr: well; dhab: to melt; thaj: snow; barad: hail; 'ayn: spring. Translation: (2) Then water is of five types. (1) Pure, purifying, and not disliked, that is absolute water. Explanation: ... that is the first type, called absolute water because it has no admixture and no karahah. The seven types mentioned earlier are all absolute water. Proof: In this verse and hadith, the word tahur is used, meaning it is pure and can purify others. (1) The verse: And We send down from the sky pure water (tahuran) (Surah Furqan 25:48). (2) The hadith: From Abu Hurairah... a man asked: Do we perform wudu from the sea? He said: Its water is purifying (tahur) and its dead animals are permissible. (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that sea water is tahur, i.e., pure and purifying.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the first category of water: absolute water (al-ma' al-mutlaq). The author begins by listing seven types of water that fall under this category: rain, sea, river, well, snow, hail, and spring water. He then states that waters are divided into five types (of which this is the first). The first type is: pure (tahir) in itself, purifying (mutahhir) for others, and not disliked (ghayr makruh). This is absolute water. The author provides proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The verse [25:48] uses the word tahur, which indicates both purity and purifying power. The sea water hadith also uses tahur. The author explains that absolute water has no admixture and no dislike attached to it. This is the default category upon which all other water rulings are based.

Key Terms
الماء المطلق (al-ma' al-mutlaq): Water that has not changed from its original creation and has no added substance that would alter its purity.
طهور (tahur): A quality of water meaning it is pure in itself and has the ability to purify other things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of absolute water according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is pure but not purifying.
B) It is pure and purifying but disliked.
C) It is pure, purifying, and not disliked.
D) It is impure.

Key Takeaway
Absolute water (al-ma' al-mutlaq) is the default water for purification; it is defined as pure, purifying, and not disliked, and its basis is the Quranic word 'tahur'.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

The Ruling on Cat's Leftover Water (Su'r al-Hirrah): Pure but Disliked
Ruling and proofs for water left by a cat: pure, purifying, but disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water drunk by a cat, explain the evidence used, and reconcile the apparent conflict between hadiths.

Core Idea
Cat's leftover water is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzihi) due to ease in the Shariah.

This lesson examines the second category of water in Hanafi fiqh: water from which a cat (or similar domestic animal) has drunk. The author rules it pure and purifying but disliked. We will explore the evidence from Hadith and the method of reconciling apparent contradictions to reach this nuanced ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on cat's leftover water? It is pure, purifying, but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
The ruling is specifically for water that is little (qalil).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites several hadiths: (a) the washing hadith (dog vs cat), (b) the hadith of the cat being a predator, (c) the hadith of the cat being among those who go around, (d) the hadith of Aisha tilting the vessel, and (e) the athar of Ibn Umar.
The hadiths are from Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Dar Qutni, and Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The washing hadith seems to imply impurity (wash once), but the other hadiths show purity and ease. The Hanafi reconciliation: the washing once is not obligatory but recommended (mustahabb) due to the principle of ease (tashil).
The key is combining all evidence; the ruling becomes makruh tanzihi, not najis.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars might consider the cat's leftover impure based on the literal washing hadith, but the Hanafi school reconciles the evidence differently.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the water is pure and purifying but disliked when other water is available. This is established in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The tarjih is based on harmonizing all hadiths and the principle of ease.

(3) And pure, purifying, disliked: it is water from which a cat or similar has drunk and it is little. Translation: (3) The second type of water: pure, purifying but disliked. That is water from which a cat or similar animal has drunk and the water is little. Explanation: This is the second type: it is pure and can purify other things, but due to the cat drinking, it becomes disliked. If other water is available, one should perform wudu with that; if not, one may perform wudu with this water. Wudu and ghusl are valid because it still has purifying ability. Proof: (1) The cat is a predatory animal, so its leftover should be pure, but it lives in the house and it is difficult to avoid, so the Shariah facilitated and made its leftover disliked. (2) Hadith: The vessel should be washed if a dog drinks from it seven times, with earth on first and last, and if a cat drinks from it, one time. (Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that cat's leftover is impure. (3) Another hadith indicates that cat is predatory, so its leftover should be pure: The Prophet said: The cat is a predator. (Sunan... Dar Qutni) (4) Another hadith indicates that the cat lives in the house, so its leftover is pure: from Kabshah bint Ka'b: Abu Qatadah... the Prophet said: It is not impure; it is of those who go around you. (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) (5) Another hadith: from Aishah: The Prophet would tilt the vessel for the cat to drink, then perform wudu with its leftover. (Dar Qutni) These hadiths show cat's leftover is pure. So combining them, they say it is makruh tanzihi. The same applies to all domestic animals. (6) A narration from Ibn Umar: He disliked the leftover of the cat. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq)
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the second category of water: water that has been drunk by a cat or similar domesticated animal. The author states that such water is pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir) but disliked (makruh). The degree of dislike is tanzihi, meaning it is better to avoid but using it is valid. The author provides a detailed discussion of the evidence. He reconciles apparent contradictions in the hadiths: some hadiths seem to indicate impurity, while others indicate purity. The Hanafi conclusion is that the cat's leftover is pure but disliked due to the ease of the Shariah. This applies to all animals that live in the house, such as chickens, etc., though the text specifically mentions cats and similar animals.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water or food after an animal drinks or eats from a vessel.
الهرة (al-hirrah): The domestic cat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on water from which a cat has drunk?
A) It is impure (najis).
B) It is pure and purifying without any dislike.
C) It is pure and purifying but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
D) It is permissible only if no other water is available.

Key Takeaway
Cat's leftover water is pure and purifying, but its use is lightly disliked (makruh tanzihi) to facilitate ease for domestic cat owners.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Water Made Makruh by Cat's Leftover (Su'ur al-Hirrah)
Ruling and proofs for water that is pure but disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water from which a cat has drunk, explain the reconciliation of conflicting hadiths, and apply the ruling to similar domestic animals.

Core Idea
Cat's leftover water is pure and purifying, but using it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) when other water is available.

This lesson examines the second category of water in the Hanafi school: water that is pure and purifying but disliked. The specific case is water drunk by a cat or similar domestic animal when the water is little. You will learn how the Hanafi school reconciles apparently conflicting hadiths to derive this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using water from which a cat has drunk. The ruling is that the water is tahir (pure) and mutahhir (purifying) but makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked).
This is a category of water, not an act of worship.
2
Locate the dalil (proofs) from Sunnah
The text cites multiple hadiths: one ordering washing a vessel after a cat drinks (Tirmidhi), and others showing the Prophet tilting vessels for cats and using their leftover water (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Dar Qutni).
All hadiths are ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how each proof is used)
The first hadith (imperative 'yughsal') might imply impurity, but the other hadiths (practical actions) indicate purity. Hanafis combine: the command is for caution, leading to dislike, not impurity.
The Hanafi method of jam' al-adillah (reconciliation) is applied.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement) with other schools
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that cat's leftover is pure without any dislike. They rely on the hadiths showing purity and consider the washing command specific to dogs.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether avoiding such water is recommended or not.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred position)
The Hanafi school takes the middle path: the water is pure (due to evidence of purity) but disliked (due to the cautionary command). This ruling is mufta bihi and based on reconciling all texts.
The ruling applies to all domestic animals that cannot be easily avoided.

(۳) وطاهر مطهّر مكروه وهو ما شرب منه الهرة ونحوها وكان قليلا. ترجمه : (۳) دوسرا پانی پاک ہو دوسرے کو پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو لیکن مکر وہ ہو، یہ وہ پانی ہے جس سے بلی ، یا اس قسم کے جانور نے پیا ہو اور پانی تھوڑا ہو۔ تشریح : یہ دوسرے قسم کا پانی ہے، کہ وہ خود پاک ہے اور دوسری چیز کو پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت بھی ہے لیکن بلی کے پینے کی وجہ سے پانی مکروہ ہو گیا، اگر دوسرا پانی موجود ہو تو اس سے وضو کرے اور نہ ہو تو اس پانی سے وضو کرے، وضو اور غسل جائز ہو جائے گا کیونکہ پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے۔ وجه : (1) بلی پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہ گھر میں رہتی ہے اور اس سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے شریعت نے تسہیل دیدی اور اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہوا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يغسل الاناء اذا ولغ فيه الكلب سبع مرات اولاهن واخراهن بالتراب واذا ولغت فيه الهرة غسل مرة ۔ ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی سور الکلب ،ص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلی کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہے۔(۳) اور دوسری حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بلی پھاڑ کھانے والی ہے ، اس لئے اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونا چاہئے ، حدیث یہ ہے عن ابی ھریرۃ قال النبى الله الله السنور سبع. (سن اسمجھتی ، باب سور الھر ق ، ج اول ص ۳۷۷ نمبر ۱۷۶ار دار قطنی باب سو را گھر ۃ، ج اول بص ۲۸، نمبر ۲۰۲) (۴) اور اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بلی گھر میں رہتی ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا پاک ہے ، اس لئے دونوں حدیثوں کو ملا کر یہی کہا جائے گا کہ بلی کا جوٹھا پاک تو ہے لیکن مکروہ ہے ، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن كبشة بنت کعب بن مالک. ان ابا قتادة دخل عليها قالت فسكبت له وضوء ا قالت فجائت هرة تشرب فأصغى لها الاناء حتى شربت ، قالت كبشة فرأني انظر اليه فقال أ تعجبين يا ابنة اخى ؟ فقلت نعم ، قال ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال انها ليست بنجس انما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی سوراکھر ق ص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۲ را بوداؤد شریف، باب سؤر الهرة ، ص۱۲ نمبر ۷۵ ) (۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ بلی کے لئے برتن ٹیڑھا کیا کرتے تھے ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس کا جوٹھا پاک ہے، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة أنها قالت : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمر به الهرة فيصغى لها الاناء ، فتشرب ، ثم يتوضأ بفضلها - ( دار قطنی ، باب سو را هر ة ، ج اول ص ۶۷ نمبر ۱۹۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلی کا جھوٹا پاک ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں حدیثوں کو ملانے کی وجہ سے یہ کہتے ہیں کہ بلی کا جوٹھا مکروہ تنزیہی ہے ۔ یہی حال گھر میں رہنے والے تمام جانوروں کا ہے۔ (۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بلی کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر أنه كان يكره سؤر السنور - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب سور السنور ، ج اول ص ۷۷، نمبر ۳۴۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بلی کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے۔

ثمرة النجاح جلد ا
۳۹
كتاب الطهارة
(۴) وطاهر غير مطهّر وهو ما استعمل لرفع حدث او لقربة كالوضوء على الوضوء بنيته. لغت : و كان قليلا دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا تالاب یا حوض ہو تو اس کو غدیر عظیم، بڑا تالاب کہتے ہیں اور حنفیہ کے نزدیک زیادہ پانی کہتے ہیں ، اس میں کوئی ناپاکی گر جائے، یا اس سے بلی یا چوہا، یا سانپ پانی پی لے تو یہ نا پاک نہیں ہوتا ، اور اس سے کم ہو تو اس کو تھوڑا پانی کہتے ہیں، اس میں ناپا کی گر جائے تو پانی نا پاک ہو جاتا ہے، اور بلی یا چوہا، یا سانپ پانی پی لے تو پانی پاک تو رہے گا لیکن پانی مکروہ ہو جائے گا۔ قلیلا تھوڑا پانی ، یہاں مراد ہے جو پانی دو در دہ سے کم ہو ، یعنی دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا تالاب سے کم ہو۔ ھرة : بلی مطھر : مبالغہ کا صیغہ ہے دوسرے کو پاک کرنے والا۔
The third type: pure and purifying but disliked, which is water from which a cat or similar animal drank and it was little. Translation: (3) Second water is pure and has the ability to purify others but is disliked; this is water from which a cat or similar animal drank and the water was little. Explanation: This is the second type of water; it is itself pure and also capable of purifying other things, but due to the cat drinking, the water became disliked. If another water is available, perform ablution with that; if not, then perform ablution with this water. Ablution and bath are valid because it has the ability to purify. Reason: (1) The cat is a carnivorous animal, so its leftover should be pure, but it stays in the house and it is difficult to avoid it; therefore, the Shariah made it easy and its leftover is disliked. (2) Hadith: from Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (SAW): 'Wash the vessel when a dog drinks from it seven times, the first and last with soil, and when a cat drinks from it, wash it once.' (Tirmidhi) From this hadith, it is known that the cat's leftover is impure. (3) Another hadith shows that the cat is carnivorous so its leftover should be pure: from Abu Hurairah, the Prophet (SAW) said: 'The cat is a wild beast.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi? Dar Qutni) (4) And from this hadith it is known that the cat lives in the house, so its leftover is pure. Therefore, combining the two hadiths, it is said that the cat's leftover is pure but disliked. The hadith is from Kabshah bint Ka'b ibn Malik: Abu Qatadah entered upon her; she said she poured water for him for ablution, then a cat came to drink, and he tilted the vessel for her until she drank. Kabshah said: I saw him looking, and he said, 'Do you wonder, O daughter of my brother?' She said yes. He said, 'The Messenger of Allah (SAW) said: It is not impure; it is one of those who go around among you.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) (5) In this hadith, he used to tilt the vessel for the cat, indicating that its leftover is pure. Hadith from Aisha: She said: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) would pass by a cat and tilt the vessel for it, and it would drink, then he would perform ablution with its leftover. (Dar Qutni) From these hadiths, it is said that the cat's leftover is pure. Therefore, combining the two hadiths, they say that the cat's leftover is makruh tanzihi. The same applies to all domestic animals. (6) In this athar, it is that the cat's leftover is disliked: from Ibn Umar, that he disliked the leftover of a cat. (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq) Linguistic note: 'wa kana qalilan' - a pond or basin ten cubits long and ten cubits wide is called a large pond (ghadir 'azim), and in the Hanafi school it is called abundant water; if impurity falls into it, or a cat, rat, or snake drinks from it, it does not become impure. Less than that is called small water; if impurity falls into it, the water becomes impure; and if a cat, rat, or snake drinks from it, the water remains pure but becomes disliked. 'Qalilan' means little water; here it means water less than two kurrs, i.e., less than a pond ten cubits long and ten cubits wide. 'Hirrah': cat. 'Mutahhir': intensive form, meaning purifying.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the second category of water: water that is pure and purifying but makruh. The author first states the ruling: water from which a cat (or similar domestic animal) has drunk, provided the water is little (qalil), is pure and purifying but disliked. He then explains the practical application: if other water is available, use that; if not, use this water as it remains valid for purification. The bulk of the passage is devoted to proofs. The reasoning (wajh) is structured: cats are carnivores by nature but live intimately with humans, so the law eases; conflicting hadiths are reconciled. The hadith from Abu Hurairah ordering washing a vessel after a cat once seems to indicate impurity, but other hadiths (from Kabshah and Aisha) show the Prophet tilting vessels for cats and using their leftover water, indicating purity. The Hanafi reconciliation is that cat's leftover is pure but makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked). The linguistic note clarifies that 'qalil' refers to water less than a large pond (ghadir 'azim) of 10×10 cubits, i.e., less than two kurrs (approximately 200 liters). The same ruling applies to all domestic animals that cannot be easily avoided. The hadiths are from reliable sources (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Dar Qutni, Musannaf Abdur Razzaq). The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting textual evidence through the principle of combining proofs (jam' al-adillah) rather than preferring one over the other. The ultimate ruling is that the water is pure and can be used for purification, but it is better to avoid it if possible.

Key Terms
طاهر مطهر (tahir mutahhir): Water that is pure in itself and capable of purifying other things
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; here specifically makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not sinful but better to avoid
سؤر (su'ur): Leftover water after an animal drinks
قليل (qalil): Little water; water less than a ghadir 'azim (10x10 cubits pond, approx. 200 liters)
غدير عظيم (ghadir 'azim): A large pond or basin of water of dimensions 10 cubits by 10 cubits, considered abundant water

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is cat's leftover water considered makruh tanzihi rather than pure or impure in the Hanafi school?
A) Because cats are impure animals
B) Because conflicting hadiths are reconciled, showing purity but with slight dislike
C) Because the water is little and cats are carnivores, so it becomes impure
D) Because the Prophet explicitly said it is makruh

Key Takeaway
Cat's leftover water is pure and purifying but makruh tanzihi because the Hanafi school reconciles conflicting hadiths by combining them rather than rejecting any.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Used Water (Ma' Musta'mal) – Pure but Not Purifying
Ruling and proofs for used water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ma' musta'mal and explain why it is pure but not purifying, using the textual proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Water used for worship remains pure but loses its purifying power.

This lesson addresses a key category of water in Hanafi fiqh: ma' musta'mal – water that has been used for a valid act of purification or worship. Understanding its ruling is essential for correctly performing wudu and ghusl. We will examine when water becomes musta'mal, its legal status, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Define ma' musta'mal
Identify the two ways water becomes musta'mal: (1) removing hadath (ritual impurity) in wudu/ghusl, (2) performing wudu for qurbah (closeness to Allah) by one already in purity.
Intention is key for qurbah-based wudu.
2
State the ruling and its parts
The water is tahir (pure) – it does not make impurity – but ghayr mutahhir (not purifying) – it cannot be used for wudu/ghusl or to remove physical impurity.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
3
Examine the proofs
First proof: rational – Companions' clothes got wet from wudu but they did not wash them, meaning the water is pure. Second proof: hadith – Prophet gave his wudu water to drink, indicating purity but not intending its reuse for purification.
Two hadith from Bukhari are cited.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Distinguish musta'mal from water used for najasah (impure) and from wudu without intention (which remains purifying).
Only water used intentionally for worship becomes musta'mal.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is hold that ma' musta'mal remains purifying because the water's substance unchanged. Hanafis argue the 'use' in worship removes its purifying capacity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴) تیسرا پانی پاک ہے لیکن پاک کرنے والا نہیں ہے، یہ وہ پانی ہے جس کو حدث کو دور کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا ہو، یا قربت حاصل کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا ہو، جیسے قربت کی نیت سے وضو پر وضو کیا ہو۔
تشریح : یہ تیسرے قسم کا پانی ہے، اس کو ماء مستعمل کہتے ہیں، یہ پانی پاک تو ہے اس لئے کسی کپڑے پر لگ جائے تو کپڑا نا پاک نہیں ہوگا لیکن یہ پانی کسی چیز کو پاک نہیں کرتا، چنانچہ اس پانی سے وضو کرنا جائز نہیں اور اس سے ناپاک کپڑا پاک نہیں ہوگا۔ دو طرح سے پانی مستعمل ہوتا ہے [1] آدمی حدث والا ہو ، وہ حدث دور کرنے کے لئے وضو کرے، اب اس وضو سے جو پانی گرے وہ ماء مستعمل ہے ۔ [۲] آدمی پہلے سے وضو کیا ہوا ہے پھر قربت اور ثواب حاصل کرنے کے لئے دوبارہ وضو کرے تو اس وضو سے جو پانی گرے گا وہ ماء مستعمل ہے۔ [۳] آدمی کے جس حصے پر نجاست موجود ہو اس نجاست کو دھونے کے لئے پانی استعمال کرے تو یہ پانی ناپاک ہوگا ، اس سے کسی چیز کو پاک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ [۴] آدمی پہلے سے پاک ہو مثلا وضو کیا ہو، اور وضو کی نیت کے بغیر وضو کر لیا تو یہ پانی مستعمل نہیں ہے، اس سے دوبارہ وضوکرنا جائز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماء مستعمل صحابہ کے کپڑوں میں وضو اور غسل کے بعد لگتار ہا لیکن آج تک کسی نے ماء مستعمل کی وجہ سے کپر انہیں دھویا۔ اور پاک کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل عرب کو پانی کی سخت ضرورت ہونے کے باوجود کسی نے ماء مستعمل استعمال کر کے وضو یا غسل نہیں کیا۔ اور نہ اس کو دوسرے برتن میں وضو یا غسل کے لئے رکھا ہو (۲) پاک ہونے کی دلیل وہ احادیث ہیں جن میں حضور نے وضو کے لئے استعمال کیا ہوا پانی مریضوں کو پلایا ہے۔ اگر ماء مستعمل پاک نہ ہوتا تو آپ اس کو بیماروں کو کیسے پلاتے ؟ حدیث میں ہے عن جابر يقول جاء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يعودني وانا مريض لا اعقل فتوضأ وصب على من وضوئه فعقلت ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صب النبی به وضوءه على المغمی علیہ، ص۳۲ نمبر ۱۹۴) (۳) سمعت السائب بن يزيد يقول ذهبت بی خالتي الى النبي فقالت یا رسول الله ان ابن اختی وقع فمسح رأسى ودعا لى بالبركة ثم توضأ فشربت من وضوءه بخارى شر ه. ( بخاری شریف، باب استعمال فضل وضوء الناس
Translation: (4) The third water is pure but not purifying; it is water that has been used for removing hadath or for attaining closeness (qurbah), like performing ablution on top of ablution with intention. Explanation: This is the third type of water, called ma' musta'mal. This water is pure, so if it touches cloth, the cloth does not become impure, but this water does not purify anything; thus making ablution with it is invalid and it cannot purify impure cloth. Water becomes musta'mal in two ways: [1] A person with hadath performs wudu to remove it; the water that drips from that wudu is ma' musta'mal. [2] A person already in wudu performs wudu again for reward; that water is ma' musta'mal. [3] Water used to wash off actual impurity becomes impure (najis), not musta'mal. [4] If a person without hadath (already in wudu) performs wudu without intention, that water is not musta'mal; it is valid to use again. Reason: (1) The proof of purity is that the Companions' clothes would get wet from wudu and ghusl, but no one ever washed their clothes because of ma' musta'mal. As for not being purifying, the Arabs had severe need of water yet no one used ma' musta'mal for wudu or ghusl, nor stored it for that purpose. (2) The proof of purity is the hadiths in which the Prophet used his wudu water to give to sick people to drink; if it were impure, he would not have done so. Hadith: Jabir said: 'The Messenger of Allah came to visit me while I was ill and unconscious; he performed wudu and poured some of his wudu water on me, and I regained consciousness.' (Bukhari) (3) I heard Sa'ib ibn Yazid say: My aunt took me to the Prophet and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, my nephew is ill'; he wiped my head, prayed for blessing, then performed wudu and I drank from his wudu water.' (Bukhari)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage addresses the third category of water: ma' musta'mal (used water). It is water that has been used for a valid act of purification (removing hadath) or for a supererogatory act with the intention of worship (like wudu on wudu for reward). The ruling: the water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr mutahhir). This means if it touches a garment, it does not make it impure, but it cannot be used for valid purification (wudu or ghusl) nor can it be used to remove impurity from objects. The author then provides practical applications: (1) water from obligatory wudu, (2) water from supererogatory wudu, and clarifies that (3) water used to wash actual impurity is impure (najis), and (4) water from wudu without intention (no niyyah) by a pure person is not musta'mal because it was not 'used' for worship. The proofs are rational and textual: (i) the constant practice of the Companions (clothes wet but not washed) and the Arabs' avoidance of using such water for purification indicates it is pure but not purifying; (ii) two sahih hadiths from Bukhari show the Prophet giving his wudu water to sick and young companions to drink, proving the water is pure and not harmful. The Hanafi position is that ma' musta'mal is tahir but not mutahhir; it cannot be used for ritual purification but is not impure. This differs from some other schools that consider it pure and purifying, or even impure. The passage emphasizes that the ruling is based on practical necessity and prophetic practice.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a valid act of purification (wudu/ghusl) or supererogatory worship; it is pure but cannot purify.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that requires wudu (hadath asghar) or ghusl (hadath akbar)
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship done to draw closer to Allah, here specifically a supererogatory wudu

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on water used by a person in hadath to perform wudu (ma' musta'mal) according to Hanafis?
A) It is pure and can be used for wudu again
B) It is impure and must be disposed of
C) It is pure but cannot be used for wudu or ghusl
D) It is pure and purifying like fresh water

Key Takeaway
Water used intentionally for ritual purification or supererogatory worship is pure but loses its capacity to purify; it cannot be reused for wudu or ghusl.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Used Water (Musta'mal): Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on when water becomes musta'mal with hadith and athar proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when water becomes musta'mal and explain the hadith evidence that proves it is pure but not purifying.

Core Idea
Water becomes musta'mal immediately upon separation from the limb – tahir but not mutahhir.

Understanding what makes water musta'mal is crucial for valid wudu and ghusl. The Hanafi school holds that water becomes used the moment it leaves the body part being washed. This lesson examines the textual proofs from the Prophet's practice and the Companions' statements, and addresses a differing opinion to solidify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scenarios
Extract the core ruling from the passage: water becomes musta'mal simply by separating from the body. Note the three possible timings (on limb, upon separation, after collection) and which one the author adopts.
The author says 'sahih qawl yahi hai' – the correct opinion is immediate separation.
2
Collect the Hadith Proofs for Pure (tahir)
Find the hadith and athar that show used water is pure. Look at the hadiths cited from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, the story of the Prophet giving used wudu water to drink, and the athar from Ibn Abbas.
The water being given to drink proves it is not impure.
3
Collect the Hadith Proofs for Not Purifying (ghayr mutahhir)
Find the evidence that used water cannot be reused for purification. The key proof is the Prophet taking new water for each limb. Also the prohibition of bathing in standing water while junub, and the athar stating 'the water is purifying but does not purify'.
The Prophet's action is a strong indicator: if the water were still purifying, he would have reused it.
4
Analyze the Dispute with Sufyan al-Thawri
Identify the opposing view: water becomes musta'mal only after collecting in a vessel. Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the need ends upon separation, and the Prophet's practice disproves Thawri's position.
The author dismisses Thawri's view as not sahih.
5
Confirm the Mufta Bihi Position
Conclude that the Hanafi position – immediate separation – is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling. Recognize the linguistic distinction between tahir and mutahhir as key.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and has practical consequences for daily wudu.
