Little vs Large Water: Hanafi Rulings on Impurity
Defines little and large water and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of little and large water, explain why little water becomes impure even without visible change, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Little water (less than 10x10 cubits) becomes impure on contact; large water only if attributes change.

In Hanafi fiqh, the size of a water body determines its purity status upon contact with impurity. This lesson unpacks the key ruling, the proofs from hadith, and the debate with the Shafi'i school. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying rulings on wudu, ghusl, and purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for little water
Read the first sentence: little water is less than 10x10 cubits. It becomes impure (najis) even if the impurity's effect (color, taste, smell) does not appear. State this rule clearly.
The measure is a practical approximation; the actual principle is that impurity does not spread to the other side.
2
Identify the ruling for large water
Large water (10x10 cubits or more) does not become impure unless one of three attributes (color, taste, smell) changes due to the impurity. State this contrast.
This is the key difference: for large water, visible change is required.
3
Locate the primary hadith proof
Find the hadith 'لا يبولن احدكم في الماء الدائم الذي لايجرى ثم يغتسل فيه' (Sahih al-Bukhari 239). How does this proof apply? The prohibition implies that still water becomes impure by urine, and bathing in it would spread impurity.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for establishing the ruling in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the Hanafi argument from the well of Buda'ah
The well of Buda'ah (six cubits wide) had impure objects thrown in, yet the Prophet said it is pure because no change occurred. This shows that for large water, only change matters; for small water, a different rule applies.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i 'water is pure' hadith is that it applies to large water, not small.
5
Note the Shafi'i position and the practical difference
The Shafi'i school holds that any water remains pure until an attribute changes, regardless of quantity. The practical difference: a 6x6 pond is large for Shafi'i but little for Hanafi, so it becomes impure in the Hanafi school.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is essential for real-world application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقليل مادون عشر في عشر فينجس وان لم يظهر اثرها فيه.
ہو، اور جاری بھی نہ ہو، مثلا لوٹے یا مٹکے میں پانی ہو، یا چھوٹے تالاب میں پانی ہو اور اس میں ناپاکی گر جائے تو چاہے ناپاکی کا اثر ، رنگ، بو، مزا پانی میں ظاہر نہ ہوا ہو، پھر بھی پانی ناپاک ہو جائے گا، اور اس سے کسی چیز کو پاک کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ یہ پانی کسی کولنگ جائے تو وہ بھی ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔
وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو پانی جاری نہ ہواور تھوڑا ہو تو اس میں پیشاب نہ کرو، جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ غسل کرنے سے ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ سمع ابو ھریرة انه سمع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول لا يبولن احدكم في الماء الدائم الذي لايجرى ثم يغتسل فيه - ( بخاری شریف ، باب البول في الماء الدائم ص ۱۳۷ نمبر ۲۳۹ مسلم شریف ، باب النھی عن البول في الماء الراكد ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۲ ۶۵۶/۲۸) (۲) غسل کے بارے میں یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمع أبا هريرة يقول قال رسول الله الله لا يغتسل احدكم فى الماء الدائم وهو جنب (مسلم شریف ، باب النھی عن الاغتسال في الماء الراكد، . . ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۶۵۸/۲۸۳) (۳) نیند سے بیدار ہونے کے بعد تین مرتبہ ہاتھ دھونے کا حکم اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان النبي عل الله قال اذا استيقظ احدكم من نومه فلا يغمس يده في الاناء حتى يغسلها ثلاثا فانه لا يدرى اين باتت يده . (مسلم شریف، باب کراھیہ شمس المتوضی و غیره بده المشکوک فی نجاستها فی الانا قبل غسلها ثلاثا ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۶۴۳/۲۷۸ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء اذا استيقظ احدکم من منامه، ص۱۳، نمبر ۲۴) یہ احادیث اور اس قسم کی بہت سی احادیث ہیں جن میں پانی میں نجاست ڈالنے سے منع فرمایا ہے جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تھوڑے پانی میں نجاست گرنے سے وہ ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ ورنہ منع کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہے۔ (۴) اور ماء را کد کے بارے میں یہ حدیث ہے ۔ سـمـع ابـا هريرة يقول : قال
صلى الله
رسول الله له : لا يغسل أحـدكـم فـي الماء الدائم و هو جنب . فقال : كيف يفعل يا أبا هريرة ؟ قال : يتناوله تناولاً - (مسلم شریف ، باب النھی عن الاغتسال في الماء الراكد ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۳ ۲۸/ ۶۵۸) اس حدیث میں بھی ٹھرے ہوئے تھوڑے پانی میں غسل کرنے سے منع اسی لئے کیا کہ اس سے ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے۔
اور بڑا تالاب هو یا ماء جاری ھو تو تھوڑی نجاست سے ناپاک نہیں ہوگا ، جب تک کہ نجاست کی وجہ سے پانی کا رنگ، یا مزا، یا بونہ بدل جائے (۱) اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي امامه الباهلي قال قال رسول الله الله ان الماء لا ينجسه شيء الا ما غلب على ريحه وطعمه ولونه. (ابن ماجه شریف، باب الحیاض، ص ۷۴ ، نمبر ۵۲۱ طحاوی، باب الماء تقع فیہ النجاسۃ ص ۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بڑے تالاب میں جب تک تین وصف میں سے ایک نہ بدلے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی اس کا اشارہ ہے کہ بیر بضاعہ میں ناپاکی کی وجہ سے تینوں میں سے ایک وصف نہیں بدلا تو حدیث میں ناپاک
ہونے کا حکم نہیں لگایا ، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدری قال قبل یا رسول الله انتوضأ من بئر بضاعه و هي بئر يلقى فيها الحيض ولحوم الكلاب والنتن؟ فقال رسول الله الله ان الماء طهور لا ينجسه شيء۔(ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء ان الماء لا ینجسه شی ص ۲۱ نمبر ۶۶ را بود او د شریف ، باب ماجاء فی بئر بضاعته ص ا نمبر ۶۶ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نا پاک چیز گرنے سے جب تک مزا، بو یا رنگ نہ بدل جائے پانی ناپاک نہیں ہوگا۔(۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حوض بڑا ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس سے کوئی حرام جانور بھی پانی پی لے تو نا پاک نہیں ہوگا ۔ ان عمر بن الخطاب خرج في ركب فيهم عمر و
بن العاص حتى وردوا حوضا فقال عمر و بن العاص لصاحب الحوض هل ترد حوضک السباع ؟ فقال عمر بن الخطاب : ياصاحب الحوض لا تخبرنا فانا نرد على السباع و ترد علينا (سن للبیھقی ، باب سورسائر الحيوا ناتسوی الکلب والخنزیر ، ج اول ص ۱۳۷۹ نمبر ۱۱۸۱) اس قول صحابی کے اشارے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بڑا حوض ناپاک نہیں ہوتا ۔(۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بڑا تالاب ہو تو نا پاکی گرنے سے ناپاک نہیں ہوتا۔ عن ابی سعيد الخدري ان النبي الله توضأ او شرب من غدير كان يلقى فيه لحوم الكلاب ، قال و لا أعلمه الا قال : و الجيف فذكر ذالک له فقال له ان الماء لا ينجسه شيء - (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الماء لا ينجسه شي ، وما جاء فی ذالک ، ج اول ص ۶۱ نمبر ۲۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بڑے تالاب سے وضو فر مایا اور پانی پیا، جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ ناپاک نہیں ہوتا۔ لغت : حلت : حلول سے مشتق ہے، داخل ہونا ، خلط ملط ہونا۔ راکدا بہہرا ہوا۔ اثر ھا: نجاست کا اثر ، سے مراد یہ ہے کہ نجاست کی وجہ سے پانی کا رنگ، یا مزا، یا بو بدل جائے۔
و القليل مادون عشر في عشر
دس ہاتھ لمبا ہو اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا حوض ہو تو ماء کثیر ہے، اور اس سے کم ہو تو اس کو ما قلیل کہتے ہیں۔
وجه (۱) اصل بنیاد یہ ہے کہ ماء کثیر، یا بڑا تالاب اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ اتنا بڑا تالاب ہو کہ اس کی ایک جانب نجاست گری ہو اور آدمی تالاب کی دوسری جانب وضو یا غسل کرے تو اس کی حرکت سے نجاست کا اثر آدمی تک نہ پہنچ پاتا ہو تو اس کو بڑا تالاب کہتے ہیں، اور اسی کو ماء کثیر کہتے ہیں، کیونکہ تالاب کے لمبے چوڑے ہونے کی وجہ سے نجاست کا اثر آدمی تک نہیں پہنچا، تو جس جانب نجاست گری ہے اس جانب ناپاک ہے اور آدمی کی جانب پاک ہے۔ وہاں وضو غسل کرنا جائز ہے۔ اب فقہاء نے دیکھا کہ دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا تالاب ہو تو دوسری جانب نجاست کا اثر نہیں پہنچتا ہے، اس لئے عوام پر سہولت کے لئے وہ دردہ کا قول اختیار کر لیا، ورنہ اصل غد ر عظیم ہے۔ (۲) اس اثر میں اسکا اشارہ ملتا ہے۔ قال ابو داود : و قدرت انا بئر بضاعة بردائي مددته عليها
ثم ذرعته فاذا عرضها ستة أذرع (ابوداود شریف، باب ما جاء في بئر بضانہ جس نمبر 1) اس اثر میں امام ابو داود نے ، ۱۱
Little water is what is less than ten by ten cubits; it becomes impure even if no effect (of impurity) appears in it. And if it is not flowing, e.g., water in a pitcher or pot, or a small pond, and impurity falls into it, even if the effect (color, smell, taste) does not appear, the water becomes impure, and it is not permissible to purify anything with it; rather, if this water touches something, that also becomes impure. Proof: (1) There is a hadith: do not urinate in still water that does not flow, then bathe in it – meaning it becomes impure by bathing. (2) Another hadith: do not bathe in still water while in a state of major impurity. (3) The command to wash hands three times after waking up. These hadiths indicate that little water becomes impure by impurity, otherwise prohibition would be meaningless. (4) Another hadith about still water. And a large pond or flowing water does not become impure by a small amount of impurity unless the color, taste, or smell changes. (1) Hadith: Water is not made impure by anything except what overpowers its smell, taste, and color. (2) Hadith of the well of Buda'ah: water is pure and not made impure. (3) Effect of Umar: a large pond does not become impure even if predatory animals drink from it. (4) Hadith: the Prophet performed wudu and drank from a large pond where dog meat was thrown. Lexicon: hulla: derived from hulul, meaning entering, mixing. rakidan: stagnant. atharuha: effect of impurity, meaning change in color, taste, or smell due to impurity. And little water is what is less than ten by ten cubits. Explanation: A pond ten cubits long and ten cubits wide is large water; less than that is little water. The basic principle is that large water is such that if impurity falls on one side and a person performs wudu on the other side, the effect of impurity does not reach him due to the size. So the side with impurity is impure, the person's side is pure. Jurists adopted the measure of ten by ten cubits for convenience, though the actual measure is larger. Evidence: Abu Dawud measured the well of Buda'ah with his garment and found its width six cubits.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) on the classification of water in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by stating the ruling for little water (ma' qalil): any water less than 10 cubits by 10 cubits (approximately 5.6 meters square) becomes impure (najis) upon contact with impurity, even if no change in color, taste, or smell is apparent. The author then provides several hadith proofs, including the prohibition of urinating in still water and the command to wash hands after waking, implying that water in a vessel is easily contaminated. For large water (ma' kathir), defined as a pond of 10x10 cubits or larger, the water does not become impure unless one of its three attributes (color, taste, smell) changes due to the impurity. Proofs include the hadith of Abu Umamah that water is only impure by change in these attributes, the hadith of the well of Buda'ah where impure things were thrown yet the water remained pure, the effect of Umar allowing wild animals to drink from large ponds, and the hadith of the Prophet using water from a pond where dog meat was thrown. The author explains that the 10x10 measure is a practical convention for the public, while the actual criterion is that the impurity's effect does not spread to the other side of the pond. The passage also defines key terms like 'hulla' (entering/mixing), 'rakidan' (stagnant), and 'atharuha' (effect of impurity).

Key Terms
ماء قليل (ma' qalil): Water less than 10x10 cubits in area (approximately 5.6m x 5.6m). It becomes impure by contact with any impurity even without visible change.
ماء كثير (ma' kathir): Water at least 10x10 cubits in area. It does not become impure unless one of three attributes (color, taste, smell) changes due to impurity.
اثر (athar): Effect of impurity, specifically change in color, taste, or smell of the water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the definition of little water (ma' qalil) in the Hanafi school?
A) Any water that is not flowing.
B) Water less than 10 cubits by 10 cubits in area.
C) Water that changes color, taste, or smell upon impurity.
D) Water that is stored in a container.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the size of a body of water determines how impurity affects it: little water becomes impure on contact, large water only when attributes change.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Definition of Abundant Water (Ma' Kathir) in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines ma' kathir as ten cubits square with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of abundant water (ma' kathir) and apply the ruling that it remains pure unless an impurity changes its color, taste, or smell.

Core Idea
A basin of ten by ten cubits or larger is abundant water — it stays pure unless impurity changes its properties.

In Hanafi Taharah, the category of water determines the effect of impurity. Abundant water (ma' kathir) enjoys a strong presumption of purity, while little water (ma' qalil) becomes impure upon contact with any impurity. This lesson examines the specific definition of ma' kathir adopted by the Hanafi school and the evidential basis from the Prophet's tradition and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
First, determine the legal status of abundant water: it is pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahir) as long as its color, taste, or smell remain unchanged. The key condition is the size: a basin of ten cubits long by ten cubits wide (or greater) qualifies as abundant.
2
Examine the primary dalil: Hadith of the Well of Buda'ah
The Prophet said, 'Water is purifying and nothing makes it impure.' This hadith indicates that water is intrinsically pure; impurity does not render it impure unless it changes one of its properties. The Hanafi school relies on this to deduce that a large body of water (like the well of Buda'ah, which was six cubits wide) remains pure despite impurities falling into it.
The hadith is from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, recorded in Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyse the secondary evidence: Athar of Umar
Umar ibn al-Khattab indicated that a large reservoir frequented by wild beasts remains pure. This supports the idea that size matters: a reservoir that is large enough for both humans and animals to use without concern is not impurified by the beasts' presence.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
4
Understand the juristic rationale (wajh) and the adopted measure
The jurists observed that in a basin of ten by ten cubits, impurity on one side does not affect the other side due to the movement of a person on the opposite side. This practical measure (tashil) was chosen for convenience. The original principle is the 'large pond' (ghadir) effect, but the specific measurement simplifies application for the general public.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ا ۴۹ دهدر ده بئر بضاعہ کونا پا تو وہ چھ ہاتھ تھا اور اسکے بارے میں حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ نجاست گرنے سے ناپاک نہیں ہوتا۔ اس سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے حنفیہ نے مزید احتیاط فرمایا اور دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا کا مسلک اختیار کیا۔
ده درده، انچ فٹ ، اور میٹر کے حساب سے کچھ دہ دردہ ، فٹ کے حساب سے کچھ ایک ہاتھ ڈیڑھ فٹ کا ہوتا ہے، یعنی اٹھارہ (18) انچ کا ہوتا ہے، اس اعتبار سے دس ہا تھ لمبا پندرہ فٹ لمبا ہوا اور وہی پندرہ فٹ چوڑا ہوا۔ اور پندرہ کو پندرہ میں ضرب دیں تو دوسو پچھیں (225) مربع فٹ بڑا تالاب ہوا۔ نوٹ :۔ لمبائی اور چوڑائی کو ضرب دینے سے مربع نکلتا ہے۔ دہ دردہ ، گز کے حساب سے ) ایک ہاتھ آدھے گز کا ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے دس ہاتھ پانچ گز کا ہوا۔ اسلئے پانچ گز لمبا اور پانچ گز چوڑا بڑا تالاب ہوا۔ جسکا مربع (25) گز ہوگا۔ وہ دردہ، میٹر کے حساب سے کا ایک ہاتھ 0.4572 میٹر کا ہوتا ہے اسلئے دس ہاتھ 4.572 میٹر لمبا ہوا ۔ اور وہی 4.572 میٹر چوڑا ہوا اور مجموعہ 20.903 مربع میٹر ہوا۔ گول کنواں کا قطر اور اگر کوئی حوض ، یا کنواں گول ہو تو اسکے بیچ کا قطر 16.925 فٹ ہونا چاہئے۔ اور میٹر کے اعتبار سے 5.158 میٹر قطر ہونا چاہئے۔
Book of Purification. It is not ruled that... The hadith is: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: O Messenger of Allah, shall we perform wudu from the well of Buda'ah? It is a well into which menstrual cloths, dog meat, and putrid things are thrown. The Messenger of Allah said: Water is purifying and nothing makes it impure. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a anna al-mah? etc.) From this hadith it is understood that when a dirty thing falls into water, as long as the taste, smell, or color does not change, the water does not become impure. (3) In this athar it is that the reservoir is large, so even if a non-permissible animal drinks from it, the water is not impure: Umar ibn al-Khattab went out with a group including Amr ibn al-'As until they came to a reservoir. Amr asked its owner: 'Do wild beasts frequent your reservoir?' Umar said: 'O owner of the reservoir, do not tell us; we frequent the wild beasts and they frequent us.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ?) The indication of this saying of the Companion is that a large reservoir does not become impure. (4) In this hadith it is that if there is a large pond, it does not become impure from the fall of impurity: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet performed wudu or drank from a ghadir (pond) into which dog meat was thrown, and he said, and I think he said: and carcasses, so it was mentioned to him, and he said: Water is not made impure by anything. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-ma' la yunajjisuhu shay') The hadith indicates that he performed wudu from a large pond and drank water, meaning it is not impure. Lexicon: 'halla' derived from 'hulul' meaning to enter, to mix. 'Rakidan' stagnant. 'Atharuha: the effect of impurity' meaning that due to impurity the color, taste, or smell changes. And the small [water] is that which is less than ten by ten. A reservoir that is ten cubits long and ten cubits wide is abundant water (ma' kathir), and less than that is called little water (ma' qalil). Rationale: (1) The basic principle is that abundant water or a large pond is that, such that if impurity falls on one side and a person performs wudu or ghusl on the other side, the effect of the impurity does not reach the person due to his movement. That is called a large pond, and it is called abundant water. Because due to the length and breadth of the pond, the effect of the impurity does not reach the person. So the side where the impurity fell is impure, and the person's side is pure. It is permissible to perform wudu and ghusl there. The jurists observed that if a pond is ten cubits long and ten cubits wide, the effect of impurity does not reach the other side. Therefore, for ease of the general public, they adopted the view of ten by ten; otherwise, the original is a large ghadir. (2) There is an indication in this athar: Abu Dawud said: I myself measured the well of Buda'ah by spreading my garment over it, then I measured it, and its width was six cubits. (Abu Dawud, Bab ma ja'a fi bi'r Buda'ah) In this athar, Imam Abu Dawud states that the well of Buda'ah was six cubits [wide], and regarding it the Prophet said that it does not become impure from falling impurity. Using this as evidence, the Hanafis took further caution and adopted the view of ten cubits long and ten cubits wide. Some measurements in inches, feet, and meters: One cubit is one and a half feet, i.e., 18 inches. Accordingly, ten cubits long is 15 feet long, and the same 15 feet wide. Multiplying 15 by 15 gives 225 square feet for a large pond. Note: length times width gives area. In yards: one cubit is half a yard, so ten cubits is five yards. So five yards long and five yards wide, area 25 square yards. In meters: one cubit is 0.4572 meters, so ten cubits is 4.572 meters, area 20.903 square meters. The diameter of a circular well: if the reservoir or well is round, its diameter should be 16.925 feet, or in meters 5.158 meters.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah defines the Hanafi concept of abundant water (ma' kathir) and its ruling. The text begins by referencing key hadith evidence: the well of Buda'ah, about which the Prophet Muhammad said 'Water is purifying and nothing makes it impure.' This hadith establishes that water remains pure even when impurities fall into it, as long as its taste, smell, or color do not change. The author then cites an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab, who indicated that a large reservoir frequented by wild animals remains pure. Another hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reports that the Prophet performed wudu from a pond containing dog meat, confirming the same principle. The author explains the lexicon of terms like 'halla' (to enter/mix) and 'rakidan' (stagnant). The central ruling is that water is classified as abundant (ma' kathir) if it forms a basin ten cubits long by ten cubits wide. Anything smaller is little water (ma' qalil). The underlying rationale (wajh) is that a basin of this size ensures that impurity falling on one side does not reach a person on the opposite side due to movement; thus the person's side remains pure. The jurists adopted this standard for ease, though the original principle was that a 'large pond' (ghadir) was defined by this effect. The author then provides practical conversions: 1 cubit = 1.5 feet (18 inches), so ten cubits = 15 feet, area 225 square feet; in yards, 5 yards square, area 25 sq yds; in meters, 4.572 m square, area 20.903 sq m. For a circular well, the diameter should be about 16.925 feet (5.158 m) to have equivalent area.

Key Terms
ماء كثير (ma' kathir): Abundant water: a basin ten cubits long by ten cubits wide or larger, which does not become impure unless a najasah changes its color, taste, or smell.
ماء قليل (ma' qalil): Little water: a basin smaller than ten cubits square; any impurity that falls into it renders all the water impure.
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit: a unit of length, approximately 1.5 feet (18 inches, 0.4572 meters) in the Hanafi measurement used here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum size for a basin to be considered abundant water (ma' kathir)?
A) 6 cubits long by 6 cubits wide
B) 10 cubits long by 10 cubits wide
C) 15 feet long by 15 feet wide
D) 5 meters in diameter

Key Takeaway
Abundant water (ma' kathir) is a basin of ten cubits by ten cubits or larger; it remains pure unless an impurity changes its color, taste, or smell.

The Hanafi Definition of a Large Pool (Bada Talab)
Ruling with proof and measurement conversions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a large pool, cite the hadith evidence, and calculate its dimensions in various units.

Core Idea
A pool of 10×10 cubits (100 square cubits) is considered large and unaffected by falling impurities.

The Hanafi school derives the definition of a large pool from the well-known hadith of Bi'r Buda'ah, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that a well of that size does not become impure by falling impurities. While the hadith mentions a depth (or diameter) of six cubits, the Hanafis, out of caution, set the minimum dimensions of a large pool at ten cubits by ten cubits. This lesson will walk you through the proof, the ruling, and the practical calculations needed to apply this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary proof (dalil)
Locate the hadith of Bi'r Buda'ah in the passage. Note that the Prophet stated a well of six cubits does not become impure from falling impurities. This is the textual basis for defining a large water body.
The hadith is classified as ahad (single-narrator) and is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
2
Recognize the Hanafi extension (istidlal)
Understand that the Hanafi school exercised additional caution (ihtiyat) by requiring a larger area than the hadith's six cubits. They set the minimum for a large pool at 10 cubits × 10 cubits (100 square cubits).
This position is from the fatawa mutakhkhirin and is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.
3
Understand dah dar dah (10×10)
The term 'dah dar dah' literally means 'ten by ten' and is the standard way to refer to a square pool of 10 cubits per side.
This term is used throughout the passage as a shorthand.
4
Perform unit conversions
Convert the 10-cubit side into feet (15 ft), yards (5 yd), and meters (4.572 m). Then compute the area: 225 sq ft, 25 sq yd, 20.903 sq m. For circular pools, derive the diameter that gives equivalent area.
One cubit (haath) = 1.5 feet = 18 inches = 45.72 cm.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Given the dimensions of any pool or water tank, determine if it meets the 'dah dar dah' standard. If it is circular, check if the diameter is at least 16.925 ft (5.158 m).
This has direct application in taharah rulings for large water bodies.

The well of Buda'ah was six cubits, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said about it that it does not become impure by falling impurity. Using this as evidence, the Hanafis exercised further caution and adopted the position that a large pool is ten cubits long and ten cubits wide. As for the calculation in inches, feet, and meters: some calculations in feet: One cubit is one and a half feet, i.e., eighteen inches. Accordingly, ten cubits long becomes fifteen feet long, and the same fifteen feet wide. Multiplying fifteen by fifteen gives two hundred twenty-five (225) square feet for the large pool. Note: Multiplying length and width gives area. Some calculations in yards: One cubit is half a yard. Therefore ten cubits becomes five yards. So a large pool is five yards long and five yards wide, with an area of twenty-five (25) square yards. Some calculations in meters: One cubit is 0.4572 meters. Therefore ten cubits is 4.572 meters long, and the same 4.572 meters wide, totaling 20.903 square meters. The diameter of a circular well: If a pool or well is circular, its diameter should be 16.925 feet. And in meters, the diameter should be 5.158 meters. [Page 51] What is a dah dar dah and how much is it? The calculation of a large pool at a glance: What is it and how much is it? One inch is 2.54 centimeters. One qabzah is 7.62 centimeters. One meter is 39.37 inches. One common cubit is 18 inches. One qabzah is four fingers. One finger is considered 0.75 inches. One common cubit is 1.50 (one and a half) feet. One common cubit is 45.72 centimeters. One foot is 12 inches. One yard is 36 inches. One qabzah is 3 inches. What is a dah dar dah? How large is a pool that is a dah dar dah? Length times width equals square feet or yards. Large pool: length: 10 cubits, 15 feet, 5 yards, 4.572 meters. Times: 10 cubits, 15 feet, 5 yards, 4.572 meters. Equals: 100 square cubits, 225 square feet, 25 square yards, 20.903 square meters. How much will be the diameter of a circular pool or circular well? How many feet or yards will be the diameter of a circular pool? The diameter of a circular pool will be 16.925 feet, then it will be a dah dar dah. The diameter of a circular pool will be 5.1589 meters, then it will be a dah dar dah.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory expansion (sharh) of the Hanafi ruling on the minimum size of a large pool (bada talab) that is not rendered impure by the falling of impurities. The author begins by citing the hadith of Bi'r Buda'ah, a well of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that was six cubits deep or in diameter, and the Prophet stated that falling impurities do not make it impure. Taking this as evidence, the Hanafi school (al-Hanafiyyah) exercised additional caution and set the standard for a large pool at ten cubits in length and ten cubits in width (i.e., 100 square cubits). This is more than the six cubits of the hadith. The passage then provides conversions for students to understand the dimension in various units: in feet (15 ft × 15 ft = 225 sq ft), in yards (5 yd × 5 yd = 25 sq yd), and in meters (4.572 m × 4.572 m = 20.903 m²). It also addresses circular pools or wells: to achieve the equivalent area, the diameter must be 16.925 feet or 5.158 meters. The author lists standard conversion ratios for Islamic measurements (cubit, qabzah, finger) to modern units. The legal ruling is that a pool of this size is considered large (kahay'ah al-kabirah) such that falling impurities do not affect the water's purity. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
بئر بضاعہ (Bi'r Buda'ah): A well in Madinah associated with the Prophet (peace be upon him) used as a basis for the size of a large water body.
ہاتھ (haath): A unit of length equal to 18 inches (1.5 feet) in this text.
دردہ (dah dar dah): Literal 'ten by ten'; refers to a pool of 10×10 cubits.
قبضہ (qabzah): A handbreadth, equal to 3 inches (or four fingers) as used in this text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A large pool (bada talab) in Hanafi fiqh is defined as 10 cubits × 10 cubits (100 square cubits), based on cautious extension from the hadith of Bi'r Buda'ah.

Measuring the Large Pond: Area and Diameter
Defining the size of a large pond and formulas for circular objects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum size of a large pond (حوض کبیر) in square cubits and calculate the equivalent diameter for a circular pond using the Hanafi standard.

Core Idea
A large pond must have at least 100 square cubits of surface area.

In Hanafi taharah, the size of a water reservoir determines whether it remains pure when impurity falls in. This lesson teaches you the precise measurements for a large pond (حوض کبیر) as defined by the classical jurists. You will learn both the square dimensions and how to apply them to a circular pond using basic geometry, ensuring you can identify a large pond in any shape.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of a large pond
The text defines a large pond (حوض کبیر) as having a surface area of 10 cubits by 10 cubits. This is the minimum threshold for the water to be considered large in taharah rulings.
Memorize: 10 cubits × 10 cubits = 100 square cubits.
2
Convert units to familiar measures
The passage provides conversions: 1 cubit (ہاتھ) ≈ 1.5 feet, so 10 cubits = 15 feet. Thus, a square pond of 15 ft × 15 ft (225 sq ft) is a large pond. Similar conversions for yards and meters are given.
Focus on the equivalence in feet and yards, as these are commonly used.
3
Determine the area for a square pond
For a square or rectangular pond, multiply length by width. The resulting area must equal or exceed 100 square cubits (or 225 sq ft, etc.).
4
Compute the diameter for a circular pond
For a circular pond, the text gives the diameter required to achieve the same area: approximately 16.925 feet (or 5.1589 meters). This is derived using the formula for the area of a circle (πr²) set equal to 225 sq ft.
The formula: Diameter = 2 × √(Area/π). For 225 sq ft, diameter ≈ 16.925 ft.
5
Apply the ruling to your context
If you encounter a pond, measure its surface area. If it is at least 100 square cubits (or equivalent), it is a large pond; otherwise, it is small. For circular ponds, compare the diameter to 16.925 ft.
This ruling applies to standing water, not flowing water.

گول چیز ناپنے کا فارمولہ
گول چیز ناپنے کے لئے چار الفاظ کی تشریح یاد رکھنا ضروری ہے۔ (۱) قطر (۲) پائی (۳) گول کروی کا رقبہ (۴) گول درھمی کا رقبہ۔
(۱) قطر: گول چیز کے درمیان کی لمبائی کو قطر کہتے ہیں اس گول کے بیچ میں جو نکیر ہے یہ قطر ہے : (۲) پائی کسی گول چیز کو ناپنے کے لئے پائی کی عدد کو ضرور استعمال کیا جاتا ہے - 22 بے 7 کو پائی کہتے ہیں کیلکولیٹر سے اسکا حساب 3.14285 ہوتا ہے، لیکن انگریزی کتاب میں اسکا حساب 3.1416 دیا ہوا ہے اسلئے کلکیولیٹر سے پائی کا حساب اسی سے ہوگا۔
(۳) گول کروی کا رقبہ؛ - گیند جیسی چیز جو بالکل گول مول ہو اسکو گول کروی کہتے ہیں، جو کرأۃ سے مشتق ہے۔ گول کروی میں دو قطر ہوتے ہیں، ایک دائیں سے بائیں کی جانب، اور دوسرا اوپر سے نیچے کی جانب، اسلئے گول کروی کے اوپر کا پورا رقبہ نکالنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ایک قطر کو دوسرے قطر سے ضرب دیں، جو حاصل ضرب ہوگا اسکو پائی سے ضرب دیں تو گول کروی کے اوپر کا پورا رقبہ نکل جائے گا۔ مثلا ایک گیند کا قطر 7 انچ ہے، اور گیند مکمل گول ہے اسلئے دونوں قطر سات سات انچ کے ہونگے، اسلئے ایک قطر7 کو 7 میں ضرب دیں حاصل ضرب 49 مربع انچ ہوئے، اسکو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دیں تو حاصل ضرب 153.938 مربع انچ پورے گیند کا رقبہ ہوا۔ اور اگر گیند کو کاٹ کر اسکی کٹی ہوئی جانب کے رقبے کو معلوم کرنا ہو تو گیند کے پورے رقبے کو 4 سے تقسیم دے دیں تو گیند کی ایک جانب کا رقبہ معلوم ہو جائے گا۔ مثال مذکور میں پورے گیند کا رقبہ 153.938 مربع انچ تھا اسکو 4 سے تقسیم کیا تو حاصل تقسیم 38.4845 مربع انچ ہوا یہ گیند کی ایک جانب کا رقبہ ہے اور گیند کی گولائی ناپنا ہو تو گیند کے قطر کو پائی سے ضرب دے دیں، حاصل ضرب گیند کی گولائی ہوگی ۔ مثال مذکور میں گیند کا قطر 7 انچ تھا تو 7 کو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دیں تو حاصل ضرب 21.9912 مربع انچ ہوگا، یہ گیند کی گولائی ہوئی ۔ نوٹ : یہ حساب سمت قبلہ ناپنے میں کام آئے گا۔
(٤) گول درھمی کا رقبہ : ۔ یہ درھم سے مشتق ہے اسلئے اسکو گول درھمی کہتے ہیں ۔ درھم چاروں طرف سے گول نہیں ہوتا صرف اوپر سے گول ہوتا ہے۔ اسکی گولائی کو ناپنے کے لئے بھی اوپر کا ہی فارمولہ استعمال کرنا پڑتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر اسکی گولائی ناپنا ہو تو اسکے قطر کو پائی سے ضرب دے دیں تو اوپر کی گولائی نکل آئے گی ۔ مثلا درھم کا قطر 2.75 سینٹی میٹر ہوتا ہے اسلئے اسکو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دے دیں حاصل ضرب 8.6394 مربع سینٹی میٹر ہوگا، یہ درھم کی اوپر کی گولائی ہوگی۔
Thamrat al-Najah Volume 1. Ten by ten. What is it? How much is it? Calculation of a large pond at a glance. What is it? How much is it? One inch is 2.54 centimeters. One qabda is 7.62 centimeters. One meter is 39.37 inches. One common hand is 18 inches. One qabda is 4 fingers. One finger is considered 0.75 inches. One common hand is 1.50 feet. One common hand is 45.72 centimeters. One foot is 12 inches. One yard is 36 inches. One qabda is 3 inches. That darda, how big is the pond that? Length times width equals square feet or yards. Large pond length: large pond 10 hands, large pond 15 feet, large pond 5 yards, large pond 4.572 meters. X 10 hands, 15 feet, 5 yards, 4.572 meters = 100 square hands, 225 square feet, 25 square yards, 20.903 square meters. For a round pond or round well, what will be the diameter? Diameter of round pond in feet or yards. Diameter of round pond will be 16.925 feet then it will become darda, diameter of round pond will be 5.1589 meters then it will become darda. Thamrat al-Najah Volume 1 page 51. Ten by ten. Formula for measuring round objects. For measuring round objects, it is necessary to remember the explanation of four words. (1) Diameter (2) Pi (3) Area of a sphere (4) Area of a disc. (1) Diameter: The length through the middle of a round object is called diameter; the peg in the middle of this round thing is the diameter. (2) Pi: To measure any round object, the number pi must be used. 22/7 is called pi. Its calculation on a calculator is 3.14285, but in English books its calculation is given as 3.1416, so the calculation of pi on a calculator will be from that. (3) Area of a sphere: An object like a ball that is completely round is called a sphere (gol karvi), derived from kura. A sphere has two diameters, one from right to left and the other from top to bottom. So the method to find the entire surface area of a sphere is to multiply one diameter by the other diameter, then multiply the product by pi, then the entire surface area of the sphere will be obtained. For example, a ball's diameter is 7 inches, and since the ball is completely round, both diameters are 7 inches each. So multiply one diameter 7 by 7, product 49 square inches. Multiply that by pi 3.1416, product 153.938 square inches, the surface area of the whole ball. And if the ball is cut and we want to find the area of the cut side, divide the whole surface area of the ball by 4, then the area of one side of the ball will be found. In the mentioned example, the whole ball's area was 153.938 square inches, divided by 4 gave 38.4845 square inches, this is the area of one side of the ball. And to measure the circumference of the ball, multiply the diameter by pi, the product will be the circumference. In the example, the ball's diameter was 7 inches, multiply 7 by pi 3.1416, product 21.9912 square inches, this is the circumference of the ball. Note: This calculation will be useful in measuring the direction of Qibla. (4) Area of a disc: This is derived from dirham, so it is called a disc. A dirham is not round on all sides, only round on top. To measure its circumference, the same formula as above is used. If you want to measure its circumference, multiply its diameter by pi, then the top circumference will be obtained. For example, a dirham's diameter is 2.75 centimeters, so multiply it by pi 3.1416, product 8.6394 square centimeters, this will be the top circumference of the dirham.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage provides practical measurements for determining the size of a large pond (حوض کبیر) in Hanafi fiqh. In taharah, a large pond is defined as one that measures approximately 10 cubits by 10 cubits (i.e., 100 square cubits). The text first converts various units (inches, feet, yards, meters) to cubits (ہاتھ) and then gives the equivalent area for a square pond. For a circular pond, it provides the diameter that yields the same area, approximately 16.925 feet or 5.1589 meters. This is crucial because water in a pond of this size or larger does not become impure when an impurity falls into it unless it changes one of its three qualities (color, taste, smell). The second part of the passage explains formulas for measuring circular objects—specifically, how to calculate the surface area and circumference of a sphere and a disc (like a dirham). These calculations are applied to the round pond and are noted to be useful in determining the direction of Qibla, likely for constructing a water feature aligned with the Qibla. The author follows a systematic approach: first defining terms (diameter, pi, sphere, disc), then giving step-by-step examples with numbers. The inclusion of both square and round pond measurements shows that the Hanafi ruling applies to any shape as long as the surface area meets the minimum.

Key Terms
حوض (hawd): A pool or basin of water, here specifically the large pond used for purification rulings.
دردہ (darda): A term for a pond that is ten cubits by ten cubits (or equivalent area), i.e., a large pond.
قطر (qutr): The diameter of a circle or sphere; the straight line passing through the center.
پائی (pai): The mathematical constant pi (π), approximately 22/7 or 3.1416.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum diameter (in feet) for a round pond to be considered a large pond (دردہ)?
A) 10 feet
B) 16.925 feet
C) 15 feet
D) 5.1589 feet

Key Takeaway
A large pond (حوض کبیر) is defined by a minimum surface area of 100 square cubits, regardless of shape, with a circular pond requiring a diameter of approximately 16.925 feet.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Measurement of Round Objects and the Ruling on Water Purity
Defines key terms, provides geometric formulas, and states the ruling on water purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the equivalent round diameter for a ten-by-ten cubit cistern and state the condition under which water remains pure despite falling impurity.

Core Idea
Water is pure unless its taste, color, or smell changes — even if impurity falls, if it flows or is large enough.

This lesson bridges practical geometry with a core Hanafi ruling on water purity. You'll learn how to measure round objects like wells and dirhams using pi and diameter, and apply these calculations to determine whether a body of water is large enough (like a 10x10 cubit cistern) to remain pure despite contact with impurity. The key fiqh principle: impurity only renders water impure if one of its three attributes (taste, color, smell) changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Learn the four terms: qutr (diameter), pai (pi), area of sphere, area of round dirham. These are foundational for the geometric calculations.
The term 'athar' (effect) refers to change in taste, color, or smell.
2
Calculate the area of a sphere
Apply the formula: diameter × diameter × pi = total surface area. This is used in determining the size of round bodies and has applications in Qibla direction measurement.
For a sphere, two diameters (horizontal and vertical) are equal if it is perfectly spherical.
3
Calculate the area of a dirham's back/belly
Use the formula: (diameter × diameter × pi) / 4. This measurement is used for determining the spread of thick impurity (najasat ghalizah) on surfaces.
The dirham's flat back and belly area is calculated to see if impurity covers an area equal to or greater than that.
4
Convert square cistern to round well
Given a square cistern of 10x10 cubits, find the equivalent round diameter using: diameter = sqrt( (length × width × 4) / pi ). This helps in applying the purity ruling to round wells.
One cubit = 1.5 feet = 45.72 cm. Calculate in feet or meters accordingly.
5
Apply the purity ruling
Understand that if water is flowing or meets the size threshold (≥ 10x10 cubits or equivalent round), it remains pure unless one of the three attributes (taste, color, smell) changes due to the impurity.
If no change occurs, the water is considered pure and can be used for wudu.

گول چیز ناپنے کا فارمولہ
گول چیز ناپنے کے لئے چار الفاظ کی تشریح یا د رکھنا ضروری ہے۔ (۱) قطر (۲) پائی (۳) گول کروی کا رقبہ (۴) گول در ھمی کا رقبہ۔
(۱) قطر: مول چیز کے درمیان کی لمبائی کو قطر کہتے ہیں اس گول کے بیچ میں جونکیر ہے یہ قطر ہے : (۲) پائی کسی گول چیز کو ناپنے کے لئے پائی کی عدد کو ضرور استعمال کیا جاتا ھے - 22 بے 7 کو پائی کہتے ہیں کالکیولیٹر سے اسکا حساب 3.14285 ہوتا ہے، لیکن انگریزی کتاب میں اسکا حساب 3.1416 دیا ہوا ہے اسلئے کلکیولیٹر سے پائی کا حساب اسی سے ہوگا۔
(۳) گول کروی کا رقبه؛ - گیند جیسی چیز جو بالکل گول مول ہو اسکو گول کر دی، کہتے ہیں، جو، کرأۃ، سے مشتق ہے۔ گول کروی میں دو قطر ہوتے ہیں، ایک دائیں سے بائیں کی جانب، اور دوسرا اوپر سے نیچے کی جانب،اسلئے گول کر وی کے اوپر کا پورا رقبہ نکالنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ایک قطر کو دوسرے قطر سے ضرب دیں، جو حاصل ضرب ہوگا اسکو پائی سے ضرب دیں تو گول کروی کے اوپر کا پورا رقبہ نکل جائے گا۔ مثلا ایک گیند کا قطر 7 انچ ہے، اور گیند مکمل گول ہے اسلئے دونوں قطر سات سات انچ کے ہونگے، اسلئے ایک قطر7 کو 7 میں ضرب دیں حاصل ضرب 49 مربع انچ ہوئے، اسکو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دیں تو حاصل ضرب 153.938 مربع انچ پورے گند کا رقبہ ہوا۔ اور اگر گیند کو کاٹ کر اسکی کٹی ہوئی جانب کے رقبے کو معلوم کرنا ہو تو گیند کے پورے رقبے کو 4 سے تقسیم دے دیں تو گیند کی ایک جانب کا رقبہ معلوم ہو جائے گا۔ مثال مذکور میں پورے گیند کا رقبہ 153.938 مربع انچ تھا اسکو 4 سے تقسیم کیا تو حاصل تقسیم 38.4845 مربع انچ ہوا یہ گیند کی ایک جانب کا رقبہ ہے اور گیند کی گولائی نا پنا ہو تو گیند کے قطر کو پائی سے ضرب دے دیں، حاصل ضرب گیند کی گولائی ہوگی۔ مثال مذکور میں گیند کا قطر 7 انچ تھا تو 7 کو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دیں تو حاصل ضرب 21.9912 مربع انچ ہوگا، یہ گیند کی گولائی ہوئی۔ نوٹ: یہ حساب سمت قبلہ ناپنے میں کام آئے گا۔
(٤) گول در همی کا رقبه: ۔ یہ درھم سے مشتق ہے اسلئے اسکو گول در ھمی کہتے ہیں۔ درھم چاروں طرف سے گول نہیں ہوتا صرف اوپر سے گول ہوتا ہے۔ اسکی گولائی کو ناپنے کے لئے بھی اوپر کا ہی فارمولہ استعمال کرنا پڑتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر اسکی گولائی ناپنا ہوتو اسکے قطر کو پائی سے ضرب دے دیں تو اوپر کی گولائی نکل آئے گی۔ مثلا درھم کا قطر 2.75 سینٹی میٹر ہوتا ہے اسلئے اسکو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دے دیں حاصل ضرب 8.6394 مربع سینٹی میٹر ہوگا، یہ درھم کی اوپر کی گولائی ہوگی۔
(۱۴) او جاريا وظهر فيه اثرها (۱۵) والاثر طعم او لون او ريح.
اور اگر درھم کی پیٹھ، یا پیٹ کا رقبہ ناپنا ہوتو درھم کے قطر کو قطر سے ضرب دیں، جو حاصل ضرب ہو اسکو پائی سے ضرب دیں اور اس حاصل ضرب کو چار سے تقسیم کر دیں تو جو حاصل تقسیم ہوگا وہ درھم کی پیٹھ، یا پیٹ کا رقبہ ہو گا۔ مثال مذکور میں درھم کا قطر 2,75 سینٹی میٹر ہے اسلئے 2.75 کو 2.75 سے ضرب دیں حاصل ضرب 7.5625 مربع سینٹی میٹر ہوگا، پھر اسکو پائی 3.1416 سے ضرب دیں، حاصل ضرب 23.7583 مربع سینٹی میٹر ہوگا، پھر اسکو 4 سے تقسیم دے دیں حاصل تقسیم 5.93958 مربع سینٹی میٹر ہوگا، یہ درھم کی پیٹھ، یا پیٹ کا رقبہ ہے نوٹ:۔ یہ حساب آپکو نجاست غلیظہ کی پیمائش میں کام آئے گا۔
ده در ده حوض کو گول حوض میں تبدیل کرنے کا حساب او پردہ دردہ یعنی دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا حوض کے بارے میں بتایا کہ اس میں وضو جائز ہے لیکن اگر بڑا کنواں ہو یا گول حوض ہو تو اسکا حساب اس طرح ہوگا۔ کہ حوض کی لمبائی اور چوڑائی کو ضرب دیں حاصل ضرب کو پھر 4 سے ضرب دیں پھر اس حاصل ضرب کو پائی 3.1416 سے تقسیم کریں پھر حاصل تقسیم کو برابر برابر میں تقسیم کر دیں تو گول کنویں کا قطر نکل جائے گا اور گول کنویں، یا گول حوض کے قطر کو ناپ نے سے مسئلہ حل ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا دس ہاتھ لمبا اور دس ہاتھ چوڑا حوض پندرہ فٹ لمبا اور پندرہ فٹ چوڑا ہو گا اسلئے کہ ایک ہاتھ ڈیڑ فٹ کا ہوتا ہے۔ اور 15 کو 15 سے ضرب دیں تو 225 مربع فٹ دو دردہ حوض ہوا، پھر اسکو 4 سے ضرب دیں تو 900 مربع فٹ ہوا اسکو اب پائی 3.1416 سے تقسیم دیں 286.478 مربع فٹ ہوا، اس حاصل تقسیم کو برابر برابر میں تقسیم کریں تو 16.9256 فٹ گول حوض کا قطر ہو جائے گا یعنی اگر کسی کنویں کا قطر 16.9256 فٹ ہو تو وہ وہ دردہ حوض کے مطابق ہے اور اس سے وضو کرنا جائز ہے۔
میٹر کے حساب سے گول حوض کا حساب اس طرح ہوگا:۔ ایک ہاتھ 45.72 سینٹی میٹر کا ہوتا ہے اسلئے دس ہاتھ لمبا 4.572 میٹر ہوگا اور وہی 4.572 میٹر چوڑا ہو گا ان دونوں کو ضرب کریں تو 1 20.903 مربع میٹر وہ دردہ حوض ہو گا۔ اب اسکو 4 سے ضرب دیجئے تو حاصل ضرب 83.6127 مربع میٹر ہو جائے گا، اسکو پائی 3.1416 سے تقسیم کریں تو حاصل تقسیم 26.6146 ہوگا، پھر اسکو برابر برابر میں تقسیم کریں تو 5.1589 میٹر ہو گا جو گول کنویں کا قطر ہوگا یہ کنواں وہ دردہ کے برابر ہے اس سے وضو کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور حوض اتنا گہرا ہو کہ چلو بھرنے سے زمین نہ کھلے، پیچ روایت یہی ہے۔
لغت: حلت: حلول سے مشتق ہے، حلول کر گیا ہو، گر گیا ہو۔ را کدا: ٹھہرا ہوا ہو، بہتا پانی نہ ہو۔
ترجمه: (۱۴) یا پانی جاری ہو اور اس میں نجاست کاثر ظاہر ہو گیا ہو تو پانی ناپاک ہو گا ]
تشریح: پانی جاری ہو، یا پانی وہ دردہ ہو لیکن اس میں نجاست گرنے کی وجہ سے تینوں اثر [ یعنی رنگ، بو، مزا] میں سے کوئی ایک بدل گیا تو پانی ناپاک شمار کیا جائے گا، اور یہ نہ بدلا ہو نجاست گرنے کے باوجود اس کو نا پاک نہیں شمار کیا جائے گا۔
ترجمه (۱۵) اور اثر مزا، رنگ اور بو ہے۔
Ten by ten. The formula for measuring round objects. It is necessary to remember the definition of four terms for measuring round objects: (1) Diameter (2) Pi (3) Area of a sphere (4) Area of a round dirham.
(1) Diameter: The length through the middle of a round object is called diameter. The line in the middle of the circle is the diameter.
(2) Pi: To measure any round object, the number pi must be used. 22/7 is called pi. Its value from a calculator is 3.14285, but in English books it is given as 3.1416, so the calculation of pi will be done with that.
(3) Area of a sphere: A ball-like object that is completely round is called a sphere, derived from kurah. A sphere has two diameters, one from right to left and the other from top to bottom. Therefore, to find the total surface area of a sphere, multiply one diameter by the other, then multiply that product by pi. For example, a ball's diameter is 7 inches, and the ball is completely spherical, so both diameters are 7 inches. Multiply 7 by 7, product 49 square inches, multiply by pi 3.1416, product 153.938 square inches, the total area of the ball. And if you want to find the area of a cut side of the ball, divide the total area by 4. In the example, total area 153.938 divided by 4 gives 38.4845 square inches, which is the area of one side. And to measure the circumference of the ball, multiply the diameter by pi. In the example, 7 multiplied by 3.1416 gives 21.9912 inches, that is the circumference of the ball. Note: This calculation will be used in measuring the direction of Qibla.
(4) Area of a round dirham: It is derived from dirham, so it is called a round dirham. A dirham is not round on all sides, only on top. To measure its circumference, the same formula must be used. That is, if you want to measure its circumference, multiply its diameter by pi, then the top circumference will be found. For example, the diameter of a dirham is 2.75 cm, so multiply it by pi 3.1416, product 8.6394 square cm, that will be the top circumference of the dirham.
(14) Or flowing water and its effect appears in it (15) And the effect is taste, color, or smell.
And if you want to measure the area of the back or belly of a dirham, multiply the diameter by the diameter, then multiply that product by pi, and then divide that product by four, then whatever quotient results is the area of the back or belly of the dirham. In the mentioned example, the diameter of the dirham is 2.75 cm, so multiply 2.75 by 2.75, product 7.5625 square cm, then multiply it by pi 3.1416, product 23.7583 square cm, then divide it by 4, quotient 5.93958 square cm, that is the area of the back or belly of the dirham. Note: This calculation will be useful in measuring thick impurity.
Ten by ten: The calculation for converting a square cistern into a round cistern: It has been stated that about a cistern ten cubits long and ten cubits wide, that performing wudu in it is permissible. But if there is a large well or a round cistern, its calculation will be as follows: Multiply the length and width of the cistern, then multiply the product by 4, then divide that product by pi 3.1416, then divide the quotient equally into two equal parts, then the diameter of the round well will emerge. And by measuring the diameter of the round well or round cistern, the problem will be solved. For example, a cistern ten cubits long and ten cubits wide will be fifteen feet long and fifteen feet wide, because one cubit is 1.5 feet. Multiply 15 by 15, product 225 square feet for the ten-by-ten cistern, then multiply it by 4, product 900 square feet, then divide it by pi 3.1416, quotient 286.478 square feet, then divide that quotient equally, resulting in 16.9256 feet, which will be the diameter of the round cistern. So if any well has a diameter of 16.9256 feet, then it matches the ten-by-ten cistern, and performing wudu from it is permissible.
The calculation of the round cistern in meters is as follows: One cubit is 45.72 cm, so ten cubits long is 4.572 meters, and the same width. Multiply both, product is 20.903 square meters for the ten-by-ten cistern. Now multiply it by 4, product becomes 83.6127 square meters, divide it by pi 3.1416, quotient is 26.6146, then divide it equally, resulting in 5.1589 meters, which will be the diameter of the round well. This well is equivalent to the ten-by-ten cistern, so performing wudu from it is permissible. And the cistern should be deep enough that when you scoop water, the ground does not become exposed. This is the established narration.
Lexicon: halta: derived from hulul, has settled, has fallen. raakida: stagnant, not flowing water.
Translation: (14) Or water is flowing and the effect of impurity appears in it, then the water becomes impure.
Explanation: Water is flowing, or water is ten-by-ten, but due to impurity falling into it, one of the three effects (i.e., color, smell, taste) changes, then the water will be considered impure. And if it does not change despite impurity falling, it will not be considered impure.
Translation (15) And the effect is taste, color, or smell.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a practical application of geometry to fiqh rulings on water purity (taharah). It begins by defining four key terms for measuring round objects: qutr (diameter), pai (pi), area of a sphere (gol karvi), and area of a round dirham (gol dirhami). These definitions serve as tools for later fiqh calculations. The author then explains the formula for the surface area of a sphere (multiply diameters, then by pi) and its circumference (diameter times pi), with a note that this is useful for measuring the direction of Qibla. Next, he covers the round dirham, noting its curved top and flat back/belly, providing formulas for its circumference and area. Significantly, he mentions that the area calculation of the dirham's back/belly is used for measuring thick impurity (najasat ghalizah), a key concept in Hanafi fiqh for determining the spread of impurity. The passage then transitions to a specific fiqh problem: converting the dimensions of a square cistern of ten cubits by ten cubits (dhur dar dhur) into the equivalent diameter for a round well or cistern. This size is important because Hanafi law considers that such a large body of water is not rendered impure by the mere falling of impurity unless one of its three attributes (color, smell, taste) changes. The author provides calculations in feet and meters to determine that a round well with diameter approximately 16.93 feet or 5.16 meters is equivalent in capacity. Finally, the passage states the ruling explicitly: flowing water or water meeting the size threshold remains pure unless an effect (taste, color, or smell) changes due to impurity. If no change occurs, the water remains pure. The lexicon clarifies words used in the Arabic text: 'halta' (has settled) and 'raakida' (stagnant). This passage is characteristic of Thamaratun Najah, combining practical calculation with fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
اثر (athar): The effect of impurity on water; specifically any change in taste (طعم), color (لون), or smell (ریح).
نجاست غلیظہ (najasat ghalizah): Thick impurity, such as blood, urine, or wine, which requires specific measurement of area (using dirham size) to determine its spread.
ده در ده (dhur dar dhur): A square cistern of ten cubits by ten cubits; a standard measure for determining if water is considered 'large' and thus not instantly contaminated by falling impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for flowing water to become impure due to impurity falling into it?
A) The water must be stagnant and small in quantity.
B) One of the three attributes (taste, color, or smell) must change.
C) The impurity must be thick (ghalizah).
D) The water must be less than ten cubits in depth.

Key Takeaway
Water is presumed pure; only a change in taste, color, or smell due to impurity renders it impure, provided the water is flowing or of sufficient volume (equivalent to a 10x10 cubit cistern).

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Ruling on Water Impurity: Property Change Requirement
States ruling and proof for impurity when taste/color/smell changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when water becomes impure and identify the proof (dalil) from the hadith of Abu Umamah.

Core Idea
Water remains pure unless its taste, color, or smell changes due to impurity.

Water purity is fundamental for acts of worship like wudu and ghusl. This lesson presents the core Hanafi criterion: water, whether flowing or in a large basin, stays pure (tahir) even if impurity falls into it, as long as one of its three sensory properties—taste, color, or smell—remains unchanged. The ruling is firmly grounded in a prophetic hadith that limits impurity to alteration of these properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The state of water (pure or impure). Identify the conditions: water is either flowing or in a large basin (ten by ten cubits). The ruling is that it remains pure unless a sensory change occurs.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Umamah al-Bahili recorded in Ibn Majah and Tahawi: 'Water is not made impure by anything except that which overcomes its smell, taste, and color.' This is the primary proof.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses a general negation ('لا ينجسه شيء') followed by an exception ('إلا ما غلب'). In Hanafi usul, the exception restricts the general rule: impurity only occurs when one of the three properties changes. Thus, the ruling is directly derived from the text.
The exception 'ما غلب' implies a significant change, not a mere trace.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that if water is less than two qullahs (approx. 270 liters), it becomes impure upon contact with impurity regardless of property change. The Hanafi school maintains that property change is required for all water sizes, but for small water (less than ten by ten), additional rules apply outside this passage.
This difference arises from different interpretations of other hadith.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, check: Is the water flowing or in a large basin? Did a detectable impurity fall? Has any one of the three properties changed? If no change, water remains pure and can be used for wudu.
If the water is still (not flowing) and smaller than ten by ten, the ruling may differ; this passage covers large or flowing water.

Ten by ten. (14) Or it is flowing and its effect appears in it. (15) The effect is taste, color, or smell. And if you want to measure the back or belly area of a dirham, multiply the dirham's diameter by itself, multiply the product by pi, and divide by 4; the result is the area of the dirham's back or belly. Note: This calculation will help you in measuring thick impurity. Calculation for converting a ten-by-ten basin into a circular basin: It was said that ablution is permissible in a basin ten cubits long and ten cubits wide. But if there is a large well or circular basin, its calculation is as follows: Multiply length and width of the basin, then multiply by 4, then divide by pi 3.1416, then take the square root; this will give the diameter of the circular well. For example, a ten-cubit-long and ten-cubit-wide basin is 15 feet long and 15 feet wide because one cubit is 1.5 feet. Multiply 15 by 15 to get 225 sq ft for the ten-by-ten basin, then multiply by 4 to get 900 sq ft, then divide by pi 3.1416 to get 286.478 sq ft, then take the square root to get 16.9256 ft as the diameter of the circular well; so if a well's diameter is 16.9256 ft, it corresponds to the ten-by-ten basin and ablution from it is permissible. Then multiply by 4 to get 83.6127 sq m, divide by pi 3.1416 to get 26.6146, then take the square root to get 5.1589 m, which is the diameter of the circular well; this well is equivalent to the ten-by-ten basin and ablution from it is permissible. And the basin should be deep enough that the ground does not become exposed when scooping water; this is the correct narration. Translation: (14) Or water is flowing and the effect of impurity appears in it, then the water is impure. Explanation: If water is flowing, or it is a ten-by-ten basin, but due to impurity falling in it, one of the three effects (color, smell, taste) changes, then the water is considered impure. If it does not change, despite impurity falling, it is not considered impure. Translation: (15) And the effect is taste, color, and smell.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on water impurity under two conditions: the water must be either flowing or a large reservoir (at least ten cubits by ten cubits), and the impurity must change one of its three primary properties—taste, color, or smell. If any of these changes, the water becomes impure (najis); if none change, the water remains pure (tahir). The author supports this with a hadith from Abu Umamah al-Bahili (recorded in Ibn Majah and Tahawi) that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Water is not made impure by anything except that which overcomes its smell, taste, and color.' This passage also provides detailed mathematical formulas to determine the equivalent diameter of a circular well that holds the same volume as a square ten-by-ten cubit basin, which is a standard measure for water purity in the Hanafi school. This calculation is given in feet and meters and is used for practical application when measuring large wells. The commentary confirms that as long as the water's properties remain unchanged, even if impurity falls into it, the water is not impure. The passage thus combines legal ruling with practical measurement guidelines.

Key Terms
ده در ده (dah dar dah): A basin ten cubits long and ten cubits wide, a standard measure for water purity in the Hanafi school.
اثر (athar): The effect of impurity on water, namely change in taste (طعم), color (لون), or smell (ريح).
ماء جار (ma'un jarin): Flowing water, such as a river or stream, which is considered immune to impurity unless its properties change.

A) Immediately upon contact with any impurity

C) Only if two of the three properties change
D) Only if the water becomes turbid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, large or flowing water remains pure despite impurity unless its taste, color, or smell perceptibly changes.

Water Drunk by Donkey or Mule: The Doubtful Water (Mā’ Mashkūk)
Defines the fifth water type as mashkook (doubtful) due to conflicting evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies water drunk by a donkey or mule as mashkook (doubtful) and derive the operative ruling for wudu.

Core Idea
Water drunk by a donkey or mule is legally doubtful due to conflicting evidence: prohibition of its meat vs. permissibility of its sweat.

In Hanafi fiqh, water is categorized into types based on purity. The fifth type is mashkook (doubtful) water — water drunk by a donkey or mule. This lesson unpacks the evidence that creates the doubt and the practical ruling: when such water is the only source, one should perform tayammum instead of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the water category
The passage defines the fifth type of water: mā’ mashkūk, specifically water from which a donkey or mule has drunk. Note the term 'su'r' (remnant) is used.
This is a distinct category only in the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the two conflicting proofs
One proof: the Prophet forbade donkey meat (Bukhari, Muslim) — implying impurity. Another proof: the Prophet rode a donkey, and his clothes contacted its sweat — sweat is pure, so saliva should also be pure.
The conflict is between qiyas (meat prohibitions) and direct practice (riding).
3
Understand the resulting doubt and ruling
Because both proofs have strength, the water's purity is uncertain. The Hanafi ruling is that one should not use it for wudu; instead, perform tayammum as a precaution.
This is a case of ihtiyāt (caution) due to doubt.
4
Apply the ruling to related cases
The same ruling applies to mules because they are born from donkeys. Water from a horse, however, is pure (as horse meat was permitted).
See the hadith from Abu Dawood about mule and donkey prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵ [ب]) والخامس ماء مشكوك في طهوريته وهو ما شرب منه حمار او بغل.
صلى
تشریح : نجاست کا اثر ظاہر ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ، مزا، رنگ، یا بو بدل گیا ہو۔ وجه: اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت گزر گیا ہے۔ عن ابي امامة الباهلي قال قال رسول الله لهم ان الماء لا ينجسه شيء الا ما غلب على ريحه وطعمه ولونه (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الحیاض، ص ۷۴ نمبر ۵۲۱ طحاوی شریف باب الماء تقع فیه النجاسۃ ص (۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بڑا تالاب ہو یا جاری پانی ہو تو تینوں اوصاف میں سے ایک نہ بدل جائے پانی ناپاک نہیں
ہوگا۔
ترجمه : (۱۵[ب]) اور پانچویں قسم اس کے پاک ہونے میں مشکوک پانی ہے، اور وہ جس سے گدھے یا خچر نے پیا ہو۔ تشریح یہ پانی کی پانچویں قسم ہے، جسکو ماء مشکوک، کہتے ہیں، جس پانی کو گدھے نے پیا ہو، یا خچر نے پیا ہو تو اس کا جوٹھا مشکوک ہو گیا ۔ مشکوک کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ بھی شک ہے کہ وہ پانی پاک ہے، اس لئے اس سے وضو جائز ہے۔ اور یہ بھی شک ہے کہ وہ پانی ناپاک ہے اس لئے اس سے وضو جائز نہیں ہے، اسلئے تیتم کیا جائے۔
وجه : (۱) مشکوک ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ گدھے کے گوشت اور پسینے کے سلسلے میں دونوں قسم کے دلائل ہیں ۔ آپ نے گدھے کا گوشت کھانے سے منع فرمایا۔ اور جب گوشت حلال نہیں ہوگا تو اس کا نکلا ہوا تھوک بھی نجس ہوگا۔ اس اعتبار سے گدھے کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہونا چاہئے ۔ لیکن آپ گدھے پر سوار ہوئے ہیں جس کی وجہ سے آپ کے کپڑے پر گدھے کا پسینہ لگا ہوگا اور پسینہ گوشت سے نکلتا ہے اور پسینے کا حکم بھی وہی ہے جو تھوک کا حکم ہے۔ اس لئے اگر پسینہ لگنے سے کپڑا نہیں دھویا اور پسینہ پاک ہے تو اس اعتبار سے تھوک بھی پاک ہونا چاہئے ۔ گویا کہ گدھے کے تھوک کے سلسلے میں دونوں قسم کے دلائل ہیں اس لئے گدھے کا جوٹھا مشکوک ہے۔ (۲) نجس ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال نهى رسول الله له يوم خيبر عن لحوم
صلى الله
الحمر ورخص في الخيل. (بخاری شریف، باب غزوۃ خیبر ، ج ثانی، ص ۶۰۶ نمبر ۴۲۱۹ مسلم شریف، باب تحريم أكل لحم الحمر الانسية ،ص ۸۶۶، نمبر ۵۰۰۵/۱۹۳۶) جب گوشت حلال نہیں تو تھوک بھی پاک نہیں ہوگا۔ (۳) اثر میں ہے کہ گدھے کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے۔ عن ابن عمر أنه كان يكره سئور الحمار - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، ۳۱ فی الوضوء بسور الحمار والكلب من كرهه ، ج اول ص ۳۵ نمبر ۳۰۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گدھے کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے۔ خچر کا حکم گدھے کا حکم ہے کیونکہ خچر گدھے سے پیدا ہوتا ہے۔(۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن جابـر بـن عبـد الله قال : ذبحنا يوم
خيبر الـخـيـل و البغال والحمير ، فنهانا رسول الله الا الله عن البغال والحمير ، و لم ينهنا عن الخيل ( ابوداود شریف ، باب فی اكل لحوم الخیل ،ص ۵۴۱ نمبر ۳۷۸۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خچر کا گوشت گدھے کی طرح ممنوع ہے
(15b) And the fifth is water whose purity is doubtful, and that is what a donkey or mule has drunk from. Explanation: The meaning of 'effect of impurity appearing' is that taste, color, or smell has changed. Evidence: The proof for this has passed in the hadith of Abu Umamah al-Bahili: the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Water is not made impure by anything except what overpowers its smell, taste, and color.' This hadith states that whether it is a large pond or flowing water, if one of the three properties does not change, the water is not impure. Translation: (15b) And the fifth type is water whose purity is doubtful, and that is what a donkey or mule has drunk from. Explanation: This is the fifth type of water, called mashkook water. Water from which a donkey or mule has drunk has a doubtful remnant (su'r). The meaning of doubtful is that it is doubted whether the water is pure, so wudu from it is permissible, and also doubted whether it is impure, so wudu from it is not permissible. Therefore, tayammum is performed. Reasoning: (1) The reason for doubt is that there are two kinds of evidence concerning donkey's meat and sweat. The Prophet (ﷺ) forbade eating donkey's meat. Since the meat is not halal, its saliva would also be impure. From this perspective, the donkey's remnant should be impure. However, the Prophet (ﷺ) rode a donkey, so his clothes would have come into contact with donkey's sweat, and sweat comes from the flesh, and the ruling on sweat is the same as on saliva. Therefore, if the clothes were not washed due to sweat contact, and sweat is pure, then from this perspective, the saliva should also be pure. Thus, there are conflicting evidences regarding donkey's saliva, so its remnant is doubtful. (2) The evidence for impurity is the hadith of Jabir ibn 'Abdillah: The Prophet (ﷺ) forbade on the day of Khaybar the meat of domestic donkeys and permitted horses. (Bukhari, Muslim). Since the meat is not halal, the saliva is also not pure. (3) There is an athar that the remnant of a donkey is disliked. Ibn 'Umar used to dislike the su'r of a donkey. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). The ruling for mule is the same as for donkey because the mule is born from a donkey. Hadith: Jabir ibn 'Abdillah said: We slaughtered horses, mules, and donkeys on the day of Khaybar, then the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade us from mules and donkeys, and did not forbid horses. (Abu Dawood). This hadith states that the meat of mule is prohibited like that of donkey.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth category of water in Hanafi fiqh: water from which a donkey or mule has drunk. This water is termed 'mashkook' (doubtful) because there is conflicting evidence regarding the purity of the animal's saliva. On one hand, the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade eating donkey meat, which would imply the animal is impure and thus its saliva is impure. On the other hand, the Prophet (ﷺ) rode donkeys, and his clothes would have contacted their sweat, which is analogous to saliva; yet he did not instruct washing the clothes, suggesting the sweat (and by extension saliva) is pure. Due to this contradiction, the water's purity status is doubtful. The author cites hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about the prohibition of donkey meat, and an athar from Ibn 'Umar that he disliked (considered makruh) the remnant (su'r) of a donkey. The ruling for mule is derived analogously because the mule is born from a donkey, and a hadith from Abu Dawood confirms the prohibition of mule meat. Therefore, the operative Hanafi ruling is that one should not perform wudu with such water; instead, one should perform tayammum (dry ablution) because the water's purity is uncertain.

Key Terms
ماء مشکوک (ma'un mashkook): Water whose purity is doubtful; specifically water drunk by a donkey or mule. The doubt arises from conflicting evidences.
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water or remnant after an animal drinks from it.
جوٹھا (jutha): Urdu term for su'r; the leftover water after drinking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on water from which a donkey has drunk according to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage?
A) It is pure and can be used for wudu
B) It is impure and cannot be used for wudu
C) It is doubtful (mashkook); one should perform tayammum
D) It is impermissible to use it under any circumstance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies water drunk by a donkey or mule as mashkook (doubtful); due to conflicting evidence, one should avoid it for wudu and perform tayammum.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
12 min
The Four Categories of Su'r (Leftover Water)
Classifies leftover water by source animal into four categories with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the leftover water (su'r) by source animal into pure, impure, disliked, and doubtful categories, and cite the proofs for each ruling.

Core Idea
Su'r is pure if from a human or halal-meat animal; impure if from dog, pig, or beast of prey.

This lesson categorizes leftover water (su'r) based on the animal that drank from it. The Hanafi school distinguishes four types: pure (tahir), impure (najis), disliked (makruh), and doubtful (mashkuk). Understanding this classification is essential for daily taharah practice and avoiding invalid purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four types of su'r as given in the passage: 1) from humans, horses, and halal-meat animals (pure); 2) from dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey (impure); 3) from cats and uncaged hens (disliked); 4) from donkeys and mules (doubtful).
Note the Urdu table enumerating these.
2
State the ruling for each category
For each category, determine the fiqh ruling (hukm) for using the water in wudu or ghusl. Pure water (tahir) is permissible, impure (najis) is prohibited, disliked (makruh) is valid but discouraged, doubtful (mashkuk) requires precaution.
3
Locate the proofs
Associate each category with its evidence. For humans: hadith of Ibn Abbas and Aisha. For horses: hadith of Asma and Jabir. For dogs: hadith of Abu Huraira (washing seven times). For pigs: Quran 6:45. For beasts of prey: hadith of Abu Thalaba.
The author cites multiple hadiths and the Quran.
4
Understand the Hanafi principle
The underlying principle: su'r inherits the ruling of the animal's meat (halal or haram). The saliva (spittle) originates from the meat, so if the meat is halal, the su'r is pure; if haram, the su'r is impure (or disliked if doubt exists).
This principle is key to deriving the rules.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
The Shafi'i school generally considers the su'r of all non-human animals as impure. The Hanafi school differentiates based on meat permissibility. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (scholarly difference).
Understanding the dispute prevents confusion in practice.

Chapter on rulings of su'r. (16) And a small amount of water, if an animal drinks from it, is of four types and is called su'r. (17) The first is pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir), and it is what a human, a horse, or an animal whose meat is eaten has drunk from. (18) The second is impure (najis), its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, a pig, or any beast of prey like a leopard or wolf has drunk from. The third category (from Urdu table) is makruh (disliked) from cat, uncaged hen, etc. The fourth is mashkuk (doubtful) from donkey and mule. Proofs: Hadith of Ibn Abbas showing human su'r is pure; hadith of Aisha showing menstruating woman's su'r is pure; hadith of Asma showing horse meat is halal so its su'r is pure; hadith of Jabir showing horse meat halal; hadith of Bara' stating that meat of halal animals has pure su'r. For impure: hadith of Abu Huraira regarding dog's su'r requiring washing seven times; Quran verse 6:45 declaring pig impure; hadith of Abu Thalaba forbidding eating fanged beasts of prey.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the classification of su'r (leftover water) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by defining su'r and then categorizes it into four types based on the animal that drank from the water. The first category is water drunk by humans, horses, and halal-meat animals; this water is tahir (pure) and mutahir (purifying), meaning it can be used for wudu and ghusl. The second category is water drunk by dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey (like leopards and wolves); this water is najis (impure) and cannot be used for purification. The third category (mentioned in the Urdu table) includes cats and uncaged hens, and their su'r is makruh (disliked). The fourth category is donkeys and mules, and their su'r is mashkuk (doubtful). The author then provides proofs from hadith and Quran: for humans, the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Aisha; for horses, hadiths showing horse meat is halal; for dogs, the hadith of washing a vessel seven times; for pigs, Quranic verse; for beasts of prey, the prohibition of eating them. The commentary follows the author's order, clarifying each category and its evidence.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water in a vessel after an animal or human has drunk from it.
طاهر (tahir): Pure; ritually clean and capable of purifying other things.
نجس (najis): Ritually impure; cannot be used for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on su'r (leftover water) of a dog?
A) It is pure and can be used for wudu.
B) It is impure and cannot be used for purification.
C) It is disliked (makruh).
D) It is doubtful (mashkuk).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of su'r is based on the principle that the leftover water takes the ruling of the animal's meat: halal-meat animals yield pure su'r, while haram-meat animals yield impure su'r.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The Three Categories of Su'r (Leftover Water)
Enumerates three categories of leftover water with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of su'r and identify the ruling for each category based on the type of animal.

Core Idea
Leftover water's ruling follows the meat: halal meat = pure, haram meat = impure, but difficulty may reduce it to disliked.

The Hanafi school classifies leftover water (su'r) from animals into three categories: pure and purifying, impure, and disliked. This lesson introduces the framework and the foundational principle that saliva derives from meat, linking the animal's dietary status to the purity of its leftover water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and list the three rulings: pure/purifying, impure, and disliked. Note that each corresponds to a specific group of animals.
The categories are exhaustive for domestic and wild animals.
2
Understand the linking principle
In Hanafi fiqh, the ruling on leftover water is directly tied to the permissibility of the animal's meat. Saliva originates from flesh, so halal meat yields pure saliva, haram meat yields impure saliva.
This principle is derived from the hadith: 'ما أكل لحمه فلا بأس بسؤره' (What is eaten of its meat, no harm in its leftover).
3
Recognize the exception of difficulty
For animals whose meat is haram but which are difficult to avoid (like cats and domestic rodents), the ruling is reduced to makruh (disliked) rather than najis (impure).
This is based on the principle of facilitation (tashil) in the Shariah.

(ترندى شریف، باب ماجاء فی سور الکلب ص ۲۷ نمبر (۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلی کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہے تب ہی تو ایک مرتبہ دھونے کے لئے کہا (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال النبی الله السنور سبع (سنن ابیتی ، باب سوراکھر ۃ، ج اول ص ۷ ۲۷ نمبر ۱۷۶اردار
Chapter on the rulings of leftover water. (18) Purifier, and it is what a human or horse or what is eaten of its meat drinks from. And the second is impure, its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, or pig, or any beast of prey like leopard and wolf drinks from. (19) And the third is disliked to use in the presence of other water, and it is the leftover of a cat, a free-range hen, and birds of prey like falcon, goshawk, and kite, and domestic vermin like mice, but not the scorpion.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the three categories of leftover water (su'r) in Hanafi fiqh. The first category (18) is purifying: leftover water from humans, horses, and animals whose meat is halal. The commentary provides hadith proofs: for horse meat being halal (from Asma and Jabir), and the principle that saliva derives from meat, so halal meat implies pure saliva. The second category is impure: from dogs, pigs, and wild beasts of prey. Proofs: hadith on dog's saliva requiring seven washes, Quranic verse declaring pig impure, and prohibition of eating fanged beasts. The third category (19) is disliked (makruh) when other water is available: from cats, free-range hens, birds of prey, and domestic rodents, but not scorpions. The reasoning: these animals' meat is generally haram, so their saliva would be impure by analogy, but due to difficulty of avoidance (they frequent homes and vessels), the Shariah grants leniency, declaring it disliked rather than impure. Scorpion's leftover is pure because it lacks flowing blood.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water remaining after an animal or human drinks from a vessel.
مطهر (mutahhir): A purifier; leftover water that is itself pure and can be used for purification.
نجس (najis): Ritually impure; such water cannot be used for purification and must be avoided.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; using this water when other pure water is available is discouraged but not sinful.
سباع (siba'): Predatory animals that tear their prey with fangs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the leftover water (su'r) of a cat if other pure water is available?
A) Pure and purifying
B) Impure and not permissible to use
C) Disliked to use
D) Permissible and preferred

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies su'r into three categories based on the animal's meat and the difficulty of avoidance, with the general rule that saliva follows meat.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Category 1: Su'r of Halal Meat Animals
Defines the first category and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animals' leftover water is pure and purifying and explain the proof that links halal meat to pure saliva.

Core Idea
Leftover water from humans, horses, and halal meat animals is pure and purifies other things.

The first category of su'r includes water from humans, horses, and animals whose meat is halal. The Hanafi school relies on the principle that saliva derives from flesh, so if the meat is halal, the saliva is pure. This lesson examines the animals in this category and the proofs from hadith that establish the ruling.

Guided Path
1
List the animals in the first category
From the passage, identify the animals: humans, horses, and any animal whose meat is halal (e.g., cows, sheep, goats, chickens).
Note that the horse is explicitly mentioned; its meat is halal according to most Hanafi authorities.
2
Trace the proof: saliva comes from meat
The logical link: saliva is produced from the flesh. If the flesh is permissible (halal), the saliva is pure. Evidence is the hadith: 'Who eats its meat, there is no harm in its leftover.'
This hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Examine the hadith proofs for horse
Two hadith are cited: one from Asma (ra) about eating horse meat, and another from Jabir (ra) permitting horse meat while prohibiting donkey meat. These establish that horse is halal, so its su'r is pure.
The principle is applied generally to all halal meat animals.
