۳۶ نمبر (۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جسکا گوشت حلال ہے اسکا جوٹھا بھی پاک ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۸) دوسرا ناپاک پانی ہے، جس کا استعمال جائز نہیں ہے، یہ وہ پانی ہے جس سے کتے نے ہور نے ، یا پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور نے پیا ہو، جیسے چیتا اور بھیڑیا۔ تشریح : یہ دوسرے قسم کا پانی ہے جسکو ایسے جانور نے پیا ہے جس کا گوشت کھانا حرام ہے، ابھی گزرا کہ تھوک گوشت سے پیدا ہوتا ہے، اس لئے جس جانور کا گوشت حرام ہے اس جانور نے پانی پیا ہو تو اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہے ، اس کو کسی چیز کو پاک کرنے کے لئے استعمال کرنا جائز نہیں۔ جیسے کتے کا جوٹھا ، سور کا جوٹھا، چیتے کا جوٹھا اور بھیڑیے کا جوٹھا۔ وجه : (۱) کتے کا جوٹھانا پاک ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا شرب الكلب في اناء احدكم فليغسله سبعا ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا شرب الكلب فى اناء احد کم فلیغسله سبعا ،ص ۲۹، نمبر ۷۲ ارابو داود شریف ، باب ماجاء فی سور الکلب ، ص ۲۷ نمبر ۹۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کتے کا جوٹھانا پاک ہے اس لئے اس برتن کو بھی سات مرتبہ دھوؤ و۔ (۲) سور کا جوٹھانا پاک ہے اس لئے کہ وہ نجس العین ہے، اس کے لئے یہ آیت ہے۔ ولحم خنزیر فانه رجس ( آیت ۴۵ سورۃ الانعام ۶) اس آیت میں سور کو نجس کہا گیا ہے۔ اسلئے اسکا جوٹھا بھی نجس ہے۔(۳) ہر پھاڑ کھانے والے جانور کا جوٹھانا پاک ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ثعلبة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نھی عن اكل كل ذي ناب من السباع - ( بخاری شریف ، باب اکل کل ذی ناب من السباع ، ص ۹۸۴ نمبر ۵۵۳۰ مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم اکل کل ذی ناب من السباع وكل ذی مخلب من الطير ، ص ۸۶۳، نمبر ۴۹۸۹/۱۹۳۲) قاعدہ گزر چکا ہے کہ جس کا گوشت حرام اس کا جوٹھا نا پاک ہے۔ چیتے اور بھیڑیے کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا بھی ناپاک ہے۔ (۴) بھیڑ یا پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور ہے، اور اس کا گوشت صلى الله عليه وسلم حرام ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عـن حـبـان جـزء عن أخيه خزيمة بن جزء قال سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أكل الضبع قال ويأكل الضبع أحد ؟ و سألته عن أكل الذئب فقال ويأكل الذئب أحد فيه خير ؟ (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی أكل الضبع ، ص ۴۲۴، نمبر ۱۷۹۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بھیڑیا کا گوشت نہیں کھایا جا سکتا ہے۔ لغت: سباع: پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور ۔ بہائم جنگلی جانور۔ فھد : چیتا۔الذئب: بھیڑیا۔ (۱۹) والثالث مكروه استعماله مع وجود غيره وهو سؤر الهرة والدجاجة المخلاة وسباع الطير كالصقر والشاهين والحداة وسواكن البيوت كالفارة لا العقرب . ترجمه : (۱۹) تیسری قسم کا وہ پانی ہے کہ دوسرے پانی کے ہوتے ہوئے اس کا استعمال مکروہ ہو، یہ بلی، اور کھلی ہوئی مرغی ، اور پھاڑ کھانے والے پرندے،مثلا شکرے اور باز اور چیل کا جوٹھا، اور گھر میں رہنے والے جانو کا جوٹھا، جیسے چوہا سوائے بچھو کے۔ تشریح : یہ تیسری قسم کا پانی ہے، یہ مکروہ پانی ہے۔ دوسرے پانی کے رہتے ہوئے اس پانی کا استعمال کرنا مکروہ ہے ، یہ سارے وہ جانور ہیں جن کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، جیسے بلی کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، وہ مرغی جو کھلی پھرتی ہے اور نا پا کی میں منہ ڈالتی رہتی ہے اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، پھاڑ کھانے والے پرندے کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا نا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہ اڑتے ہوئے آکر پانی پی لیتا ہے، اس لئے اس کے جو ٹھے سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے اس مجبوری کی وجہ سے اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ قرار دیا ، اور گھر میں رہنے والے جانور مثلا چوہا، بلی وغیرہ کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا بھی ناپاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن رات ہی میں یہ پانی پی لے گا ، یا کھانا کھالے گا ، اس لئے اس کے جوٹھے سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے اس کے جو ٹھے کو بھی ناپاک کے بجائے مکروہ قرار دیا۔ بچھو کا جوٹھا پاک اس لئے قرار دیا کہ اس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے، اس لئے وہ کبھی کے درجے میں ہے اور اس کا جوٹھا مگر نہیں ہے، پاک ہے۔ دلیل وجہ میں دیکھیں۔ وجه : (۱) بلی پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہ گھر میں رہتی ہے اور اس سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے شریعت نے تسہیل دیدی اور اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہوا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يغسل الاناء اذا ولـغ فـيـه الـكـلـب سبع مرات اولاهن واخراهن بالتراب واذا ولغت فيه الهرة غسل مرة. (ترندى شریف، باب ماجاء فی سور الکلب ص ۲۷ نمبر (۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلی کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہے تب ہی تو ایک مرتبہ دھونے کے لئے کہا (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال النبی الله السنور سبع (سنن ابیتی ، باب سوراکھر ۃ، ج اول ص ۷ ۲۷ نمبر ۱۷۶اردار
Chapter on the rulings of leftover water. (18) Purifier, and it is what a human or horse or what is eaten of its meat drinks from. And the second is impure, its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, or pig, or any beast of prey like leopard and wolf drinks from. (19) And the third is disliked to use in the presence of other water, and it is the leftover of a cat, a free-range hen, and birds of prey like falcon, goshawk, and kite, and domestic vermin like mice, but not the scorpion.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the three categories of leftover water (su'r) in Hanafi fiqh. The first category (18) is purifying: leftover water from humans, horses, and animals whose meat is halal. The commentary provides hadith proofs: for horse meat being halal (from Asma and Jabir), and the principle that saliva derives from meat, so halal meat implies pure saliva. The second category is impure: from dogs, pigs, and wild beasts of prey. Proofs: hadith on dog's saliva requiring seven washes, Quranic verse declaring pig impure, and prohibition of eating fanged beasts. The third category (19) is disliked (makruh) when other water is available: from cats, free-range hens, birds of prey, and domestic rodents, but not scorpions. The reasoning: these animals' meat is generally haram, so their saliva would be impure by analogy, but due to difficulty of avoidance (they frequent homes and vessels), the Shariah grants leniency, declaring it disliked rather than impure. Scorpion's leftover is pure because it lacks flowing blood.

Key Terms
مطهر (mutahhir): A purifier; leftover water that is itself pure and can be used for purification.
حلال اللحم (halal al-lahm): An animal whose meat is permissible to eat according to Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a proof that the horse's leftover water is pure?
A) Quranic verse about horses
B) Hadith that horse meat is halal
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy with water

Key Takeaway
Leftover water from humans and halal meat animals (including horses) is pure and purifying based on the principle that saliva follows meat.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Category 2: Su'r of Impure Animals
Defines second category and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which animals' leftover water is impure and identify the proofs from Quran and hadith for each.

Core Idea
Leftover water from dogs, pigs, and wild beasts of prey is impure and cannot be used for purification.

The second category of su'r is impure (najis), meaning the water itself becomes impure and cannot be used for any purification. This category includes water drunk by dogs, pigs, and any beast of prey (like leopards and wolves). The Hanafi school provides specific proofs: for dogs, the hadith about washing a vessel seven times; for pigs, the Quranic verse declaring them impure; for beasts of prey, the hadith prohibiting their meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals in the second category
From the passage: dog, pig, and any beast of prey (siba') such as leopard and wolf.
Beast of prey includes all fanged predators that hunt with claws.
2
Examine the proof for dog's su'r
The hadith: 'When a dog drinks from your vessel, wash it seven times.' This indicates the water is impure because it requires washing.
The number seven is specific to dog; other animals do not require seven washes.
3
Examine the proof for pig's su'r
The Quranic verse: 'Or pig meat, for that is impure (rijs)' (Surah al-An'am, 6:145). This establishes the pig as inherently impure (najis al-ayn).
Pig is the only animal considered najis al-ayn in the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the proof for beasts of prey
The hadith: 'The Prophet prohibited eating every fanged beast of prey.' Prohibition of meat implies impurity of saliva.
This is a general rule applied to all siba'.

پانی ہے، یہ مکروہ پانی ہے۔ دوسرے پانی کے رہتے ہوئے اس پانی کا استعمال کرنا مکروہ ہے ، یہ سارے وہ جانور ہیں جن کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، جیسے بلی کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، وہ مرغی جو کھلی پھرتی ہے اور نا پا کی میں منہ ڈالتی رہتی ہے اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، پھاڑ کھانے والے پرندے کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا نا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہ اڑتے ہوئے آکر پانی پی لیتا ہے، اس لئے اس کے جو ٹھے سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے اس مجبوری کی وجہ سے اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ قرار دیا ، اور گھر میں رہنے والے جانور مثلا چوہا، بلی وغیرہ کا گوشت حرام ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا بھی ناپاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن رات ہی میں یہ پانی پی لے گا ، یا کھانا کھالے گا ، اس لئے اس کے جوٹھے سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے اس کے جو ٹھے کو بھی ناپاک کے بجائے مکروہ قرار دیا۔ بچھو کا جوٹھا پاک اس لئے قرار دیا کہ اس میں بہتا ہوا خون نہیں ہے، اس لئے وہ کبھی کے درجے میں ہے اور اس کا جوٹھا مگر نہیں ہے، پاک ہے۔ دلیل وجہ میں دیکھیں۔ وجه : (۱) بلی پھاڑ کھانے والا جانور ہے اس لئے اس کا جوٹھانا پاک ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہ گھر میں رہتی ہے اور اس سے بچنا مشکل ہے اس لئے شریعت نے تسہیل دیدی اور اس کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہوا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يغسل الاناء اذا ولـغ فـيـه الـكـلـب سبع مرات اولاهن واخراهن بالتراب واذا ولغت فيه الهرة غسل مرة. (ترندى شریف، باب ماجاء فی سور الکلب ص ۲۷ نمبر (۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بلی کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہے تب ہی تو ایک مرتبہ دھونے کے لئے کہا (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال النبی الله السنور سبع (سنن ابیتی ، باب سوراکھر ۃ، ج اول ص ۷ ۲۷ نمبر ۱۷۶اردار
Chapter on the rulings of leftover water. (18) Purifier, and it is what a human or horse or what is eaten of its meat drinks from. And the second is impure, its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, or pig, or any beast of prey like leopard and wolf drinks from. (19) And the third is disliked to use in the presence of other water, and it is the leftover of a cat, a free-range hen, and birds of prey like falcon, goshawk, and kite, and domestic vermin like mice, but not the scorpion.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the three categories of leftover water (su'r) in Hanafi fiqh. The first category (18) is purifying: leftover water from humans, horses, and animals whose meat is halal. The commentary provides hadith proofs: for horse meat being halal (from Asma and Jabir), and the principle that saliva derives from meat, so halal meat implies pure saliva. The second category is impure: from dogs, pigs, and wild beasts of prey. Proofs: hadith on dog's saliva requiring seven washes, Quranic verse declaring pig impure, and prohibition of eating fanged beasts. The third category (19) is disliked (makruh) when other water is available: from cats, free-range hens, birds of prey, and domestic rodents, but not scorpions. The reasoning: these animals' meat is generally haram, so their saliva would be impure by analogy, but due to difficulty of avoidance (they frequent homes and vessels), the Shariah grants leniency, declaring it disliked rather than impure. Scorpion's leftover is pure because it lacks flowing blood.

Key Terms
نجس (najis): Ritually impure; such water cannot be used for purification and must be avoided.
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): Inherently impure, like the pig; every part of it is impure.
سباع (siba'): Predatory animals that tear their prey with fangs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence that the pig's leftover water is impure?
A) The hadith about seven washes
B) The Quranic verse calling pig meat 'rijs' (impure)
C) Analogy with the dog
D) The hadith prohibiting fanged beasts

Key Takeaway
Leftover water from dogs, pigs, and beasts of prey is impure based on explicit texts and the principle that haram meat yields impure saliva.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
7 min
Category 3: Su'r of Disliked Animals
Defines third category and explains reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animals' leftover water is makruh (disliked) and explain the reasoning of facilitation (tashil) that reduces it from impure to disliked.

Core Idea
Leftover water from cats, free-range hens, birds of prey, and domestic rodents is disliked, not impure, due to the difficulty of avoidance.

The third category of su'r is makruh (disliked) — water that is to be avoided when other pure water is available, but if there is no other water, it may be used out of necessity. This ruling applies to animals whose meat is generally not eaten or considered haram, but which are common in homes and cannot be easily prevented from drinking from water vessels. The Hanafi school balances the principle that haram meat gives impure saliva against the practical difficulty of avoidance, resulting in a concession (rukhsah) of disliked status.

Guided Path
1
List the animals in the third category
From the passage: cat, free-range hen (dajaja mukhalla), birds of prey (falcon, goshawk, kite), and domestic vermin (mouse). Scorpion is excluded.
The common factor: they are difficult to keep away from water sources in homes.
2
Understand the tension: haram meat vs. difficulty
For most of these, the meat is either haram (birds of prey) or makruh (cat according to some), but their constant presence makes strict impurity impractical.
The Shariah grants rukhsah (concession) by reducing the ruling from najis to makruh.
3
Examine the evidence for cat's su'r
The hadith: 'If a cat drinks from a vessel, wash it once.' The Hanafi argue that if it were pure, washing would not be necessary; the single wash indicates it is between pure and impure, hence makruh.
The Shafi'i school interprets this as a recommendation, not an obligation, thus cat's su'r is pure.
4
Note the exception of scorpion
Scorpion's leftover is pure because it lacks flowing blood and is not considered a source of impurity.
Scorpions are not included in the category of difficult-to-avoid animals because they are not typically found in water containers.

Chapter on the rulings of leftover water. (18) Purifier, and it is what a human or horse or what is eaten of its meat drinks from. And the second is impure, its use is not permissible, and it is what a dog, or pig, or any beast of prey like leopard and wolf drinks from. (19) And the third is disliked to use in the presence of other water, and it is the leftover of a cat, a free-range hen, and birds of prey like falcon, goshawk, and kite, and domestic vermin like mice, but not the scorpion.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the three categories of leftover water (su'r) in Hanafi fiqh. The first category (18) is purifying: leftover water from humans, horses, and animals whose meat is halal. The commentary provides hadith proofs: for horse meat being halal (from Asma and Jabir), and the principle that saliva derives from meat, so halal meat implies pure saliva. The second category is impure: from dogs, pigs, and wild beasts of prey. Proofs: hadith on dog's saliva requiring seven washes, Quranic verse declaring pig impure, and prohibition of eating fanged beasts. The third category (19) is disliked (makruh) when other water is available: from cats, free-range hens, birds of prey, and domestic rodents, but not scorpions. The reasoning: these animals' meat is generally haram, so their saliva would be impure by analogy, but due to difficulty of avoidance (they frequent homes and vessels), the Shariah grants leniency, declaring it disliked rather than impure. Scorpion's leftover is pure because it lacks flowing blood.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; using this water when other pure water is available is discouraged but not sinful.
تسهيل (tashil): Facilitation; the Shariah grants leniency due to difficulty.
دجاجة مخلاة (dajaja mukhalla): A free-range hen that roams freely and may eat impurities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the leftover water of a cat considered makruh rather than impure in the Hanafi school?
A) Because cat meat is halal
B) Because cats are difficult to avoid in homes
C) Because the hadith says it is pure
D) Because cats are not predators

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies leftover water from cats, free-range hens, birds of prey, and domestic rodents as makruh due to the principle of facilitation (tashil), balancing legal purity rules with practical necessity.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
The Makruh Su'ur: Reconciling Proofs and the Principle of Ease
Ruling with proof on makruh su'ur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the su'ur of a cat, hen, predatory birds, and domestic pests, identify the proofs used, and apply the principle of tashil (ease) in reconciling conflicting evidence.

Core Idea
When avoidance is difficult, the Lawgiver grants ease: su'ur of domestic animals is makruh, not najis.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah introduces the third category of residual water (su'ur): that which is makruh tanzihi when pure water is available. The author lists specific animals and provides the rationale and proofs, particularly showing how the Hanafi school reconciles conflicting hadith on the cat's su'ur by considering the difficulty of avoidance. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals and their su'ur ruling
From the passage, list the animals whose su'ur is ruled makruh tanzihi. Note the exclusion of the scorpion.
Animals: cat, free-range hen, predatory birds (falcon, hawk, kite), domestic pests (mouse). Scorpion is pure.
2
Analyze the proof for the cat
Two hadith are cited: one commands washing the vessel once after a cat drinks (suggesting impurity), another states the cat is not impure. Determine how the Hanafi school reconciles them.
Reconciliation leads to makruh tanzihi, not najis or pure.
3
Apply the principle of difficulty (mashaqqa)
For each animal, the commentary explains that their su'ur would normally be najis (due to haram meat or likely filth), but because avoiding their su'ur is difficult, the ruling is lightened to makruh.
This is an application of the legal maxim 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).
4
Understand the exception of the scorpion
The scorpion's su'ur is ruled pure because it lacks flowing blood, placing it in the category of insects like the dung beetle.
This is based on the general rule that animals without flowing blood are not impure.
5
Evaluate the overall three-category framework
Place this third category within the Hanafi classification of su'ur: pure (tahir), impure (najis), and makruh. Recognize that the makruh category exists only when other pure water is available.
If no other water is available, the su'ur of these animals can be used for purification according to some views.

(مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۳۴ الوضوء بسور الدجاجۃ ، ج اول ص ۳۶ نمبر ۳۲۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مرغی کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے، مرغی بندھی ہوئی ہو، اور نجاست نہ ہونے کا یقین ہو تو اس کا جوٹھا پاک ہے، اور نجاست کا یقین ہو تو اس کا جوٹھا ناپاک ہے ۔(۵) اثر میں ہے کہ پرندے کی بیٹ ناپاک نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں مجبوری ہے، جب اسکی بیٹ نا پاک نہیں تو اسکا تھوک بدرجہ اولی ناپاک نہیں ہونا چاہئے ۔ اثر یہ ہے۔ عن الحسن قال : سقطت هائمة على الحسن فذرقت عليه فقال له بعض القوم : نأتيک بماء تغسله فقال : لا ، و جعل يمسحه عنه (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۱۴۵ الذی یصلی و فی ثوبه خرء الطير ، ج اول ص 110 نمبر ۱۲۵۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ پرندے کی بیٹ نا پاک نہیں ہے۔ (۶) عن عائشة أن رسول الله الله قال خمس من الدواب كلهن فاسق يقتلن في الحرم : الغراب و الحدأ و العقرب ، و الفأرة و الكلب العقور ۔(بخاری شریف، باب ما يقتل المحرم من الدواب ،ص ۲۹۵، نمبر ۱۸۹۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ چیل ، بچھو، اور چوہا فاسق ہے، یعنی وہ بدمعاش بھی ہیں اور ان کا گوشت حرام بھی ہے۔ لیکن سوا کن البیوت کی وجہ سے ان کا جوٹھا مکروہ ہے۔ بچھو کا جوٹھا پاک ہے۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں بہتا خون نہیں ہے اس لئے وہ کبھی کے درجے میں ہے، اس لئے اس کا جوٹھا پاک ہے۔ (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال اذا وقع الذباب في اناء احدكم فليغمسه كله ثم ليطرحه فان في احدى جناحيه شفاء وفي الآخر دواء (بخاری شریف، کتاب الطب، باب اذا وقع الذباب فی الانا ص ۸۶۰، جلد ثانی نمبر ۵۷۸۲) حدیث میں پوری مکھی کو برتن میں ڈالنے کے لئے کہا۔ اگر کھی سے کھانا یا پانی
Chapter on the rulings of su'ur. (19) The third [type] is that whose use is makruh when others exist: it is the su'ur of the cat, the free-ranging hen, predatory birds like the falcon, hawk, and kite, and domestic pests like the mouse, but not the scorpion. Commentary: The rule mentioned earlier: an animal whose meat is haram, its su'ur is najis. The cheetah and wolf have haram meat, so their su'ur is najis. The wolf is a predator, and its meat is haram, as proven by the hadith from Hubban... (the hadith about hyena and wolf). Translation: (19) The third type is water whose use is makruh when other water exists: it is the su'ur of the cat, the free-ranging hen, predatory birds like the falcon, hawk, and kite, and domestic pests like the mouse, except the scorpion. Explanation: This is the third category; it is makruh water. Using it when other water exists is makruh. All these animals have makruh su'ur. For example, the cat's su'ur is makruh. The hen that roams freely and puts its beak in filth, its su'ur is makruh. The meat of predatory birds is haram, so its su'ur should be najis, but since they fly and drink water, avoiding their su'ur is difficult; due to this difficulty, its su'ur is ruled makruh. Similarly, domestic pests like mice and cats have haram meat, so their su'ur should be najis, but they drink water at night or eat food, making avoidance difficult; so their su'ur is ruled makruh instead of najis. The scorpion's su'ur is ruled pure because it has no flowing blood; thus it is like the dung beetle, and its su'ur is pure, not najis. (1) The cat is a predator, so its su'ur should be najis, but it lives in the house and avoidance is difficult, so the Sharia granted ease and made its su'ur makruh. (2) Hadith from Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: 'The vessel when a dog drinks from it is washed seven times, first and last with soil; and when a cat drinks from it, it is washed once.' This hadith indicates the cat's su'ur is najis, otherwise it would not have been commanded to wash once. (3) But there is another hadith showing ease: from Kabsha bint Ka'b bin Malik that Abu Qatada entered upon her... a cat came to drink and he tilted the vessel for it. She said: I was looking at him, and he said: 'Do you wonder, O daughter of my brother?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'The Messenger of Allah said: It is not najis; it is one of those who go around among you.' This hadith shows the cat's su'ur is pure. So combining the two hadith, they say the cat's su'ur is makruh tanzihi. Same for all domestic animals. (4) Hen's meat is halal, but because it roams freely, it may put its beak in filth; thus its su'ur should be najis, but avoidance is difficult, so it is ruled makruh. There is an athar from Hasan: 'Concerning the hen that drinks from a vessel, he disliked using that water for wudu.' This shows the hen's su'ur is makruh. If the hen is confined and certainty of no filth, its su'ur is pure; if certainty of filth, its su'ur is najis. (5) There is an athar that bird droppings are not najis because of difficulty; if its droppings are not najis, its saliva is even more likely not najis. (6) Hadith from Aisha: The Prophet said: 'Five animals are all fasiq, they are killed in the haram: the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the mouse, and the biting dog.' This shows these animals are rebellious and their meat is haram. But because they are domestic pests, their su'ur is makruh. The scorpion's su'ur is pure because it has no flowing blood; thus it is like the dung beetle. Hadith about the fly: the Prophet said: 'If a fly falls into the vessel of one of you, let him immerse it completely then remove it, for in one of its wings is cure and in the other is disease.' The hadith commands to immerse the whole fly.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on su'ur (residual water). The author states the third category of water: water left by certain animals is makruh to use when other pure water is available. The animals listed are: cat, free-range hen, predatory birds (falcon, hawk, kite), and domestic pests (like mice). Scorpion is excluded because it lacks flowing blood. The commentary explains the rationale: even though these animals either have haram meat or likely consume filth, making their su'ur impure by the general rule, the Sharia grants leniency because avoiding their su'ur is difficult. For the cat, two hadith are cited: one from Abu Huraira that a cat's lick necessitates washing the vessel once, implying impurity; another from Kabsha that the Prophet said the cat is not impure. Reconciling them, the Hanafi ruling is that cat's su'ur is makruh tanzihi (recommended to avoid). Similarly, for the free-range hen, Hasan al-Basri's athar indicates dislike. For predatory birds, difficulty of avoidance due to their flying leads to makruh. For domestic pests like mice, night-time access makes difficulty. The scorpion is pure because it has no flowing blood, analogous to insects like the dung beetle. The passage also includes a hadith about the fly, which commands immersing it completely if it falls into a vessel, indicating the fly itself is not najis. The sources are from Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, and Bukhari. The overall lesson is that the Hanafi school balances textual evidence with ease (tashil) in ruling on su'ur.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ur): Residual water left after an animal drinks from a vessel.
مكروه تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An action that is disliked and should be avoided but is not sinful.
سباع (siba'): Predatory animals, especially those that hunt and eat meat.
تسہیل (tashil): Granting ease or leniency in a ruling due to difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the su'ur of a free-range hen when other pure water is available, according to this passage?
A) Pure (tahir)
B) Impure (najis)
C) Makruh tanzihi
D) Makruh tahrimi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules the su'ur of domestic animals (cat, hen, predatory birds, pests) as makruh tanzihi, balancing textual evidence of impurity with the practical difficulty of avoidance.

Taharah — Purification

Taharrī When Most Vessels Are Pure
Ruling with proof on taharrī for wudu and drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on taharrī for wudu and drinking when most vessels are pure and distinguish it from cases where the majority is impure.

Core Idea
When most vessels are pure, taharrī is wajib to find the pure water.

Imagine arriving at a place with many water vessels, some pure and some impure, but no way to tell which is which. You need wudu or a drink. The Hanafi school teaches that you must investigate (taharrī) and act on your dominant opinion. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and the proofs from Quran and Sunnah that justify this practical solution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage describes a mixture of vessels where most are pure (طاهر). The ruling is that one must perform taharrī (exert effort to form a dominant opinion) for both wudu and drinking.
If the majority were impure, the ruling would differ.
2
Understand the condition
The condition is that there is no clear sign (قرینہ) to distinguish pure from impure. The majority being pure is a key factor that makes taharrī valid.
If majority were impure, taharrī would not be allowed; instead, one would do tayammum.
3
Examine the proofs
The passage cites three proofs: (1) Quranic principle that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity (2:286); (2) Hadith of Jabir about taharrī for qibla in cloudy weather; (3) Hadith of Abd Allah ibn Amir ibn Rabi'a about praying in darkness.
The hadiths show that the Prophet approved taharrī even when the result was later found incorrect, establishing its validity.
4
Note the principle of taharrī
The commentary states: 'In a doubtful thing, the ruling is of taharrī, and whichever side the dominant opinion goes, that is used.' This is a general Hanafi principle applicable to purity and beyond.
Taharrī is not mere guessing but genuine investigation.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools do not permit taharrī in matters of purity; they require certainty. The Hanafi school allows it due to necessity (darura) and the principle of ease.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Ummah.

فصل : في التحرى فصل في التحرى (۲۱) لو اختلط اوان اكثرها طاهر تحرى للتوضأ والشرب. فصل تحری کے بیان میں ترجمه : (۲۱) اگر پاک اور نا پاک برتن مل جائیں اور اکثر برتن پاک ہوں تو وضو کے لئے ، اور پینے کے لئے تحری کرے۔ تشریح : کئی برتن ہیں جن میں سے کچھ میں ناپاک پانی ہے، اور کچھ میں پاک پانی ہے، اور یہ معلوم ہے کہ زیادہ تر برتنوں میں پاک پانی ہے ، اور کم برتنوں میں ناپاک پانی ہے، اور کوئی قرینہ یا علامت نہیں جس سے معلوم ہو سکے کہ کسی برتن کا پانی پاک ہے اور کس کا ناپاک ، تو اس صورت میں غور فکر کرے کہ کس برتن کا پانی پاک ہو سکتا ہے، جس برتن کی طرف پاک کارجحان ہواسی برتن کے پانی سے وضو کر لے، اور بینا ہوتو پی لے۔ اس وقت اس کے لئے یہی تحری کا حکم ہے۔ وجه : (۱) کوئی چیز مشتبہ ہو تو غور فکر اور تحری کر کے جدھر گمان غالب ہو اسی کو کر لینے سے جواز ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ انسان کی قدرت میں اتنا ہی ہے۔ آیت میں ہے۔ لا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها - ( آیت ۲۸۶ ،سورة البقرة ٢) (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قبلہ مشتبہ ہوا تو تحری کر کے جدھر غالب گمان ہوا اسی طرف نماز پڑھی اور جائز ہوگئی۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن جابر قال كنا مع النبی في مسير او سرية فاصابنا غيم فتحرينا واختلفنا في القبلة فصلى كل رجل منا على حدة فجعل احدنا يخط بين يديه لنعلم امكنتنا فلما اصبحنا نظرناه فاذا نحن قد صلينا على غير القبلة فذكرنا ذلك للنبي الله فقال قد اجزأت صلواتكم - (سن للبیھقی ، باب الاختلاف في القبلة عند التحری ، ج خانی ص ۱۶، نمبر ۲۲۳۵ متر مندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يصلى لغير القبلۃ فی الغیم ص۸۰ نمبر ۳۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تحری کر کے نماز پڑھی تو ہو گئی ۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن عامر بن ربيعة عن أبيه قال : كنا مع النبي الله في سفر في ليلة مظلمة ، فلم ندر أين القبلة فصلى كل رجل منا على حياله ، فلما أصبحنا ذكرنا ذالك للنبي الله فنزل : فأينما تولوا فثم وجه الله آیت ۱۱۵ سورة البقرة ٢) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل یصلی لغير القبلة في الغیم ص ۸۰ نمبر ۳۴۵ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب من يصلى لغير القبلة وصولا یعلم ص ۱۴۳، نمبر ۱۰۲۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تحری کر کے نماز پڑھی تو نماز ہوگئی۔ اصول مشتبہ چیز میں تحری کا حکم ہے، اور جس طرف گمان غالب ہو اسی کو استعمال کر لے۔
Section on Taharrī. (21) If vessels are mixed, most of which are pure, he performs taharrī for wudu and for drinking. Translation: If pure and impure vessels are mixed and most vessels are pure, then for wudu and for drinking he performs taharrī. Explanation: ... etc. Principles: In a doubtful thing, the ruling is of taharrī, and whichever side suspicion/dominant opinion goes, that is used.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on performing ijtihad (taharrī) when pure and impure water vessels are mixed and the majority are pure. The author (Thamaratun Najah) states the matn ruling that one must investigate (taharrī) for both wudu and drinking. The Urdu commentary explains that one should ponder and use the vessel towards which the dominant opinion leans. The proofs (wajh) are then given: first, the Quranic principle of no burden beyond capacity (2:286); second, a hadith about taharrī for the qibla during cloudiness; third, another hadith about taharrī in darkness, supported by Quran 2:115. The principle concludes that in doubtful matters, taharrī is the ruling and one acts upon the dominant opinion. This ruling is specific to when the majority is pure; different ruling applies when majority is impure (next lesson).

Key Terms
تحرى (taharrī): To exert effort and form a dominant opinion by investigation when faced with doubt, and act upon it.
اوان (awān): Vessels, containers for water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling when most water vessels are pure and no distinguishing sign exists?
A) Do tayammum because the water is doubtful.
B) Perform taharrī and use the vessel with the dominant opinion of purity.
C) Use any vessel arbitrarily.
D) Mix all water together and use.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when most vessels are pure and no sign distinguishes them, one must perform taharrī (investigation) and act on the dominant opinion; this is wajib and based on Quranic principle and Prophetic practice.

Taharrī Only for Drinking When Most Vessels Impure
Ruling on taharrī when majority of vessels are impure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing taharrī when most vessels are impure and apply the principle of substituting an alternative.

Core Idea
When a valid substitute exists, taharrī is not needed; only when no substitute exists must one perform taharrī.

In the previous lesson, you learned about taharrī when impure and pure vessels are equal. Here, the majority of vessels are impure. The Hanafi school introduces a critical distinction: if a legal alternative is available, it takes precedence over taharrī. This lesson explores that principle and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the majority of water vessels are impure or not. This lesson assumes the majority are impure.
This is a conditional ruling; the majority status changes the obligation.
2
Check for a valid substitute
For each intended purpose (wudu, drinking, etc.), ask: Is there a legally valid alternative? For wudu, tayammum is a substitute; for drinking, there is no substitute.
Tayammum is a rukhsah (concession) that replaces wudu when water is unavailable or unusable.
3
Apply the ruling
If a substitute exists, use it and do not perform taharrī. If no substitute exists, perform taharrī to find a pure vessel.
The principle: 'If another path exists, go that way; otherwise take the first path.'
4
Note the exception for drinking
Drinking is a necessity with no alternative; therefore, taharrī is permitted and even required to obtain drinkable water.
This shows the Hanafi concern for preserving life and easing difficulty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲) وان كان اكثرها نجسا لا يتحرى الا للشرب. ترجمه : (۲۲) اور اگر اکثر برتن ناپاک ہوں تو صرف پینے کے لئے تحری کرے۔ تشریح : زیادہ تر برتن میں ناپاک پانی ہے اور کم برتن میں پاک پانی ہے تو وضو کے لئے تحری کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، تیم کرلے، کیونکہ یہاں وضو کا نائب تیم موجود ہے لیکن پینے کا پانی نہیں ہے اس لئے مجبوری ہے، اس لئے تحری کر کے جس برتن کے بارے غالب گمان ہو کہ پاک ہو گا اس سے پی لے۔ اصول: دوسرا راستہ موجود ہو تو اس طرف جائے ورنہ پہلا راستہ اختیار کرے۔
(22) And if most of them are impure, he does not perform taharrī except for drinking. If most vessels are impure, then for wudu there is no need for taharrī; perform tayammum, because here tayammum is available as substitute for wudu, but drinking water is a necessity, so for that he performs taharrī and drinks from the vessel with dominant opinion of purity. Principle: If another path exists, go that way; otherwise take the first path.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling when the majority of vessels are impure. In contrast to the previous case, one should not perform taharrī for wudu because tayammum is an alternative substitute. However, for drinking, there is no substitute, so taharrī is allowed. The principle states that if an alternative legal pathway exists (like tayammum), one should take it; only when no alternative exists does one resort to taharrī. This demonstrates Hanafi legal reasoning using istihsan and consideration of alternatives.

Key Terms
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
تحری (taharrī): The process of seeking the purest option among uncertain items by forming a dominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because wudu is less important than drinking.
B) Because tayammum is a valid substitute that removes the need for seeking pure water.
C) Because all vessels are impure anyway.
D) Because the ruling is different for men and women.

Key Takeaway
When a valid alternative exists, use it; only when none exists should one resort to taharrī.

Taharrī for Mixed Clothes: No Substitute for Covering the Body
Ruling on taharrī for mixed clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for mixed pure and impure clothes and explain why taharrī is required regardless of whether the majority is pure or impure.

Core Idea
When pure and impure clothes are mixed, taharrī is always required because covering the body has no substitute.

In the previous lesson, we saw that for mixed water vessels, if the majority is impure, tayammum is performed instead of taharrī. Here, the ruling for clothes is different: taharrī is done in all cases, whether the majority is pure or impure. The reason is that covering the nakedness (satr) is obligatory and has no alternative like tayammum. Therefore, one must exert effort to identify a pure garment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Recognize that the ruling applies when pure and impure clothes are mixed and no pure clothes are available.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that one must perform taharrī—i.e., ascertain to the best of one's ability which garment is likely pure—and then wear it for prayer.
This applies whether the majority of clothes are pure or impure.
3
Understand the reason
The reason given is that covering the nakedness (satr) has no substitute. Unlike water, where tayammum can replace wudu, there is no alternative to covering the body in prayer.
4
Contrast with water vessels
Recall that for mixed water vessels, if the majority is impure, one does not perform taharrī but instead uses tayammum. This contrast highlights the unique necessity of clothing for prayer.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a person with a mixed set of clothes should carefully examine and choose the garment he most strongly suspects is pure. He then prays with that garment. The prayer is valid even if it later turns out the garment was impure, because he acted on his best effort (taharrī).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۳) وفى الثياب المختلطة يتحرى سواء كان اكثرها طاهرا او نجسا. ترجمه : (۲۳) اور ملے ہوئے کپڑے میں تحری کرے، چاہےاکثر کپڑا پاک ہو یا نا پاک ہو۔ تشریح : پاک اور ناپاک کپڑے ملے ہوئے ہیں، اور کوئی پاک کپڑا موجود نہیں ہے، تو چاہے زیادہ کپڑا پاک ہو یا کم دونوں صورتوں میں تحری کر کے جس کپڑے کے بارے میں غالب گمان ہو کہ پاک ہوگا اسی کو پہن کر نماز پڑھ لے۔ وجه (۱) چونکہ ستر ڈھانکنے کا کوئی بدل نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر حال میں تحری کرے۔
(23) And regarding mixed clothes, he performs taharrī, whether most of them are pure or impure. For mixed clothes, taharrī is performed, whether most clothes are pure or impure. Explanation: Pure and impure clothes are mixed, and no pure clothes are available; so in either case, he performs taharrī and wears the one he strongly suspects is pure, then prays. Reason: Because covering the nakedness has no substitute, so taharrī is done in all cases.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for taharrī regarding mixed clothes. Unlike the case of water vessels where the majority matters and tayammum is an alternative, for clothes there is no substitute for covering the nakedness (satr). Therefore, taharrī is required regardless of whether the majority of clothes are pure or impure. The reasoning is that necessity (covering the body for prayer) has no alternative, so one must make an effort to find a pure garment.

Key Terms
ثياب (thiyāb): Clothes, garments used for covering the body during prayer.
تحرّى (taharrā): To exert utmost effort to ascertain the ruling or the pure status; to make a considered judgment based on signs and likelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because clothes are less important than water.
B) Because there is no substitute for covering the body.
C) Because impurity in clothes does not invalidate prayer.
D) Because most clothes are assumed pure.

Key Takeaway
Taharrī for mixed clothes is always required because covering the body has no alternative; unlike water, tayammum cannot substitute for clothing.

Small Well: The Ruling on Impurity and the Exception for Animal Dung
Ruling on drawing water from a small well when impurity falls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a small well when impurity falls, identify the exception for animal dung, and explain the principle of facilitation.

Core Idea
A small well becomes impure by any impurity except animal dung, due to the principle of facilitation.

The category of wells in Hanafi fiqh has special rulings based on the size of the well and the nature of the impurity. In this passage, we learn the key rule for small wells: any impurity, even a tiny drop, renders the entire well impure, requiring all water to be drawn. However, there is a critical exception for animal dung, which is exempted to avoid hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the well type
Confirm that the well is 'small' (less than ten cubits deep). This is the condition for the ruling.
The depth measure is from the commentary.
2
State the general rule
Any impurity (e.g., a drop of blood or wine) that falls into the well makes the water impure. The entire well must be drawn.
The text says 'whole water must be drawn' (tunzah).
3
Note the exception
Animal dung (arwath) is explicitly excluded. If only dung falls, the well remains pure.
This is a facilitation (tashil).
4
Understand the basis
The ruling is not based on strict analogy (qiyas) but on facilitation. Since dung falls frequently, requiring full drawing each time would cause hardship.
This principle is stated in the commentary.
5
Apply the ruling
If full drawing is impossible, the commentary adds that drawing 200 buckets suffices. Other categories (40, 20, or none) exist but are not detailed here.
The commentary mentions four categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۴) تُنزح البئر الصغيرة بوقوع نجاسة وان قلت من غير الارواث كقطرة دم او خمر. ترجمه : (۲۴) چھوٹے کنویں میں جودہ دردہ سے کم ہو گو بر کے علاوہ اگر تھوڑی بھی نجاست گرے تو پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا۔ سوائے گوبر کے، جیسے خون کا قطرہ ، یا شراب کا قطرہ گر جائے تو ناپاک ہو جائے گا ] تشریح : یہاں کنواں میں ناپاکی گر جائے تو اس کے لئے چار قسم کی چیزیں ہیں، اور چار قسم کے احکام ہیں [1] کنویں کا پورا پانی نکالا جائے ، اور وہ ممکن نہ ہوتو اس کے بدلے میں دوسوڈول نکالے جائیں [۲] چالیس ڈول نکالے جائیں ۔ [۳] میں ڈول نکالے جائیں ۔ [۴] اور ایسی بھی شکل ہے کہ کچھ نہ نکالنا پڑے، کنواں پاک ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ: کنواں وہ دردہ سے کم ہو اس میں ناپا کی گر جائے تو کنواں ناپاک ہو جائے گا، اور پورے کنواں کا پانی نکالنا پڑے گا ،اور پورے کنویں کا پانی نکالنا ممکن نہ ہو تو دوسوڈول نکال دے، تو کنواں پاک ہو جائے گا، البتہ تھوڑا گو بر گر جائے تو کنوان ناپاک نہیں ہو گا، اس کی وجہ آگے آرہی ہے۔ اصول : کنویں کے مسائل قیاس پر نہیں ہیں، بلکہ تسہیل پر ہیں، مثلا و بر ناپاک ہے اس لئے تھوڑے سے گرنے سے بھی پورا کنواں نکالنا چاہئے لیکن چونکہ یہ بار بار گرتا ہے اور بار بار پورا کنواں نکالنے میں پریشانی ہے ، اس لئے حکم یہ ہوا کہ اس سے کنواں نکالنا بارگرتاہے اور بار
(24) For a small well, if an impurity falls, even a little, excluding droppings, like a drop of blood or wine, the entire well is drawn. Explanation: For a well less than ten cubits, if impurity falls, it becomes impure and all water must be drawn. If that is not possible, then 200 buckets must be drawn. There are four categories: ... Principle: Well rulings are not based on qiyas but on facilitation. For example, dung is impure, so even a small amount should require drawing all water, but because it falls repeatedly and drawing all water repeatedly is difficult, the ruling is that it does not require drawing.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage begins the section on wells (masā'il al-bi'r). The ruling states that a small well (less than ten cubits deep) becomes impure by the fall of any impurity, even a small amount, except for animal dung (arwāth). If impurity falls, the entire well water must be drawn out; if that is impossible, then 200 buckets must be drawn. The commentary lists four categories of well rulings (full drawing, 40 buckets, 20 buckets, or nothing). The principle is that well rulings are based on facilitation (tashīl), not strict analogy (qiyās), because of repeated occurrence of certain impurities like dung. This explains why dung is exempted – to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
بئر صغيرة (bi'r saghīrah): A well less than ten cubits deep (according to the commentary).
ارواث (arwāth): Animal droppings/dung (plural of rawith)
تنزح (tunzah): The water is drawn out (from the well)
تسہیل (tashil): Facilitation; the principle that rulings are made easy due to practical necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Animal dung (arwāth)
C) Urine
D) A dead insect

Key Takeaway
In small wells, all impurities require full drawing except animal dung, which is exempted based on the principle of facilitation (tashil).

Mixed Vessels: Tahrri Only for Drinking, Tayammum for Wudu
Ruling statement on mixed vessels: tahrri only for drinking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mixed vessels when most are impure, distinguishing between the obligation of tahrri for drinking and tayammum for wudu.

Core Idea
When most vessels are impure, do not search (tahrri) for wudu — perform tayammum instead; only search for drinking water.

When a believer faces a situation where most available vessels contain impure water, a key question arises: should one search (tahrri) for a pure vessel for both wudu and drinking, or is there a substitution? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position based on necessity and the availability of alternatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
You need both a valid wudu and drinkable water, but most vessels are impure and you cannot easily identify which are pure.
2
Check for substitutes
For wudu, tayammum exists as a substitute when water is not available. For drinking, no substitute exists; you must find water to drink.
Tayammum is a valid replacement for wudu under certain conditions.
3
Apply the rule
Since tayammum substitutes for wudu, you do not need to search for pure water for wudu. But for drinking, you must search (tahrri) because you cannot live without water.
4
Conclude
Perform tayammum for wudu; make tahrri to find a likely pure vessel for drinking.
Tahrri means exerting best judgment based on signs.

Ruling on Mixed Clothes: Tahrri Always Required
Ruling statement on tahrri for mixed clothes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tahrri when pure and impure clothes are mixed and apply it to determine the validity of salat.

Core Idea
When pure and impure clothes are mixed, tahrri is always wajib because covering the 'awrah has no substitute.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: you have a pile of clothes, some pure, some impure, and you cannot identify any pure garment. The Hanafi ruling is clear: you must make tahrri (exert your judgment) to find the most likely pure garment, regardless of whether the majority is pure or impure. The reason is that covering the 'awrah is obligatory and has no alternative. Let's examine the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognise the situation: mixed pure and impure clothes, and no pure garment is identifiable.
This is the precondition for tahrri.
2
State the ruling
The matn says: 'yataharra' (he makes tahrri) in all cases, regardless of majority.
Tahrri is wajib, not optional.
3
Understand the reason
Covering the 'awrah in salat is obligatory and has no substitute, so tahrri must be done to ensure the garment is pure.
If tahrri is omitted, the salat may be invalid if the garment is impure.
4
Apply the ruling
Use judgment to choose the most likely pure garment, then pray in it. The salat is valid even if later the garment is found impure, because tahrri was performed.
The obligation is to make tahrri, not to achieve certainty.

Source Text

Ruling on Small Well: Impurity (Other Than Dung)
States that a small well must be emptied if any impurity except dung falls in.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when impurity except dung falls into a small well, cite the proofs from Sahaba, and explain the exception for dung based on facilitation.

Core Idea
Any impurity except dung renders a small well impure; emptying the entire well is wajib.

This lesson examines the ruling for a small well when impurity falls into it, excluding dung. You will learn that the entire well must be emptied, based on athar from Ibn Abbas and Ali (RA). The exception for dung is due to frequent occurrence and the principle of facilitation (tashil) in well rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the fall of impurity (except dung) into a small well. The ruling is that the entire well must be emptied (nazh).
'Small well' is defined as less than 10 cubits deep.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites athar from Ibn Abbas (Zamzam well) and Ali (mouse, child's urine). These are sayings of Companions, which are a type of Sunnah. They explicitly command emptying the well.
The athar are transmitted via chains that are zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'nazih' (emptying) indicates that the water is impure and must be removed. By analogy (qiyas), the same applies to drops of blood or wine.
The analogical extension is based on the common element of impurity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may have different amounts for well purification, but the Hanafi position requires full emptying for small wells.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different methodologies.
5
Evaluate the exception for dung
Dung is excepted because it frequently falls into wells, and strict application would cause hardship. The principle of tashil (facilitation) overrides qiyas here.
This is an application of istihsan.

Chapter on Issues of the Well (24) The water of a small well is drawn out due to the fall of impurity, even if little, excluding dung, like a drop of blood or wine. Lexicon: ... Translation: (24) For a small well which is less than ten [cubits], if any impurity except dung falls, even a little, the entire well is emptied. Except dung, for example, if a drop of blood or wine falls, it becomes impure. Explanation: When impurity falls into a well, there are four categories and four rulings: [1] The entire water of the well is drawn out; if that is not possible, then 200 buckets are drawn. [2] 40 buckets are drawn. [3] 20 buckets are drawn. [4] Sometimes nothing needs to be drawn; the well remains pure. Detailed explanation: A well that is less than 10 [cubits], if impurity falls into it, the well becomes impure, and all the water must be drawn out. If drawing all water is not possible, then draw 200 buckets, and the well becomes pure. However, if a little dung falls, the well does not become impure. The reason comes later. Principle: The rulings of the well are not based on qiyas but on facilitation. For example, dung is impure, so from a little falling, the entire well should be drawn, but because it falls repeatedly and repeatedly drawing the entire well is hardship, the ruling is that from dung the well remains pure unless a large amount falls. Similarly, an impure hand, impure rope, and the impure wall of the well should not become pure without washing with pure water, but due to necessity, after the well becomes pure, all these are considered pure automatically. Proof (1): The basis for the entire well becoming impure is the saying of a Companion: From Muhammad ibn Sirin that a Zanjī fell into Zamzam meaning and died, so Ibn Abbas ordered him to be taken out and ordered the well to be emptied. He said: Then a spring from the corner overcame them, so he ordered it to be plugged with garments until they emptied it. When they emptied it, it burst forth upon them. (Daraqutni, etc.) From this athar, it is understood that from the death of a human, the entire well becomes impure. Similarly, from the fall of impurity, the entire well becomes impure. (2) From Ali regarding a mouse falling into a well: he said, 'Draw water until the water overcomes them.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) This Companion's saying indicates that if a mouse swells and bursts, the entire well must be emptied. (3) A drop of blood or wine falling: the proof is the athar: That Ali was asked about a child who urinated in a well: he said, 'Draw water.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) This athar indicates that if a child urinates in a well, the entire well must be emptied. By analogy, if a drop of blood or wine falls, the entire well must be emptied.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the purification of a small well. The matn defines a small well (less than 10 cubits) and states that if any impurity except dung falls in, the well becomes impure and must be emptied. The commentary elaborates four categories of rulings: 1) emptying the entire well (or 200 buckets if not possible), 2) 40 buckets, 3) 20 buckets, 4) nothing. For this specific case (impurity other than dung), the ruling is category 1. The principle stated is that well rulings are based on facilitation (tashil), not strict analogy. For example, dung is impure but its frequent falling would cause hardship, so it is excepted. The proofs provided are athar of Ibn Abbas regarding Zamzam well, Ali regarding a mouse, and Ali regarding a child's urine. These establish that death or impurity in a well requires emptying all water, and by qiyas, the same applies to drops of blood or wine.

Key Terms
بئر صغيرة (bi'r saghīrah): A well whose depth is less than 10 cubits (about 5 meters).
تنزح (tunzah): The water is drawn out/emptied from the well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The well remains pure
B) The entire well must be emptied
C) Only 40 buckets must be drawn
D) Tayammum is sufficient

Key Takeaway
A small well becomes impure from any impurity except dung; emptying the entire well is wajib.

Ruling on Death of Dog, Sheep, or Human in a Well
States the ruling and conditions for purifying a well after an animal dies in it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling where a well must be fully emptied due to the death of a large animal or a putrefied small animal, and identify the exceptional condition for small animals.

Core Idea
A large animal's death or a small animal's putrefaction contaminates the entire well.

This lesson addresses a common scenario of taharah (purification) concerning wells. When a large animal like a dog, sheep, or human dies in a well, the water is considered impure throughout—even if the body is intact. For small animals, only putrefaction triggers the same ruling. Understanding these precise conditions prevents excessive or insufficient purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is emptying the well (nazh). The ruling is wajib (obligatory). The text states: 'the entire well will be emptied.'
This is a pure ruling statement from the matn.
2
Distinguish the animal categories
Large animals (dog, sheep, human) always require full emptying. Small animals require full emptying only if they swelled and burst due to prolonged decay.
The commentary explicitly makes this distinction.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
For large animals, impurity reaches the bottom regardless of swelling. For small animals, swelling indicates impurity spread throughout.
The reason is based on extent of contamination.
4
Note the alternative ruling
If total emptying is impractical, the alternative is to extract 200 buckets. This is a concession (rukhsah).
The number 200 is specified in the text.
5
Trace the proof
The proof is the athar of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) which states that a well is emptied when an animal dies in it. This is cited in earlier sections of the source.
This hadith is a reliable precedent in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ۲۶ ) وبموت كلب او شاة او آدمى فيها. ترجمه : (۲۶) اور پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا کتے کے مرنے سے، یا آدمی کے مرنے سے، یا حیوان کے پھول پھٹ جانے سے چاہے چھوٹا کیوں نہ ہو۔ اور دوسو ڈول اگر اس کا نکالنا ممکن نہ ہو۔ تشریح : اگر جانور بڑا ہو، جیسے کتا، یا بکری، یا آدمی ، اور وہ گر کر مر گیا ہو تو چاہے پھولا پھٹ نہ ہو پھر بھی پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا، کیونکہ جانور بڑا ہے اس لئے نیچے تک اس کی نجاست پہنچ چکی ہوگی ، اس لئے پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا۔ یا جانور چھوٹا ہو لیکن پھول پھٹ گیا ہو تو مردہ دیر تک رہنے کی وجہ سے نیچے تک نجاست پھیل چکی ہوگی اس لئے پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا۔ اور اندر چشمہ کی وجہ سے
(26) And by the death of a dog, or a sheep, or a human in it. Translation: (26) And the entire well will be emptied due to the death of a dog, or a human, or an animal that has swollen and burst, even if it is small. And 200 buckets if it is not possible to empty all. Explanation: If the animal is large, like a dog, or a goat, or a human, and it fell and died, even if it did not swell, still the entire well is emptied, because the animal is large, so its impurity has reached the bottom. Therefore, the entire well is emptied. Or if the animal is small but it has swollen, then due to remaining dead for a long time, the impurity has spread to the bottom, so the entire well is emptied. And due to a spring inside...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof for the death of a large animal or human in a well. The matn states that if a dog, sheep, or human dies in the well, the entire well must be emptied. The commentary adds that if a small animal dies and swells (putrifies), the same applies. The reason: the impurity spreads throughout the water. The text mentions 200 buckets as an alternative if total emptying is impossible. The proof is implied from the athar of Ibn Abbas previously cited.

Key Terms
بئر (bi'r): A well, a source of water.
نزح (nazh): Drawing water from the well to purify it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Empty 200 buckets of water
C) Empty the entire well
D) No action needed if the water is clear

Key Takeaway
A large animal's death (or a small animal's putrefaction) obligates full emptying of the well to achieve taharah.

Ruling on a Pig Falling into a Well
Ruling and proof that a pig renders the entire well impure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pig falls into a well and explain why the entire well becomes impure based on the principle of najis al-ayn.

Core Idea
A pig's inherent impurity contaminates the entire well immediately, even without direct contact.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi rule regarding wells and impurity. The source text addresses a seemingly edge case: a pig falling into a well but coming out alive without touching the water. Why does the entire well still become impure? The answer lies in the concept of najis al-ayn (inherent impurity). Understanding this principle clarifies many rulings in taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
When a pig falls into a well, the entire well becomes impure; all water must be removed.
2
Identify the key concept
The pig is najis al-ayn (inherently impure), not merely contaminated. Its impurity is intrinsic to its substance.
3
Apply the principle of najis al-ayn
Because the pig's entire body is impure, any contact with water — even without visible mixing — renders the water impure. Water is a subtle substance; impurity spreads instantly.
4
Check for conditions
The ruling applies regardless of whether the pig dies, touches the water, or leaves the well alive. The mere fact that it fell into the well establishes impurity.
5
Determine the necessary action
All water must be removed (nazh al-bir). Only after the well is completely emptied and cleaned does it become pure again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مسائل البئر (۲۵) وبوقوع خنزير ولو خرج حيا ولم يصب فمه الماء ترجمه : (۲۵) سور کے گرنے سے پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا اگر چہ زندہ نکل آیا ہو اور پانی اس کے منہ تک نہ پہنچا ہو۔ تشریح : سورنجس العین ہے اس کا ظاہری جسم بھی ناپاک ہے اس لئے چاہے اس کے منہ میں پانی نہ گیا اور وہ کنواں میں نہ مرا ہو تب بھی پورا کنواں ناپاک ہو جائے گا ، اور پورے کنویں کا پانی نکالنا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ نجس العین کے گرتے ہی پانی ناپاک ہو گیا۔
Chapter on Well Issues. (25) And by the falling of a pig, even if it comes out alive and its mouth did not touch the water. Translation: (25) With the falling of a pig, the entire well must be emptied, even if it came out alive and water did not reach its mouth. Explanation: The pig is inherently impure (najis al-ayn); its apparent body is also impure. Therefore, even if water did not enter its mouth and it did not die in the well, the entire well becomes impure and all water must be removed, because as soon as something inherently impure falls, the water becomes impure.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its proof. It states that if a pig falls into a well, the entire well becomes impure and all water must be removed, regardless of whether the pig touched the water or died. The proof is that the pig is najis al-ayn (inherently impure), so its mere presence contaminates the water. This is based on the Hanafi principle that najasat al-ayn items cause impurity by contact without any need for dissolution.

Key Terms
خنزير (khinzir): A pig; considered najis al-ayn (inherently impure).
نجس العين (najis al-'ayn): Something that is intrinsically impure, such as pig, dog, blood, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only twenty buckets need to be removed.
D) The well is pure if the pig did not die.

Key Takeaway
The pig is najis al-ayn; its mere presence in a well renders all water impure, requiring complete removal of water for purification.

Ruling on Well Purification when a Large Animal Dies or a Small Animal Bloats
Ruling and proofs for emptying well upon death of large animals or bloating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of full nazh upon the death of a large animal or bloating of a small animal, and apply the 200-bucket substitute when full nazh is impossible.

Core Idea
Death of a large animal or bloating of any animal in a well requires emptying all water.

When an animal dies in a well, the water becomes impure. The Hanafi school specifies that if the animal is large (like a dog, goat, or human) or if a small animal bloats, the entire well must be emptied. If complete emptying is impossible due to a spring, 200 buckets suffice. This lesson examines the ruling and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is nazh (emptying the well). What is the hukm level? The text states it is wajib when a large animal dies or a small animal bloats.
Note that for small animals that die without bloating, the ruling is different (not covered in this passage).
2
Determine when full nazh is required
Full nazh is wajib for: (a) death of a large animal (dog, sheep, human) regardless of bloating, and (b) death of any animal that bloats. The impurity is assumed to reach the bottom.
Bloating indicates decomposition and spread of impurity.
3
Understand the substitute when full nazh is impossible
If the well has a strong spring making complete emptying impossible, then 200 buckets must be removed.
This is a concession (rukhsah) based on the narration from Ata.
4
Analyze the proofs (dalil)
Three proofs are cited: (1) The action of Ibn Abbas when a man died in Zamzam well, (2) The statement of Ali regarding a mouse that bloated, (3) Qiyas from the hadith of a child urinating in a well to cases of blood or wine drops.
The first two are direct evidence for full nazh; the third is analogical.
5
Note the madhhab dispute and the relied-upon position
Some other schools require different amounts (e.g., 120 buckets). The Hanafi school adopted 200 as a precautionary maximum, and this is the mufta bihi.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Hanafis insist on 200, others may settle for 120.

Source Text

(مصنف ابن ابي شیبۃ ۱۹۸ فى الفارة والدجاجة اشباههما تقع في البئر ، ج اول ،ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۷۱ ارمصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب البئر تقع فيه الدابة ، ج اول ص ۶۴ نمبر ۲۷۳) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ چوہا پھول پھٹ جائے تو پورا کنواں نکالنا پڑے گا۔ (۳) خون کا قطرہ، یا شراب کا قطرہ گر جائے تو پورا کنواں نکالنا پڑے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ ان علیا سئل عن صبی بال في البئر قال : ينزح ۔ (مصنف ابن بي شيبة ، ۱۹۸ فى الفارة والدجاجة واشباههما تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۱۷۲۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بچہ اگر کنویں میں پیشاب کر دے تو پورا کنواں نکالنا ہوگا، اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے خون یا شراب کا قطرہ گر جائے تو پورا کنواں نکالنا ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۲۶) اور پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا کتے کے مرنے سے، یا آدمی کے مرنے سے، یا حیوان کے پھول پھٹ جانے سے چاہے چھوٹا کیوں نہ ہو۔ اور دوسو ڈول اگر اس کا نکالنا ممکن نہ ہو۔ تشریح : اگر جانور بڑا ہو، جیسے کتا، یا بکری، یا آدمی ، اور وہ گر کر مر گیا ہو تو چاہے پھولا پھٹ نہ ہو پھر بھی پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا، کیونکہ جانور بڑا ہے اس لئے نیچے تک اس کی نجاست پہنچ چکی ہوگی ، اس لئے پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا۔ یا جانور چھوٹا ہو لیکن پھول پھٹ گیا ہو تو مردہ دیر تک رہنے کی وجہ سے نیچے تک نجاست پھیل چکی ہوگی اس لئے پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا۔ اور اندر چشمہ کی وجہ سے پورا کنواں نکالنا ناممکن ہو تو دوسوڈول نکال دینے سے کنواں پاک ہو جائے گا۔
(26) And by the death of a dog, or a goat, or a human in it... This passage presents rulings and proofs for when a large animal dies or a small animal bloats in a well. The main ruling: the entire well must be emptied. If complete emptying is impossible, at least 200 buckets must be removed. The proofs include the action of Ibn Abbas regarding a man who died in Zamzam, and the statement of Ali concerning a mouse that bloats. These are used to establish that death of a large animal or bloating of any animal requires complete nazh. The Hanafi school adopts the figure of 200 buckets based on precaution and the practice of Imam Muhammad.

Medium-Sized Animals in a Well: 40 Buckets Rule
Ruling for medium animals in well purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a medium-sized animal that dies in a well and apply the exception for bloating.

Core Idea
A medium animal in a well requires 40 buckets unless bloated – then the whole well.

Purity of well water is critical for daily worship. The Hanafi school classifies animals by size to determine how much water must be removed when one dies in a well. This lesson focuses on the middle category – animals like chickens and cats – and the rule that 40 buckets suffice, with an important exception for bloating.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a medium-sized animal (chicken or cat) dying in a well. The ruling is that removing 40 buckets of water is wajib (obligatory) to purify the well.
2
Understand the size classification
Hanafis divide animals into large (e.g., goat, dog), medium (chicken, cat), and small (mouse). Medium is defined as larger than a mouse but smaller than a goat.
This classification is specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the bloating exception
If the animal has bloated (become swollen), the rule changes: the entire well must be emptied, not just 40 buckets.
Bloating indicates greater impurity spread.
4
Trace the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy). Narrations specify amounts for large (full well) and small (20 buckets) animals. The medium animal is analogized to require an intermediate amount: 40 buckets.
No direct text exists for medium animals; it is derived by analogy.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih – other schools have different amounts, but the Hanafi position is settled at 40 buckets for medium and full for bloated.
The mufta bihi (operative) is 40 buckets without bloating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۷) اور اگر کنواں میں مرغی مرگئی، پابلی ، یا اس جیسا جانور تو چالیس ڈول نکالنا لا زم ہو گا۔ تشریح : مرغی یا بلی ، یا اس جیسا جانور بکری کی طرح بڑی بھی نہیں ہے اور چوہے کی طرح چھوٹی بھی نہیں ہے، بلکہ اوسط ہے اس لئے اس کے مرنے سے چالیس ڈول نکالنے سے کنواں پاک ہو جائے گا۔ بشرطیکہ پھولا پھٹا نہ ہو، کیونکہ پھول پھٹ گیا ہو تو پورا کنواں نکالنا ہوگا۔
Translation: (27) And if a chicken or a cat or similar animal dies in it, then 40 buckets must be removed. Explanation: A chicken or a cat or similar animal is not as large as a goat nor as small as a mouse, but intermediate. Therefore, if it dies, removing 40 buckets purifies the well, provided it has not bloated, because if it bloats, the entire well must be emptied.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for medium-sized animals such as chickens and cats. The Hanafi school specifies that 40 buckets of water must be removed from the well if such an animal dies and does not bloat. If the animal bloats, the entire well must be emptied. This is based on the classification of animals: large (e.g., dog, goat, human) require full nazh; medium (chicken, cat) require 40 buckets; small (mouse) require 20 buckets unless bloated. The proof is analogy to narrations and the principle that impurity spreads proportionally.

Key Terms
دجاجة (dajajah): Chicken; classified as a medium-sized animal for well purification.
هرة (hirrah): Cat; also medium-sized.

Ruling on Swelling Animal and 200 Buckets
Ruling with proof: full well removal for swelling animals, with 200-bucket concession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for well purification when an animal dies and swells, and apply the 200-bucket concession when full removal is impractical.

Core Idea
When an animal swells in a well, full removal is required; if impossible, 200 buckets suffice as a cautionary substitute.

If an animal dies in a well and its body swells, the water becomes completely impure according to the Hanafi school. The primary obligation is to empty the entire well. However, recognizing practical difficulty, the school provides a concession: drawing 200 buckets suffices when full removal is impossible. This lesson examines the textual proofs and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Determine what event causes the well to become impure: an animal dies and its body swells (intifākh). Note that for large animals, death alone may suffice, but the passage emphasizes swelling for all animals.
The ruling applies to both large and small animals if swelling occurs.
2
State the primary ruling
The primary obligation is to remove all water from the well (nazh al-kull). This is wajib based on caution and the actions of the Companions.
3
Recognize the concession
If emptying the entire well is not possible, the school allows drawing 200 buckets as a substitute. This is based on the practice of Imam Muhammad and a cautious interpretation of the narration from 'Ata.
The 200-bucket rule is not the default but an alternative when full removal is impractical.
4
Analyze the proofs
The passage provides multiple proofs: (1) The statement of 'Ata about a dog, implying full removal upon decomposition; (2) The incident of Zamzam with a human death; (3) The statement of 'Ali about a mouse, extending the ruling to small animals. The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to derive the 200-bucket figure.
The proofs are from the sayings of a Tabi'i and Companions, which have zanni thubut and dalala.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Test your understanding: a cow dies and swells in a well that cannot be fully emptied. How many buckets are needed? Apply the 200-bucket rule. Conversely, if the animal does not swell, a different ruling applies (lesser quantities from other texts).
The key distinction is whether swelling (tafakkukh) has occurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبانـتـفـاخ حـيـوان ولـو صـغـيـرا ومائتا دلو لو لم يمكن نزحها. وجه : (۱) یہ جانور بڑے ہوتے ہیں اس کے مرتے ہی پورے کنویں میں نجاست پھیل جائے گی اس لئے پورے کنویں کا پانی نکالا جائے گا (۲) عن عطاء قال اذا سقط الكلب فى البئر فاخرج منها حين سقط نزح منها عشرون دلوا فان اخرج حين مات نزح منها ستون دلوااو سبعون دلوا فان تفسخ فيها نزح منهاماء ها فان لم تستطيعوا نزح مائة دلو و عشرون و مائة (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب البئر تقع فيه الدابة ، ج اول ص ۶۴ نمبر ۲۷۴ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۹۸۷ في الفارة تقع في البئر ۱۴۹ نمبر ۱۷۱۴) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ کتا گر جائے تو پورا کنواں نکالا جائے ، اور وہ ممکن نہ ہو تو ایک سو بیس ڈول نکالے جائیں، اور اس قول تابعی, نزح مائة دلو و عشرون و مائة ، کا ایک مطلب یہ بھی ہے کہ دوسو بیس ڈول نکالے جائیں ۔ حنفیہ نے اس پر احتیاط کرتے ہوئے دو سو ڈول نکالنے کا حکم فرمایا ہے ۔ (۳) امام محمد کے زمانے میں انکے دیار کے کنواں میں عموما دوسو ڈول سے تین سو ڈول پانی ہوا کرتا تھا اس لئے انہوں نے فرمایا کہ دوسوڈول نکال دئے جائیں تو یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ پورے کنواں کا پانی نکال دیا ، اور کنواں پاک ہو گیا ۔ (۴) اور انسان کے مرنے سے پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عـن مـحـمـد بن سيرين أن زنجيا وقع في زمزم یعنی فمات فأمر به ابن عباس فأخرج و أمر بها أن ننزح ، قال : فغلبهم عين جائتهم من الركن ،فأمر بها فدسمت بالقباطي و المطارف حتى نزحوها ، فلما نزحوها انفجرت عليهم (دارقطنی ، باب البئر از اوقع فیها حیوان ، ج اول ص ۲۷ نمبر ۶۲ رستن بینی باب ما جاء فی نزح زمزم، ج اول ، ص ۴۰۱ ، نمبر ۱۲۶۲/ مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب البئر تقع فیه الدابة ، ج اول ص ۶۴ نمبر ۲۷۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ انسان کے مرنے سے پورا کنواں ناپاک ہو جائے گا۔ (۵) اور چھوٹا جانور مر کر پھول پھٹ جائے تو پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا، اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی دلیل ہے۔ عـن عـلـى فـي الفارة تقع في البئر قال : ينزح الى ان يغلبهم الماء . (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة، باب في الفارة تقع في البئر ، ج اول ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۱۷۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ چھوٹا جانور مثلا چوہا بھی پھول پھٹ گیا ہو تو پورا کنواں نکالا جائے گا۔
And due to swelling of an animal, even if small, [the well is ruled impure,] and two hundred buckets [must be removed] if its complete removal is not possible. Explanation: (1) These animals are large; upon their death, impurity spreads throughout the well, so all water must be removed. (2) From 'Ata: he said, 'If a dog falls into a well and is removed when it fell, twenty buckets are drawn; if removed when dead, sixty or seventy buckets; if it decomposed, all water is drawn; and if you cannot, draw one hundred and twenty buckets.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, etc.) This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that if a dog falls, the entire well should be emptied, and if not possible, 120 buckets. But the Hanafis, out of caution, ruled for 200 buckets. (3) In Imam Muhammad's time, wells in his region usually contained 200-300 buckets of water, so he said that drawing 200 buckets counts as removing all water, and the well becomes pure. (4) For a human dying, the entire well must be drawn, as proven by the saying of a Companion: from Muhammad ibn Sirin: a black man fell into Zamzam and died; Ibn Abbas ordered the water to be drawn... (Dalqutni, etc.) This shows that a human's death makes the entire well impure. (5) And if a small animal dies and swells, the entire well must be drawn, as proven by the saying of a Companion: from 'Ali about a mouse falling into a well: he said, 'Draw until the water overcomes them.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, etc.) This indicates that even a small animal like a mouse, if it swells, requires full removal.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the section on wells. The Hanafi school holds that if an animal dies and its body swells (whether large or small), the entire well becomes impure and must be emptied. However, if emptying all water is not feasible, 200 buckets suffice as a practical concession. This is a mufta bihi position based on caution and the practice of Imam Muhammad. The passage provides multiple evidences: (1) Rational reasoning that large animals spread impurity upon death. (2) The statement of 'Ata about a dog, which implies full removal for decomposition, and the Hanafis interpret this as requiring 200 buckets when full removal is impossible. (3) The customary practice of Imam Muhammad's time. (4) The incident of Zamzam with a human death, showing that human death requires full removal. (5) The instruction of 'Ali regarding a mouse that swells, extending the rule to small animals. The key principle is that swelling (tafakkukh) indicates total contamination, necessitating full removal. The 200-bucket rule is a substitute when full removal is impractical, not the general rule for all animals.

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): The act of removing water from a well, specifically to purify it from impurities.
انتفاخ (intifākh): Swelling of a dead animal's body due to decomposition, which triggers the ruling of full well removal.
بئر (bi'r): A well, the source of water in question for purification rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a dog dies and its body swells in a well, and the well cannot be completely emptied?
A) 60-70 buckets
B) 120 buckets
C) 200 buckets
D) Entire well must be emptied regardless

Key Takeaway
Swelling of an animal in a well triggers full removal; if impossible, 200 buckets suffice as a cautionary measure.
